Report on the results of parallel checks on value added tax administration between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic carried out in 2005
Introductory word
The present material informs about the progress and results of parallel checks carried out by the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Najvy higher control office of the Slovak Republic, which focused on the area of value added tax administration and the use of the Value Added Tax Information Exchange System (VIES).
In May 2004, the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic joined the European Union, so the revenue from value added tax affects not only the state budgets of both countries, but also the budget of the European Union as a whole.
Parallel control actions were aimed in particular at checking the procedure of tax authorities in examining the amount of value added tax paid in commercial transactions carried out between member states of the European Union.
The introduction of the VIES system has enabled the electronic exchange of information on the registration of value added tax payers in each Member State of the European Union and on commercial transactions made by such payers.
The discrepancy between the data in the VIES system and the data in the value added tax return filed by the payer should alert the tax administrator to suspicious cases and allow the detection of tax evasion or fraud.
The benefit of the parallel checks carried out consisted not only in the exchange of information on the procedure of financial or tax authorities in the administration of value added tax, but in particular in the examination of the use of VIES in the control of the application of the right to value added tax exemption in intra-Community transactions.
The lessons learned from the implementation of parallel controls are beneficial for the development of mutual cooperation and will be used in the implementation of further parallel controls in cooperation with the control institutions of the Member States of the European Union.
Report on the results of parallel checks on value added tax administration for the period from 1 January 2007 to 31 December 2006 5. 2004 to 30. 6. 2005
Introduction
Inspection number: (CZ) 05/19 (SK) 22/2005
Subject of control: (GB) Value added tax administration, (SK) Control of the procedure of tax authorities in the administration, control and enforcement of value added tax and the fulfilment of tasks within the VIES system for the exchange of information between EU Member States
The Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the SAO, the Czech Republic) and the Najvyšší control office of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as the "SAO SR") concluded on 12 December 2004 that the Slovak Republic's audit office, the Czech Republic, was established in Slovakia. 9. 2005 Cooperation Agreement in control activities.
The subject of the contract was cooperation in the parallel control actions carried out "Value Added Tax Administration", included in the plan of control activities of the SAO, Cr for 2005 under No. 05/19 and "Control of the procedure of tax authorities in the management, control and enforcement of dane from the added value and the fulfilment of the tasks under the VIES system for the exchange of information medácií medzi by the member landscapes of the ECA", included in the plan of control activities of the SAO SR under No. 22/2005.
The control actions carried out in parallel were coordinated checks.
The result of the joint coordinated control has been processed within the meaning of European Enforcement Regulation No 31 for INTOSAI control standards.
The cooperation consisted of exchanging information to the extent set out in the contract and drawing up a joint final report on the outcome of parallel controls.
The purpose of the coordinated control was to verify selected cases of delivery and acquisition of goods in suspicious commercial transactions between value added tax payers from the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the "Cr") and the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as "Slovakia").
Both parties have contractually committed themselves to providing information from public sources, from the Value Added Tax Information Exchange System (VIES) and data on received and submitted requests for verification of commercial transactions between the Czech Republic and Slovakia.
The checks were carried out in parallel between June and December 2005.
In the Czech Republic, the control was carried out by the Department of State Budget and the Territorial Departments of Central Bohemia, North-West Bohemia, South Bohemia, South Moravia, Central Moravia and Northern Moravia.
The audited persons were the Ministry of Finance and 12 tax offices: the Tax Office in Mladá Boleslav, the Tax Office in Kolín, the Financial Office in Teplice, the Tax Office in Karlovy Vary, the Tax Office in Tábor, the Tax Office brno III, the Tax Office in Znojmo, the Tax Office in Zlín, the Tax Office in Šumperk, the Financial Office ostrava I, the Tax Office for Prague 7 and the Tax Office for Prague 9.
Control in the territory of the Slovak Republic was carried out by the Financial and Tax Section of the SAO SR in cooperation with the Expos of the SAO SR Banská Bystrica and Košice at 9 selected tax offices: Tax Office Bratislava I, Tax Office Komárno, Tax Office Trenčín, Tax Office Prievidza, Daňový úrad Zvolen, Daňový úrad Dolný Kubín, Tax Office Košice II, Tax Úradice V and Tax Council Michal.
Objective of checks:
The aim of the parallel control actions was to examine the procedure of financial or tax authorities in the administration of value added tax (hereinafter referred to as "VAT") after the integration of the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic into the single internal market of the European Union (hereinafter referred to as "the EU") and to examine the use of the VIES electronic information system, in particular when checking the application of the vat exemption entitlement.
The period of control in the coordinated period was from 1 January 2005 to 31 December 2005. 5. 2004 to 30. 6. 2005.
Summary of the results and evaluation of parallel control actions An electronic VIES system is in place in EU Member States, which allows tax authorities to check whether the supplier has been entitled to exempt taxable transactions from VAT and, in the country of destination, to check whether the purchaser has properly admitted and taxed the acquired goods.
VIES is not centralised within the EU, each Member State develops its own system.
The inspection identified differences of national systems of VIES in the Czech Republic and The Czech Republic in the following areas:
The summary reports shall indicate the values of the delivery of goods to other EU Member States, the values of the services provided shall not be included in the recapitulative reports.
Data from summary reports submitted by Czech payers are processed in the Czech Republic at the level of the tax authorities, where they are compared with data on supplies of goods to other EU Member States mentioned in vat tax returns.
The tax authorities transmit the summary report data to the Ministry of Finance (CLO), which sends it to other EU Member States.
In Slovakia, the data from the summary reports submitted by Slovak payers at the tax offices are only transferred to electronic form and processed centrally at the Tax Directorate of the Slovak Society (CLO).
In the Czech Republic, payers report the value of the supply of goods and the value of the supply of services to other EU Member States on separate lines of VAT returns, which makes it possible to compare the values specified in the summary reports with the values of the delivery of goods according to vat returns and to identify their possible differences.
In the Czech Technical Party, the values of the goods and services supplied to other EU Member States are reported cumulatively on the common line of the VAT return.
As a result, in the SR, the system does not automatically identify differences between the values of delivery of goods according to VAT returns and summary reports.
The separate reporting of the values of supplies of goods in VAT returns makes it possible to use the results of comparison of data when checking the exemption of supplies of goods to the EU from VAT.
The data received from summary reports submitted by payers in other EU Member States are processed at CLO and compared with the value of the acquisition of goods given by the payer from the Czech Republic or Slovakia in vat returns.
In the SR, this data is sent to the tax authorities and the tax authorities decide for themselves which cases of differences will be examined.
In the Czech Republic, the Ministry of Finance (CLO) determines which quantified differences between the values of delivery and acquisition of goods must be examined by the tax authorities and will transmit to the local tax authorities a list of these cases.
This ensures that the most significant derogations will ensure that VAT was granted at the correct amount when the goods were acquired.
Furthermore, the check highlighted some problems in the VAT management system of complications caused by the different reporting of intra-Community transactions (i.e. the supply and acquisition of goods carried out by payers from different EU Member States):
Summaries are submitted in the EU for each calendar quarter and the maximum deadline for processing and sending data to other EU Member States is set at 3 months from the end of the relevant quarter.
Shortening the period for which summaries are submitted to one month, together with the reduction of the processing period, would allow earlier access to data in VIES.
Thus, tax authorities could more effectively verify whether VAT has been granted at the correct level in intra-Community acquisitions.
At the same time, the submission of VAT returns and summaries for the same tax year (month) would allow for a faster verification of whether the payer has reported the same value of supplies of goods to the EU in both the recapitulative statement and the VAT return.
The differences between the values of delivery of goods reported by EU payers and the values of the acquisition of goods reported by the payers from the Czech Republic or The Czech Republic were due, inter alia, to the value of the goods reported by the payers from the Czech Republic. different reporting of intra-Community delivery and acquisition data in each EU Member State.
This included, for example, the placing of advances received in summary reports, or the reporting of intra-community deliveries in the vendor's recapitulative statement in a quarter other than intra-Community acquisitions in the purchaser's VAT return.
Unifying the conditions for reporting such data within the EU would lead to a streamlining of the control activities of national tax administrations.
The cooperation of the SAO, the Czech Republic and the SAO SR was also focused on the examination of selected intra-Community transactions carried out between the two states.
Together, a total of 40 cases of commercial transactions carried out between 29 Czech and 32 Slovak tax entities were examined, for which there were doubts about their implementation or suspected vat evasion.
The SAO, the Czech Republic and the SAO SR found, inter alia, the following:
tax entities have reported in their VAT returns for the purpose of unlawfully obtaining an excessive VAT deduction, the execution of intra-Community transactions that have not actually taken place;
tax entities have reported intra-community supplies in carousel transactions in which there has been a deliberate multiple reduction in the value of supplies in order to draw excessive VAT deductions;
suppliers reported in their VAT tax returns and summaries intra-Community supplies of goods exempt from VAT to purchasers who were so-called VAT-exempt. 'lost companies' and have not admitted the tax on the goods acquired;
suppliers have made intra-Community supplies of VAT-exempt goods to tax entities that have not been registered for VAT in another Member State.
In such cases, the supply should not have been exempted from VAT and should have been subject to vat in the supplier's country;
suppliers reported intra-Community supplies of higher value in their VAT returns than those reported by intra-Community acquisitions, in some cases the VAT was awarded at an incorrect amount.
The findings of the control action showed that VIES provides tax authorities with the information necessary to check the correct application of VAT in intra-Community transactions.
Tax authorities should pay particular attention to the thorough examination of the differences between data reported by VAT payers and data in the VIES system and the use of all information in tax proceedings.
The issue of value added tax after the accession of the Czech Republic and The Czech Republic to the EU
Value added tax
On 1 January 2005, the Council adopted Decision 5. 2004, the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic became members of the EU.
After joining the EU, internal borders and border controls on the movement of goods within the EU were abolished.
The VAT administrator was the vat administrator until 30 June 2006. 4. 2004 the competent tax office, with the exception of imports of goods and occasional bus services in the country where the tax administrator was the customs office.
In connection with the adoption of the new Act No. 235/2004 Coll., on Value Added Tax (hereinafter referred to as "Act No. 235/2004 Coll.), or Act No. 222/2004 Z. z., on the tax on added value (hereinafter referred to as "Act No. 222/2004 Z. z."), the vat administration of the acquisition of goods and services (previously imports) from other EU member states from customs offices to tax authorities, respectively.
The delivery of goods in the Czech Republic pursuant to the provisions of Section 13 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. means the transfer of the right to dispose of the goods as owner.
The delivery of goods from the Czech Republic to another EU Member State is the delivery of goods that have actually been shipped or transported to another EU Member State.
According to the provisions of Section 64 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll., this is an exempt taxable transaction with the right to deduct VAT if the goods are delivered to a person registered for VAT in another EU Member State.
The supply of goods in the SR pursuant to the provisions of Section 8 of Act No. 222/2004 Z. z. is considered to be the supply of tangible property, in which there is a change of ownership.
The supply of goods shall also be deemed to be the transfer of goods owned by a taxable person from the country to another Member State, provided that such goods are dispatched or transported by that person or on his behalf to another Member State for the purposes of his business.
According to the provisions of Section 43 of Law No 222/2004 Z. z. the supply of goods from the country to another Member State is exempt from VAT if the purchaser is a person identified for VAT in another Member State.
The acquisition of goods from another EU Member State in the Czech Republic pursuant to Section 16 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. means the acquisition of the right to dispose as owner of goods that is dispatched or transported by a person registered for VAT in another EU Member State.
The Czech payer buys goods at a price without VAT and his obligation is to grant VAT in the Czech Republic according to the provisions of Section 25 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll., subject to the conditions set out in § 73 of this Act, he is entitled to deduct VAT.
The acquisition of goods in the czech republic from another EU Member State in the Czech Republic pursuant to Section 11 of Act No. 222/2004 Z. z. means the acquisition of the right to dispose as owner of movable tangible property sent or transported by the pros andators to the supplier or the prom or on their behalf to the country from another Member State.
The tax liability in the Czech Republic is incurred by the payer when the goods are acquired in the czech republic from another Member State pursuant to the provisions of Section 20 of Act No. 222/2004 Z.z.
The payer may deduct VAT under the provisions of Section 49 of Act No. 222/2004 Z. z. if the tax is applied by him on the acquisition of goods in the country from another Member State pursuant to § §11 and 11a of this Act.
Triangular trade means, in accordance with the provisions of Section 17 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll., or Section 45 of Act No. 222/2004 Z. z. trade concluded between three persons registered for VAT in three different EU Member States, where the subject of the trade is the supply of the same goods between the three persons.
Intra-Community transactions are the supply and acquisition of goods carried out between VAT payers from different EU Member States.
The total volumes of intra-Community transactions made between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic are shown in the table below.
VIES system
A VAT information exchange system has been established within the EU to control the application of the vat exemption entitlement to intra-Community supplies of goods.
It includes the VIES electronic system, which allows tax authorities of EU Member States to check whether the supplier was entitled to exempt taxable transactions from VAT and, conversely, whether the acquirer has properly admitted and taxed the acquired goods.
The VIES information system is not centralised within the EU.
Each Member State develops its own VIES system.
National systems work on a common principle and are interconnected through the EU's common communication network, the so-called 'common communication network'. CCN (Common Communication Network; see diagram below).
In the Czech Republic, the VIES system was connected with an automated tax information system (hereinafter referred to as "ADIS"), in the Czech Republic with the application software of the tax information system (hereinafter referred to as "APV DIS").
These systems are used by the tax authorities as technical support for executive and management activities in the management of taxes and fees.
International administrative cooperation
Through international administrative cooperation, the tax administration of each EU member country obtains information on tax entities that, without such cooperation, would not have been able to obtain on its own.
The main objective of international administrative cooperation is to combat tax evasion and tax losses.
According to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, each Member State shall establish, within the internal organisational structure, a central unit in the field of administrative cooperation between EU Member States in the management of VAT, the so-called 'VAT'. CLO (Central Liaison Office).
In the Czech Republic, the Ministry of Finance – Central Financial and Tax Directorate, where the International Cooperation in VAT Management Unit (hereinafter referred to as the "MF CLO") was established, performs the tasks resulting from international cooperation.
The function of CLO in the SR is performed by the Tax Directorate of the Czech Technical Authority, the Department of International Administrative Cooperation (hereinafter referred to as "DR CLO").
These departments, inter alia, communicate with EU foreign administrations, in particular in the field of information exchange within the VIES system, exchange of spontaneous information and information at the request of EU tax administrations, coordination of multilateral (simultaneous) tax controls, verification of tax identification numbers (hereinafter referred to as "VAT registration numbers") of persons registered for VAT in other EU Member States and communicate with the European Commission.
In order to investigate an intra-Community transaction or to obtain further information relating to a particular tax entity, the tax authorities send requests for information to the EU via MF CLO or DR CLO.
Through these requests, they obtain information from the requested Member States which they can use for the correct determination of VAT.
Requests for information are mostly sent between CLO of EU Member States in electronic form, using a standardised SCAC form.

The Tax Office in the Czech Republic replied that the Czech payer had entered the acquisition of goods at this value only in an additional VAT return and delivered the same goods back to Slovak tax entities worth CZK 2,550,000 by the end of 2004. Czk.
On the basis of the international cooperation of the SAO, the Czech Republic and the SAO SR, it was found that the local tax authority granted the Slovak supplier the full right to an excessive deduction of VAT resulting from, inter alia, the slovak supplier. on the basis of this supply.
This tax office did not provide information on suspected re-export to the tax authorities locally to the relevant customers of goods imported back from the Czech payer.
These facts will prompt further scrutiny of business activities in connection with possible carousel fraud.
O
The Czech tax administrator requested, through the SCAC form, to verify the delivery of the technological line to the SR in the value of CZK 4,850,000. Czk in 2. 2004.
It emerged from the tax procedure carried out in the SR that only part of the technological line, a component worth CZK 3 395 000, was delivered. czk have not been delivered.
In examining this case, the SAO SR found that the VAT on the taxable transactions carried out was awarded by the Slovak tax entity out of eur 4 850 000. czk in the VAT tax return (hereinafter referred to as "DAP") for the tax year 7/2004.
The SAO, Cr further found that the Czech payer reported an excessive VAT deduction of CZK 655,000 for that quarter in its DAP. czk, which was created by applying the VAT deduction from the purchase of this technological line from another domestic payer.
On the basis of the results of the investigation, the Czech Tax Office concluded that the Czech and Slovak tax entities had established a business relationship for the purpose of unlawfully obtaining an excessive VAT deduction, questioned the implementation of the taxable transaction and did not recognise to the Czech payer part of the right to deduct in the amount of CZK 647 ths. Czk.

At the same time, this tax entity was not granted exemption from VAT on exports of goods in December 2002.

This tax entity did not cooperate with the tax administrator, DAP did not file and VAT for the months 7 to 12/2004 was assessed ex officio in the amount of CZK 0.

O
The Slovak company supplied goods (particleboard products) among others. american company that stored these goods in the Czech Republic in a free customs zone.
The operator of this free zone was listed on the invoices as the consignee of the goods.
In 2004, an American company, for example, was a company that was founded in 1940. purchased particleboard cladding worth USD 57,600 (at a unit price of $100/piece) from the Slovak payer, which she placed in a free zone.
Subsequently, the company transferred ownership of the goods to a Swiss company, worth USD 14,400 (unit price 25 USD/piece) and the goods were exported back to SR.
The goods were not unloaded in the Czech Republic, but left the area of the free zone on the same means of transport.
The Slovak tax administrator initiated tax checks on the individual tax periods of 2004 and 2005 with the supplier of the goods on suspicion of carousel transactions.
The examination of the underlying transactions was requested from the Czech local tax authorities through several SCAC forms.
The individual responses gradually created an image of the transactions and confirmed the involvement of stakeholders from the Czech Republic in carousel shops.
The SAO, the Czech Republic, in cooperation with the SAO SR, found that in these trade relations there was a deliberate gradual multiple reduction in the value of the goods.
On the basis of the information obtained, the Tax Directorate of the Czech Republic concluded that in this case the carousel trade was a free price formation (i.e. imports of undervalued goods and its overstatement by domestic companies located in the chain between the importer and the exporter) which is not a violation of the VAT Act in Slovakia.
Under the current legislation, the payment of an excessive VAT deduction to export companies cannot be prevented, since they fulfil all the conditions of the VAT exemption law.

O
The following 2 cases concern companies that are suspected of involvement in carousel fraud.
Transactions in goods (workwear) were carried out between the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic in the 4th century. 2004 and 1 December 2004. quarter 2005.
Slovak payer No. 1 supplied the goods to the Czech payer No. 2.
In the Czech Republic, the goods were then sold to payer No. 3, who delivered it back to the SR to payer No. 4 (see scheme No. 2).
A)
Czech payer No. 2 was to be purchased from slovak payer No. 1 in the 4th year of the year. In the quarter of 2004, goods (workwear) worth CZK 4,847,000 czk and in 1. In the quarter of 2005, goods worth CZK 17,050,000 Czk.
Since the acquisition declared by the Czech payer in DAP did not correspond to the data in VIES, the local tax administrator sent to the SR on 25 April 2005 the following information: 5. 2005 request for information.
In response, the Slovak tax administrator expressed doubts about the implementation of business cases as well as the implementation of the payment.
On 8 June 2005, the Council adopted Decision On 6. 2005, a request for information concerning goods worth CZK 16,575,000 was received at MF CLO from SR. Sk, which was to be delivered in December 2004 by the Slovak payer No. 1 to the Czech payer No. 2.
The Slovak side demanded to check whether the Czech payer No. 2 had actually accepted the goods, admitted to DAP and paid VAT.
The official record drawn up by the local tax administrator in the Czech Republic shows that the Czech payer No. 2 has not been based for a long time at an address registered in the Commercial Register.
Although they were VAT payers with a monthly tax period, dap submitted a quarterly tax period.
In view of this, the Czech tax administrator could not measure VAT.
The carrying out of taxable transactions between the Slovak payer No. 1 and the Czech payer No. 2 indicated in the application amounting to CZK 16,575,000. In view of the above, Sk could not be verified.
The Czech tax administrator suspected the involvement of both entities in the carousel trade in order to draw on an excessive VAT deduction.
B)
Czech payer No. 3, engaged in the purchase and sale of passenger cars, filed for the tax period of 1 and 2/2005 DAP, in which he reported the delivery of goods (workwear) to the Slovak payer No. 4 for a total value of CZK 21,935,000. Czk.
These workwear was to be purchased by Czech payer No. 3 from Czech payer No. 2 between December 2004 and January 2005.
The local tax authority sent to the Slovak Republic a request for information, the subject of which was, in particular, to verify whether the Slovak payer No. 4 had purchased goods worth CZK 1,025,000 from the Czech payer No. 3 in December 2004. czk and in 1. 2005, worth CZK 21,935,000. Czk.
The reply to this request for information received from the Slovak Government showed that in DAP for 12/2004, the Slovak payer No 4 reported a zero value of the acquisition of goods from another EU Member State and in DAP for months 1 and 2/2005 indicated the value of the acquisition of goods from another EU Member State at only 1 193 ths. Group.
The Slovak payer No. 4 did not respond to the call for tax documents for the tax year 10/2004 to 3/2005.
In the local investigation carried out in the SR, it was found that the company was not present at the address indicated in the Commercial Register.
The reply also stated that this payer fulfils all the characteristics of the so-called ''s'. "lost companies", and therefore there is a reasonable suspicion of carousel fraud.
The SAO SR was told that the Slovak tax administrator sent dr clo an initiative to carry out simultaneous checks with the tax administration of the Czech Republic, which will be carried out with the tax entities involved.
During the coordinated inspection, the Czech tax administrator collected documents that would confirm or refute the existence of the goods.
VAT will be measured according to the outcome of the investigation.
The case is also being dealt with by the Police of the Czech Republic.
Control action progress
In the preparation of parallel control actions, a coordination meeting of representatives of the SAO, the Czech Republic with representatives of the SAO SR took place in the first half of July 2005.
The participants of this meeting became familiar with the legislation on VAT in both countries and the integration of the VIES electronic system into national databases.
The negotiations resulted in the specification of the scope of cooperation and the setting of conditions for the selection of control samples.
Both parties agreed that cooperation would focus on the following areas: a) verification of the validity and correctness of vat registration plates of persons registered for VAT in the Czech Republic or SR in intra-Community supplies; b) examination of data on intra-community acquisitions specified in DAP by the payer in the Czech Republic using information from summary reports (hereinafter referred to as "SH") of payers from the SR system contained in the VIES system, and vice versa; c) exchange of information between tax administrations in the Czech Republic and in The Slovak Republic on commercial transactions carried out.
Furthermore, it was agreed that the selection of tax entities for inspection will be carried out on the following volume of intra-Community supplies between the Czech Republic and The Czech Republic and according to the number of requests for international cooperation sent and received between the Czech Republic and the SR via the SCAC form.
5.1 Intra-Community transactions
The procedure for processing information by the tax administrations of the Czech Republic and The Czech Republic in intra-Community delivery and acquisition of goods illustrates the following scheme.
5.1.1 Intra-Community delivery
If the VAT payer carries out intra-Community supplies, he is obliged to pay until 25 April 2010 to pay for the intra-Community delivery. the day after the end of the calendar quarter.
The payer in the Czech Republic provides in SH summary information on the deliveries made by him to another EU Member State exempt from VAT for the previous calendar quarter.
The payer in SR is obliged to enter into the SH the value of goods that have been exempted and delivered from the country to other EU Member States for the calendar quarter.
Data on the value of the delivered goods are always given in Czech or Slovak currency broken down by individual tax entities, indicating their VAT number under which they were registered in their country.
Service data are not included in sh.
If the payer in the Czech Republic finds that he has entered erroneous data in sh, he is obliged to submit a follow-up SH.
If the payer in SR finds that the data specified in the SH were incomplete or incorrect, he submits an corrective sh before the expiry of the deadline for filing sh, after the expiry of that period he is obliged to file an additional SH.
The VIES system allows the exchange of information on registration data of VAT payers in EU Member States.
Payers from the Czech Republic or The Czech Republic can verify whether the VAT number of the relevant purchaser is registered in the given EU Member State.
The data from the submitted SH are grouped by the individual VAT registration number of the purchasers at MF CLO or DR CLO by VIES system.
A summary value of all deliveries for each VAT number of the acquirer is created and the code of the method of filling from all its Czech or Slovak suppliers, the so-called "vat number". L1QD files.
Data from L1QD files shall be sent to the relevant EU Member States no later than three months after the end of the quarter to which the data relate.
The total value of intra-Community transactions between the Czech Republic and The Czech Republic (from the L1QD files) is shown in the following table.
If vies in another Member State detects the wrong VAT number of the acquirer in the L1QD files sent, it generates a so-called 'vat number'. O_MCTL message that contains all the wrong VAT registration number, indicating the type of error.
This message is subsequently sent to MF CLO or DR CLO.
The O_MCTL report can contain 4 types of errors: formally erroneous VAT registration, VAT registration is not registered in a given state or has never been allocated, the acquirer with a certain VAT number was not a VAT payer in a given quarter, the vat registration of the acquirer was terminated during the quarter.
In the Czech Republic, MF CLO transmits data from received reports O_MCTL to the tax authorities.
If the erroneous EU payer's VAT number is used in one of the sh or subsequent SH lines sent, the a so-called ADIS is generated by the relevant tax authority. "Notice of doubt on VAT ID".
The Tax Office will examine whether the delivery to the VAT-registered payer in another EU Member State has actually taken place and records the result of the verification in the system.
In SR, DR CLO in VIES processes all messages O_MCTL and electronically sends them to locally competent tax authorities together with the identification of tax payers who have mentioned the wrong VAT number in their SH.
The tax authorities subsequently invite the payer to submit an additional SH and the indication of the valid VAT number or the tax office will examine the delivery of the goods with the relevant payer when reporting the invalid VAT number in the filed SH.
Data on the number of erroneous VAT registration numbers related to intra-Community transactions carried out between the Czech Republic and The Czech Republic are given in the following table.
Out of a total of 41,728 VAT registration numbers of Czech payers listed in the Slovak payers' SH in the period from 2 January 2004 to 31 December 2004, the number of Czech payers in the Czech Period of Validity and The Czech Vat. quarter 2004 to 1 January 2004 929 erroneous VAT registrations, i.e. 929 VAT registrations, were 929 100 000 000 000 000 000 000 2,23 %.
Out of a total of 62,997 VAT registration numbers for Slovak payers listed in the Czech payers' SH in the same period, 416 were erroneous VAT registration numbers, i.e. 416 VAT registration numbers. 0,66 %.
When reporting intra-Community transactions between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, Czech VAT payers reported on average fewer erroneous VAT registration rates in their SH than the payers from the Slovak Republic.
When examining the activities of financial or tax authorities, it was found that the VIES system did not provide, in all cases, up-to-date information on the validity of VAT registrations of tax entities.
E.g.:
- although, at the request of the tax administrator in the Czech Republic, the VIES system confirmed the validity of the registration of the tax entity in the 4th ed. a report was subsequently generated O_MCTL due to the termination of the payer's registration in that quarter.
The investigation established that the marketing authorisation was terminated only on 1 January 2004. 1. 2005;
- The SAO SR also found that 6 tax entities submitted sh in which the erroneous VAT number was reported, but the reports O_MCTL did not contain that VAT number.
In the SR, the filed SH shall be transferred to the tax offices in electronic form and the data from them are sent to DR CLO.
Following the subsequent processing of this data in the VIES system, DR CLO will send to the competent tax authorities the so-called "tax authorities". breakdowns of errors in SH filed by tax entities for the relevant quarters.
The SAO SR compared the data on the occurrence of erroneous data in the SH as at 26. 7. 2005 (i.e. data processed before the start of the inspection) and on 2 January 2005, the commission concluded that the information carried out in the draft member state of the member states concerned was not carried out in respect of the information provided by the Commission. 2. 2006 (i.e. data processed after the completion of the control).
The following table provides a comparison of data.
It is apparent from the above data that the inspection of the SAO SR had an impact not only on the reduction of the number of SH with the wrong VAT number (on average 199 SH per quarter), but also on the reduction of the number of unrecedified errors in the SH (on average by 431 errors per quarter).
In the Czech Republic, the value of intra-Community deliveries specified by the payer in the relevant DAP lines is compared with the value of intra-Community deliveries specified by this payer in the quarterly SH.
ADIS automatically indicates the differences between these values.
The tax administrator should examine the differences, remove any uncertainties and use the data obtained to determine the tax liability.
The SAO, Cr found that the audited tax authorities did not check these differences in 27 cases.
The total difference between the values shown in SH and DAP in these cases was 537 231 ths. Czk.
From 3. In the quarter of 2004, the ADIS system allowed the tax administrator in the Czech Republic to consider the difference between the values specified in SH and DAP in the amount of up to 0.5% of the total value of intra-community deliveries according to the SH as a match and set it up in the ADIS system.
For payers with a large volume of intra-Community deliveries for one quarter, 0,5 % of the value represents a not insignificant amount, therefore the tax authorities should not set the sh and DAP conformity in these cases without clarifying the causes of the differences.
E.g. without verification, the tax administrator set a consensus in the event of a difference in values of CZK 1,561,000. Czk.
The examination of differences in the Czech Republic and The Czech Republic was complicated by the fact that sh for each calendar quarter was submitted to the payer within 25 days after the end of this quarter.
For taxpayers with a monthly tax period at the time of dap filing for the first two months of the calendar quarter, the tax authorities could not compare the intra-community delivery values specified in these DAPs with those according to SH.
In these cases, the tax authorities became aware of any data mismatch in DAP and SH only at the time when the tax liability or excessive deduction of VAT was assessed, or Returned.
5.1.2 Intra-Community acquisition
The VIES system provides, among other things, the information on the values of intra-Community transactions carried out within EU Member States.
Acquisition of goods in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, the delivered data from sh submitted by payers from other EU Member States (delivered L1QD) is processed by MF CLO.
During processing, the data are converted at the minimum and maximum daily exchange rates of the Czech National Bank for the relevant period and then compared with the acquisition value indicated by the Czech payers in DAP for the relevant quarter.
The value of the acquisition of goods reported by the payer in dap should be within the minimum and maximum recalculated values L1QD (L1min and L1max values).
If the value reported in DAP is lower than the L1min value, the so-called "value" is generated for the payers with the most significant irregularities. the verification command.
Orders to verify the acquisition of goods are a warning to problematic tax entities and are transmitted to the locally competent tax authorities, which must investigate the data transmitted.
The number of verification orders concerning audited tax authorities in the Czech Republic is shown in the following table.
The SAO, Cr found that the audited tax authorities in 33 cases did not check for irregularities in the values of intra-community acquisitions, to which the received verification orders pointed out.
In these cases, the total difference between the values shown in sh by payers from other EU Member States and DAP was at least 148,319,000. Czk.
The SAO, Cr selected for inspection 533 files of tax entities for which the audited tax authorities received an verification order from MF CLO.
The following common causes of differences between the values mentioned in dap of the purchaser and in the supplier's SH were identified by the inspection: on the part of the purchaser (Czech payer) in 263 cases the purchaser did not indicate the acquisition of the goods in the proper DAP, in 93 cases the payer admitted the acquisition of the goods in a tax year other than that in which he was obliged to declare tax, in 6 cases the purchaser stated the value of the acquired goods in the wrong dap line , on the part of the supplier (eu payer) in 88 cases eu payers included in their SH the values of the services provided to the Czech payer, of which in 54 cases they were payers from The Czech Republic, in 39 cases the suppliers included in sh the delivery of goods in a different tax period than the purchasers from the Czech Republic in their DAP, in 22 cases the suppliers reported in the SH incorrect VAT number of the Czech payer , in 16 cases suppliers reported erroneous values of delivery of goods in SH, in 12 cases suppliers included in sh the value of goods delivered to the Czech Republic before 1. 5. 2004, in 5 cases suppliers included in sh the value of the advances received.
On the sr payers' side, the value of the services provided was most often misclassification in the SH.
54 such cases were identified in the audited tax authorities.
E.g. when examining the verification order, it was found that the difference in the value of CZK 10,974,000 was between 10,974 and 100 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 Czk was created by the fact that the Slovak payer was introduced to SH for 1. In the third quarter of 2005, the provision of services (construction works and delivery of goods including assembly in the Czech Republic).
Another reason for the differences was the inclusion of the values of advances received in the SH, e.g. 2 Slovak payers reported in SH received advances from Czech payers, resulting in the generation of an order to verify the difference of 3,580 czk. Czk.
Orders to validate purchased items are generated only once per quarter.
In cases where there is subsequently a change in SH data in EU Member States, such as the following: change of customer of goods in the Czech Republic or increased value of delivery of goods to the Czech Republic, new verification orders are not generated.
Since VIES does not automatically draw attention to these changes, the local tax administrator may not be able to find out the facts relevant for the correct determination of the tax liability on the goods acquired and there is a strong likelihood of VAT evasion.
By checking the SAO, cr it was found that this situation occurred e.g. in the following cases:
The Slovak payer stated in SH for 2. In the quarter of 2004, the value of the delivery of goods to the Czech payer amounted to CZK 1,504,000. Group.
On 1 January 2005, the Council adopted Decision On 2. 2005, the tax office sent a request for information to the locally competent Czech payer in the SR, because the Czech payer granted the acquisition of goods in the amount of CZK 425,000. Czk.
On 1 January 2006, the Slovak payer submitted a complaint to the Slovak payer of the application of the tax procedure. 3. 2005 additional SH, in which he corrected the details of the delivery of goods to the Czech Republic, by reducing the value of the delivery for the originally mentioned Czech payer to 538,000. Sk and increasing the value of the delivered goods for another Czech payer from the amount of 194 ths. Sk to 1,160,000 Group.
The four Slovak payers mentioned in their SH for 2. In the quarter of 2004, intra-Community delivery to payers from the Czech Republic totaled CZK 10,240,000. Sk (i.e. 8,183,000 (czk 100,

On the basis of the international exchange of information, it was found that the goods were delivered in all cases to another Czech payer who was not listed in the SH submitted by the Slovak payer.
During the first period of 1 January 2004, the In the quarter of 2005, Slovak payers increased in the additional SH related to 2. In total, the value of intra-Community supplies for this Czech payer was 10,240,000. Group.

Unifying the conditions for reporting this data would lead to a streamlining of the control activities of tax authorities.
Acquisition of goods in SR
In slovakia, the APV DIS system allows you to compare data on the value of acquired goods obtained through VIES from other EU Member States with those given in the DAP of Slovak purchasers.
The method by which the data are compared is called the "MIN-MAX method".
This method shall recalculate the values of delivery of goods listed in the SH by payers from other EU Member States at the minimum and maximum exchange rates for the relevant quarter.
There will be an MIN-MAX interval, which is used to compare with the acquisition values of goods specified in the DAP of Slovak payers.
DR CLO shall send tax authorities information on the intra-Community acquisition values specified in DAP and the values of EU delivery in VIES.
The tax administrator shall decide which persons registered for VAT the difference will be verified, taking into account other risk analysis criteria.
On the basis of the data provided by the DR CLO, the SAO SR selected 57 files of Slovak goods purchasers for inspection at the audited tax offices, of which 25 payers also purchased goods from the Czech Republic, for which the highest differences were found between the acquisition values obtained from the VIES system and the values declared in dap.
The inspection carried out by the SAO SR confirmed the fact that the tax authorities did not rigorously check the differences obtained using the MIN-MAX method and thus did not verify the accuracy of the data contained in the DAP of slovak customers.
As part of the inspection, the SAO SR asked the tax authorities to carry out 47 local investigations on specific tax entities.
During the inspection of the SAO SR at the tax offices, 31 local investigations were closed.
For Slovak companies, which reported significant differences in MIN-MAX values when acquiring goods from EU member countries, among others, the total number of companies in the eu-MAX system was not limited to the fact that the total number of goods from EU member states was reported by the VIES system. the following facts are identified:

5.2 International Exchange of L3 Level Information
The exchange of information at L3 level is initiated by local tax authorities who send their requests for information (hereinafter referred to as "ŽOI") or spontaneous information (hereinafter referred to as "SPI"), relating to a particular tax entity or transaction, via the MF CLO, respectively.
dr clo to another EU country. The aim of the ZOI is, for example, to ensure that the proof of the execution of the transaction in the context of intra-Community transactions, examination of a particular VAT number, etc.
In the case of SPI, it is a communication of information relevant to tax authorities in another EU member state.
Cooperation in the field of information exchange is regulated by Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
The maximum time limit for replying to the IOI was set in Article 2 of the basic Regulation. 8 of this Regulation for 3 months.
The conditions for the admissibility of applications are laid down by the Commission Decision of the European Communities of 15 December 2003 on the application of Articles 87 and 88 of the EC Treaty to state aid to certain products covered by 11. 2004, which provides that, unless the participating States agree otherwise, the IOC must cover commercial transactions of at least EUR 1 500 excluding VAT.
Where the ZOI concerns a commercial transaction of less than EUR 15 000 net of VAT, the requested authority may refuse to reply with regard to its workload.
The procedure for dealing with the incoming ŽOI by the Tax Administration of the Czech Republic, including the internal time limits set for processing at individual organizational levels, is illustrated by the following scheme.
In the SR, an internal deadline was set for the processing of the ZOI by the tax authorities to 2 months so that the three-month period under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 could be respected.
MF CLO has received from the SR from 1 January 2004 the 5. 2004 to 30. 6. 2005 a total of 29 ŽOI and 3 SPI.
Of the 29 received IO, 26 (i.e. 89.7 %) 3 months and 3 (i.e. 10.3%) have been settled after that period.
In the same period, DR CLO from the Czech Republic adopted a total of 71 ŽOI and 7 SPI.
Of the 71 received IO, 64 (i.e. 90.1 %) within the specified period of 3 months, 5 (i.e. 7.0%) was settled after this deadline (for the other 2 cases it was not possible to determine the time limit for the materials transmitted).
The following graph provides more detailed data on the time of processing of the ŽOI received by MF CLO or DR CLO.
The following table provides the reasons for sending the ZOI, as shown on the SCAC forms.
Conclusion
On the basis of international cooperation, compliance with Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 on administrative cooperation in the field of VAT and the use of VIES for the exchange of information between EU Member States has been examined, in particular when monitoring the application of the right to VAT exemptions.
International cooperation made it possible to examine selected intra-community transactions carried out between VAT payers from the Czech Republic and The Czech Republic.
By examining the transactions selected, it was found that, on the basis of the international exchange of information, the tax authorities of both countries revealed the cases of companies carrying out fictitious intra-Community business transactions in order to obtain excessive VAT deductions, as well as cases where the purchasers did not admit VAT on the received supplies of goods at the correct amount.
Furthermore, the control identified differences in the processing and use of VIES data by the tax administrations of both countries.
The review also highlighted problems caused by the different reporting of data on intra-Community supplies and purchases of goods in each EU Member State.
Unifying the conditions for reporting such data within the EU would lead to a streamlining of the control activities of national tax administrations.
By examining the procedure of the financial or tax authorities in the management of VAT and the use of the VIES system, it was found that the tax or tax authorities did not make sufficient use of all the possibilities of the VIES system and the relevant legal authorisations.
Furthermore, it was found that VIES did not provide up-to-date information on the supply of goods and on the validity of the registration of tax entities for VAT in all cases.
The SA SAO compared the data on the occurrence of erroneous data in the SH, processed before the start of the inspection, with the data processed after the completion of the inspection.
It was clear from the comparison of these data that the inspection of the SAO SR had an impact not only on the reduction of the number of SH with the erroneously mentioned VAT number, but also on the reduction of the number of unrecedified errors in the SH.
In the event of irregularities in the reported data, the SAO SR asked the tax authorities to carry out local investigations or to carry out tax checks.
The SAO, the Czech Republic did not have such an option within the framework of the current legislation in the Czech Republic.
The findings of the control action showed that VIES provided tax authorities with the basic information necessary to check the correct application of VAT in intra-Community transactions.
Given that there is still room for tax evasion in this area, there is a need to pay increased attention to intra-Community transactions in the management of VAT.
Communiqué
This report was prepared in Czech, English and Slovak and signed by the President of the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the President of the Najvyššie Control Board of the Slovak Republic.
Parallel control of value added tax administration and excise duties between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic
Introductory word
This information material provides an overview of the progress and results of parallel control actions carried out by the Supreme Audit Office and the Najvy higher control office of the Slovak Republic, which focused on the area of value added management and excise duties.
Cooperation between the supreme control offices of the two countries was carried out on the basis of a cooperation agreement in control activities concluded in February 2004.
The theme of parallel control actions has been chosen in view of the fact that indirect taxes contribute significantly to the revenues of the state budgets of both countries.
The design of value added tax, allowing the repayment of the excessive deduction, provides scope for tax fraud or evasion.
High rates of excise duty, in particular for tobacco and tobacco products, alcohol and mineral oils, mean a high profit for those who escape taxation by illegally selling such goods.
Tax fraud is a problem not only in the Czech Republic and Slovakia, but also in other countries of the European Union.
Given the need to address this issue comprehensively throughout the European Union, the highest audit institutions of the Member States of the European Union have created a working group of VAT Working Group, involving the most active control bodies of both countries.
The greatest contribution of the control actions carried out can be seen not only in the exchange of experience, but in particular in a joint effort to identify problematic areas of indirect tax administration in order to reduce the scope for tax evasion.
The experience gained and the knowledge will be used in the framework of planned indirect tax controls, aimed primarily at involving tax authorities of both States in the VIES system, allowing for control of the movement of goods between Member States of the European Union.
Report on the results of the control of value added tax and excise duties for the period 2002 and 2003
1. Introduction
Inspection number: (CZ) 04/07 (SK) 18/2004
Subject of inspection:
(CZ) Value added tax and excise duty
(S)(100)( Control of the tax administrator's procedure for the administration, control and recovery of value added tax and excise duties
On 11.2. In 2004, the Cooperation Agreement was concluded in the control activities between the Supreme Audit Office (hereinafter referred to as the SAO) and the Najvy higher control office of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as the SAO SR). The subject of the contract was cooperation in the parallel control actions carried out 'Value added tax and excise duty', included in the SAO's control activity plan for 2004 under No 04/07 and "Control of the procedure of the dane administrator in the management, control and enforcement of the tax on the added value and the consumption taxes", included in the audit activity plan of the SAO SR under No. 18/2004.
The cooperation consisted of exchanging information to the extent set out in the contract and drawing up a joint final report on the outcome of the checks.
In the contract, the two parties undertook to provide each other with information from public sources, from the customs administration database and from the files of tax authorities kept by tax authorities in the Czech Republic and by tax authorities in the Slovak Republic, which the Contracting Parties could not obtain when checking the application of value added tax and excise duties on imports and exports from sources in the territory of the respective State.
The checks were carried out in parallel between January and August 2004.
On the territory of the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as "the Czech Republic"), the control was carried out by the Department of the State Budget and the Territorial Departments of South Bohemia, North-East Bohemia, South Moravia, Central Moravia and Northern Moravia.
The audited persons were the Directorate-General of Customs and 12 selected tax offices: The Tax Office for Prague 1, the Tax Office for Prague 3, the Tax Office in České Budějovice, the Tax Office in Frýdek-Místek, the Tax Office in Hodonin, the Tax Office in Jihlava, the Tax Office in Kostelec nad Orlicí, the Tax Office in Kroměříž, the Tax Office in Písek, the Tax Office in Rožnov pod Radhoštěm, the Financial Office in Ústí nad Orlicí , The Tax Office in Velké Meziříčí.
The inspection on the territory of the Slovak Republic (hereinafter referred to as the Slovak Republic) was carried out by the Section of the Tax and Customs Administration of the Sao SR in cooperation with the Expos of the SAO SR Banská Bystrica and Košice at 10 selected tax offices:
Tax office Bratislava pre selected tax entities, Tax Office Bratislava III, Tax Office Trnava, Tax Office Of Pooh-Breeding, Tax Office Banská Bystrica I, Tax Office Liptovský Mikuláš, Tax Office Žilina I, Tax Office Žilina II, Tax Office Košice I and Tax Office Košice IV.
Objective of the scan
The aim of the control actions was to examine the fulfilment of the obligations of the financial and tax authorities and customs offices in the administration of value added tax and excise duties, with a focus on the collection of these taxes on the import and export of goods and services.
The aim of the international cooperation was to verify imports and exports of selected commodities between the Czech Republic and The Czech Republic in the Customs Database of the Czech Republic and the Customs Database of the Czech Republic and their subsequent verification in tax returns at the relevant financial or tax offices.
The audited period was 2002 and 2003.
2. Recapitulation of the results of the inspection
2.1. General evaluation of control activities
In the framework of international cooperation, the SAO forwarded 22,206 items of single customs declarations (hereinafter referred to as "JCD") on imports and exports of goods between the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic from the Czech Customs Database and, conversely, the SAO forwarded the SAO from the SR customs database 30 221 jcd items.
A comparison of typed JCD items from the Customs Database of the Czech Republic and the Customs Database of the Czech Republic was carried out.
Of the 5,883 selected JCD items from the Czech customs database, a total of 43% of related JCD items were assigned.
Of the 12,343 JCD items selected from the SR customs database, a total of 26% of related JCD entries were assigned.
On the basis of unassigned JCD items, a selection of files of tax entities for which the reported imports and exports were further verified in cooperation with the customs administrations of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic was carried out at the financial or tax offices.
On the basis of the exchange of information from the documents of the customs administrations of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic and the financial and tax authorities, the implementation of the reported imports and exports between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic was verified in the territory of the other state.
The SAO and the SAO SR carried out a joint pilot check at the border customs crossing Stary Hrozenkov - Drietoma, in which the two parties cooperated closely in verifying the correctness of the data on the movement of goods between the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic.
The check did not identify weaknesses in the registration of selected cases of imports and exports of goods carried out in 2002.
International cooperation made it possible to examine trade transactions between trading partners from both Countries and highlighted shortcomings in the registration of imports and exports.
2.2. Summary of the results of the inspection
In the field of international cooperation, the control of the SAO and the SAO SR focused on imports and exports of spirits and spirits, tobacco and tobacco products, computers and computer components, mobile phones and their components, and other types of goods, where appropriate.
On the basis of the inspection of the files of tax entities at the selected financial or tax offices, the SAO requested verification of the implementation of exports of goods reported to 40 JCD in the total statistical value of CZK 15,301,093 and the SR SAO on export verification at a statistical value of SK 56,989.
The SAO and the SAO found, inter alia, the following:
- commercial transactions were not declared in the same way on both sides, which made it difficult to identify the corresponding imports and exports in the Customs Database of the Czech Republic and the Customs Database of the Czech Republic,
- the error rate in entering data into customs databases made it impossible to identify certain imports or exports,
- some exports from the Czech Republic have not been shown to be corresponding imports into the Czech Republic.
In such cases, there is a reasonable suspicion of fictitious exports of goods for the purpose of undue application of value added tax deductions,
- tax entities have not complied with certain statutory obligations when reporting imports and exports in value added tax returns,
- deficiencies have been identified in the activities of the tax authorities and the tax authorities in the management of value added tax and excise duties and in their cooperation with the customs authorities.
In the field of value added tax and excise duties, international trade will continue to need to be addressed in order to effectively minimise tax evasion.
In particular, it is important to improve the activities of tax administrations in the exercise of value added tax administration.
Effective control of excise duties is the control of the circulation of documents, systematic physical control of goods and mutual exchange of information on the import and export of goods.
3. Description of the status of value added tax and excise duties
Value added tax
Value added tax (hereinafter referred to as 'VAT') was levied by the tax authorities or tax authorities on taxable transactions carried out in the country and by customs authorities on importation of goods.
The tax revenues were determined by the difference between the selected own tax liability and the refunded excessive VAT deductions at the tax authorities.
VAT revenues at customs offices were determined by the amount of taxes collected by them.
The tax collected by the customs authorities was reflected in the deductions of the tax applied to the tax authorities or tax authorities in accordance with the basic principles of the VAT mechanism.
For most tax authorities or tax authorities, excessive VAT deductions outweighed the tax liability.
VAT is one of the main taxes in terms of state budget revenue, as it accounted for about 31% of the tax revenues of the State Budget of the Czech Republic in 2003 and about 42% in tax revenues of the state budget of the Czech Republic.
In 2003, the total collection of VAT in the Czech Republic amounted to EUR 162.9 billion. Czk.
In 2003, the tax and customs authorities collected a total of EUR 394.3 billion for VAT. Total vat deductions amounted to CZK 231.4 billion. Czk.
The total collection of VAT in the SR amounted to EUR 83.8 billion in 2003. Group.
In 2003, the tax and customs authorities collected EUR 187.0 billion for VAT. The total of EUR 103.2 billion was eur 103.2 billion and the excess VAT deductions were refunded. Group.
Excise duties
The collection of excise duties ('spd') was carried out by the competent tax authorities and on imports of products subject to spd by customs authorities.
The Share of the SpD in tax revenues of the state budget in the Czech Republic in 2003 was approximately 16% and in the Czech Republic about 19%.
The total collection of spd collected in the Czech Republic by the tax and customs authorities in 2003 amounted to EUR 85.6 billion. in the Czech Air And amounted to CZK 38.0 billion. Group.
4. Course of control action
Cooperation between the SAO and the SAO SR took place in two stages.
In the first stage, a comparison was made of imports and exports of selected commodities from the customs databases of the Czech Republic and The Czech Republic, in the second stage the results of this comparison were used in the mutual verification of the realization of selected commercial transactions between the Czech Republic and The Czech Republic and in the checks carried out on the territory of both states.
4.1.
Preparation of the control action
The first proposal for cooperation in parallel CONTROLS of VAT and spd was presented at a working meeting of representatives of the SAO and the SAO SR in April 2003.
In November 2003, a coordination meeting was held, at which, inter alia, the Commission adopted a meeting on the coordination of the European Union's foreign and private ly in the european union. agreed the selection of commodities - the types of goods that posed a significant risk in compliance with customs and tax regulations: - alcohol and spirits, tariff headings No. 2207 and 2208, - Tobacco and tobacco products, tariff headings Nos. 2401, 2402 and 2403, - computers and computer components, subheadings No 8471 and 8473 30, - mobile phones and their accessories, customs tariff subheadings No 8525 20 91 , 8525 20 99, 8529 90 40.
Both parties agreed that the selection of tax entities for inspection will be made: a) from unassigned items identified by comparison of exports and imports of selected commodities between the Czech Republic and The Slovak Republic, b) from entities carrying out imports and exports on a regular or one-off basis in large volumes, c) on the basis of findings from the checks carried out by the selected tax and tax authorities.
4.2. Comparison of customs databases of the Czech Republic and The Czech Republic
In the first stage, a sample of imports and exports of selected commodities for the month of October 2002 tested the mechanism for the mutual assignment of JCD items registered in the customs databases of the Czech Republic and The Czech Republic.
Subsequently, part of exports from the Czech Republic were compared with imports into the Czech Republic for 2002 and vice versa for selected commodities according to the Customs Tariff:
- Ethyl alcohol undenatured with an alcoholic strength by volume of 80% vol or more; ethyl alcohol and other distillates denatured, of any alcoholic strength,
- Ethyl alcohol undenatured with an alcoholic strength by volume of less than 80 % vol.; distillates, liqueurs and other spirit drinks,
- 2401 Unprocessed tobacco; tobacco waste,
- 2402 Cigars (whether or not with cut-off ends), cigarillos and cigarettes of tobacco or tobacco substitutes,
- 2403 Other tobacco products and tobacco substitutes; homogenised or reconstituted tobacco; tobacco extracts and essences,
- 8525 20 91 Transmitting apparatus containing receiving equipment: For the cellular network (mobile phones),
- 8525 20 99 Transmitting apparatus containing reception equipment: Other,
- 8529 90 40 Parts suitable for use solely or principally with apparatus of headings 8525 to 8528.
Other: Parts of apparatus falling within subs and other subs falling within subs and other subs falling within subs and regulations 8525 10 50, 8525 20 99, 8525 40 11 and 8527 90 92.
JCD entries from the customs databases of the Czech Republic and The Czech Republic were assigned to each other on the basis of the conformity of the individual paragraphs of the JCD (e.g. invoiced price, quantity, weight, registration number of the vehicle carrying the cargo, the date of crossing of the state border, the customs tariff item, etc.).
The results of the comparison are shown in the following tables and charts.
The intertriation of individual imports and exports made it difficult, inter alia, to export to the community. the fact that commercial transactions have not been declared in the same way on both sides.
For example, exports from the Czech Republic, declared on one export JCD, were declared in the territory of the SR to more import JCD, or the export JCD had a different number of items from the import JCD.
Other factors that influenced the success of the assignment were the different composition of data in the customs databases of the Czech Republic and The Czech Republic, as well as the time shift between the registration of exports in the customs database of one country and the records of the corresponding imports in the customs database of the other country.
The results of the comparison were used in the selection of control samples at the audited financial and/or tax offices.
Priority was given to some tax entities that made imports or exports between the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic, which were not identified in both databases.
Furthermore, some tax entities for which data on imports or exports between the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic were found in both databases were selected for verification of the business transactions reported in the VAT tax returns.
4.3. Pilot check at the Old Hrozenkov-Drietoma border customs crossing
The border customs crossing for the pilot inspection was selected on the basis of a joint analysis of unassigned JCD items in the customs databases of the Czech Republic and The Slovak Republic.
On the basis of a bilateral agreement between the customs authorities of the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic, the use of control sheets has been established at the border customs crossings between the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic since 1.6.1998.
The aim of this measure was to eliminate customs and tax evasion as far as possible, to ensure an overview of the movement of means of transport carrying goods of a commercial nature in the customs area and to create the conditions for the comparison of customs records.
The joint pilot control was carried out on 8 and 8 December 2004. 3. 2004 to 26. 3. 2004 and was aimed at examining this customs control system.
Procedure for the use of control sheets at the Border Customs Crossing of The Stary Hrozenkov-Drietoma:
1) Weighing the vehicle, issuing the control sheet and handing it over to the driver.
2) Shutdown of the vehicle in the indicated sector in the parking lot.
Customs clearance in the check-in hall by the Police of the Czech Republic, The Police of the Czech Republic, the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic.
The execution of the check-in was confirmed by the individual components by stamping the checklist.
(3) The attachment of the vehicle to the physical inspection area.
Presentation of the control certificate, JCD, or other documents to the customs administration worker - control of the execution of all prescribed operations and documents.
Perform a physical check by the relevant components.
Dissuasing the vehicle from customs.
When importing goods into the Czech Republic, the weighing of vehicles was carried out directly by the customs administration of the Czech Republic.
When importing goods into the SR, the weighing vehicles were carried out by the personnel of the authorized legal person.
The vehicles were registered in computer records after consideration.

5. Control of imports and exports of goods and services within the control of selected financial or tax authorities
5.1. Control sample
In order to verify the fulfilment of the obligations of tax entities in the import and export of goods and services and to evaluate the level of cooperation between the financial and customs authorities, the files of tax entities inspected by the tax authorities have been selected according to the following criteria:
1. tax entities were selected from the customs databases of the Czech Republic and The Czech Republic: a) with the highest volume of imports, b) with the highest amount of VAT assessed, c) with the highest volume of exports,
2. tax entities have been selected from the register of financial or tax authorities according to the above: a) the vat deductions applied on import, b) the excessive VAT deductions applied, c) the right to repayment of the SpD, d) the vat exemption applied on export,
3. tax entities for which tax control has been carried out.
Sampling was carried out regardless of the country of destination with a focus on risky commodities.

5.2.1. Checking the selected sample at tax authorities
The SAO focused in particular on the audited tax offices on:
- the procedure for the tax authorities to verify the correctness of the VAT declared,
- cooperation between the tax authorities and the customs administration,
- comparison of data from the customs database with the JCD database at the tax offices, focusing on the comparison of the declared value, the application of the correct rate of VAT following the customs classification of goods or services, or comparison of jcd data and attached invoices with data in the customs database,
- a comparison of data from VAT returns on transactions carried out and received from abroad with data in the JCD database at tax offices or in the customs database,
- the method of verifying the right to VAT exemption on the export of goods or services abroad,
- a comparison of the volume of exports of goods or services provided declared in VAT returns with data from the customs database.
The JCD database at the tax authorities contained only records of those imports and exports which were obliged to include imports or exports to the tax return.
The audited tax authorities examined the files of tax entities which reported imports totalling CZK 60 396 379 in VAT returns in 2002 and 2003. czk 12,644,052 thousand and the corresponding VAT totalling CZK 12,644,052, Czk.
Furthermore, the files of tax entities reporting in tax returns for the years 2002 and 2003 were checked with exports totalling CZK 47 323,111 000. Czk.
According to the Czech Customs Database, tax entities for which imports and exports between the Czech Republic and The Czech Republic were examined made imports to the Czech Republic from the Czech Republic with a total VAT base of CZK of CZK of CZK 3,759,352,000.
