The differences found between the records in the JCD database at the tax offices and in the Customs Database of the Czech Republic were examined as follows:
- jcd items, which were missing from the customs database of the Czech Republic, were requested directly from the General Directorate of Customs of the Czech Republic,
- for JCD items that were missing from the tax authorities database, it has been verified that the documents are not cancelled,
- for JCD items for which different values have been found between the Customs Database of the Czech Republic and the database of tax authorities, the relevant JCD was requested in writing, including attached invoices, at the General Directorate of Customs of the Czech Republic.
The examination found that the JCD database at the tax authorities did not contain, for example, records of import JCDs with a total VAT value of CZK 3 622 000. czk and records of export JCDs with a total statistical value of CZK 9,359 thousand. Czk.
5.2.1.1. Differences found
By comparing the JCD database at tax offices and the accumulated tax liability for 2002 and 2003 in the VAT returns for the selected sample of tax entities, the following differences were found:
Differences in values were mainly caused by:
- The time shift between the implementation of imports and the exercise of the right to deduct VAT measured on imports of goods.
The tax entity was able to claim the deduction of the tax on the importation of goods within 3 years of the end of the tax year in which the goods were placed under the procedure in question or, in the case of the temporary importation procedure, no later than 3 years after the end of the tax year in which the scheme was terminated.
- The time shift between the implementation of the export and the moment when the tax entity received the JCD.
The tax entity was obliged to provide data on the export carried out exempt from the obligation to apply the output tax to the VAT return first for the tax year in which the goods exited the country, if it also had a tax document, which was the JCD.
- Failure to fulfil the obligations of tax entities in the reporting of imports and exports in VAT returns.
In some cases, tax entities did not include the correct import and export information in their VAT returns.
Since the tax entities did not have to attach JCD lists to the VAT declarations filed, it was difficult to check the right to deduct VAT or the exemption from VAT by the tax authorities.
5.2.2. Synergies between financial and customs authorities
During the period audited, import or export duties and VAT were refunded or remission by the customs authorities.
Tax entities were obliged by law to reduce the previously claimed right to deduct VAT by the amount of tax returned by the customs office in the tax return for the period in which the tax was refunded.
No legislation provided for the sending of information on changes in the amount of customs duties and VAT from customs offices to the tax authorities.
Some audited tax authorities received this information, but irregularly or with considerable time delays and only from certain customs offices.
One audited tax authority did not receive this information at all.
If the tax office did not receive information on changes in the amount of customs duties and VAT directly from the customs office, it did not have the data necessary to check the fulfilment of the legal obligation of the tax entities.
In 2002, the customs authorities returned VAT in an amount of more than EUR 319 million. in 2003 in the amount of over CZK 398 million. Czk.
The results of the audit pointed to persistent shortcomings in the activities of tax authorities, some systemic errors in the cooperation of the tax authorities with customs authorities and the non-fulfilment of certain obligations of payers submitting VAT returns and spd.
In the management of VAT and the SpD, weaknesses were identified in particular in the following areas:
(a) when vat registrations are revoked, compliance with the obligation of the payers to pay VAT on the business assets registered or which was to be registered on the date of the deregistration of the registration with which the payer applied the deduction was verified only occasionally,
(b) the tax authorities have consistently failed to make use of the possibility of carrying out tax checks or local investigations.
This in some cases resulted in insufficient verification of the eligibility of the right to deduct VAT,
c) the official records and oral hearing logs did not contain all the necessary data to demonstrate the legitimacy of the excessive VAT deductions applied,
(d) the tax authorities have not sufficiently verified the imports and exports declared in the VAT returns.
5.3. Control findings in the SR
5.3.1. Checking the selected sample at tax offices
For a selected sample of SAO SR verified or carried out a tax audit for the tax year 2002 and 2003.
After analysing the tax returns and refund requests submitted to the selected tax entities of the SAO SR, the tax office requested the provision of the relevant JCD proving imports and exports, invoices and proof of payment of tax.
Subsequently, the SAO SR checked whether the JCDs submitted were registered in the customs database of imports and exports and the fulfilment of the decisive facts and statutory conditions when applying the deduction of input tax on imports, on the refund of the excess VAT deduction, in the application of the exemption from export duty and when the SpD was refunded.
The SAO SR verified at 10 audited tax offices selected cases of imports and exports of goods between the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic in the structure according to the honor of jcd items and the sum of statistical values shown in the following table.
In total, imports were checked at a statistical value of EUR 856,2 million. Sk, which represents 5.11% of the total value of imports of selected commodities from the Czech Republic to the CFR.
Exports of selected commodities were checked for a total statistical value of EUR 176 million. Sk, which represents 6.87% of the total value of exports of selected commodities from the Slovak Republic to the Czech Republic.
Furthermore, 618 cases of imports of other goods and services (mainly white equipment, packaging techniques and software) from EU countries to the SR were checked for a total statistical value of EUR 532.8 million. Group.
5.3.2. Synergies between tax and customs authorities
The SAO SR checked the tax offices to find discrepancies between the data recorded in the Customs Database of the Czech Republic and the data reported in specific VAT returns, e.g.:
- 2 tax entities (natural persons) mentioned in the tax returns imports of goods with a total value of 1 589 261 Sk, on the basis of which they claimed the right to recover excessive VAT deductions.
In local investigations carried out at the initiative of the SAO SR, tax entities have failed to demonstrate to the tax authority the legitimacy of the application of input tax by the relevant evidence of the execution of imports and payment of VAT,
- the tax entity (s. r. o.) declared in the tax return for the tax year january 2003 the taxable transaction received in the value of 77 167 576 Sk, the export of goods worth 18 006 041 Sk and applied an excessive deduction of VAT of 17 157 101 Sk.
It is apparent from the VAT returns filed for 2003 that the difference between the volume of purchases and exports of 59 161 535 Sk, which was established in January 2003, was not compensated during the whole of 2003.
In the above cases, the SAO SR asked the competent tax authorities to carry out a tax audit of the excessive VAT deductions applied.
- in another case, the tax entity (s. r. o.) for the tax year January to June 2002 indicated exports of goods with a total value of SK 87 199 in vat returns.
Verification in the customs database of the Slovak Customs Database found that the tax entity carried out exports at a statistical value of 296 747 Sk during that period.
The Tax Office carried out a local investigation at the company's headquarters, finding that the company's executive (UK citizen) had travelled and the company had left the leased premises without terminating the lease in August 2002.
At the time of the inspection of the SAO SR, the tax administrator notified the law enforcement authorities of the suspected non-tax charge of the offence.
On the basis of the results of the audit at the selected tax offices, the SAO SR notes that the biggest problems in the administration and control of VAT and the SpD were mainly in the following areas:
- non-use of the possibility of carrying out vat checks on problematic tax entities, in particular in cases of the application of the high value of excessive VAT deductions,
- the tax audit protocols did not contain an inventory of the documents checked
- JCD on the import and export of goods,
- insufficient screening of the reported import and export of goods in the tax returns,
- lengthy proceedings by tax administrations in issuing decisions, in particular in the context of the assessment procedure, as well as the termination of the right to deduct sanctions,
- non-compliance with the legal conditions in the provision of deferrals of payment of taxes,
- non-compensation of VAT arrears within the time limit for the refund of the excess VAT deduction,
- insufficient use of all forms of security and recovery of tax arrears.
On the basis of the identified deficiencies identified, the SAO SR requested the competent tax authorities to carry out a VAT tax check, focusing on the legitimacy of the excessive VAT deductions applied for 14 tax entities.
Measures have been taken at all audited tax offices to address the identified deficiencies, the fulfilment of which the SAO will monitor and control.
6. Conclusion
International cooperation made it possible to examine trade transactions between trading partners from both Countries and highlighted shortcomings in the registration of imports and exports.
The checks also resulted in the detection of persistent deficiencies in the fulfilment of the obligations of VAT and SpD payers, in the activities of financial and tax authorities, in the system of cooperation and exchange of information between tax and customs authorities, which ultimately reduced the efficiency and efficiency of tax controls.
The findings also showed that the tax authorities in the Czech Republic have basic data on imports and exports from the Customs Database of the Czech Republic within the framework of the tax information system. There is no similar system in the Czech Customs and Customs Administration of information on imports and exports of goods.
The procedure for verifying the enforcement of VAT and SpD administration was not the same due to the different rules and conditions in the territory of the two States.
The SAO verified the necessary data from the information obtained from the customs administration of the Czech Republic and from documents available at the audited tax offices. The SAO SR verified the execution of commercial transactions from documents of tax entities requested through tax authorities.
In the event of irregularities being detected, he asked the tax authorities to carry out tax checks.
The parallel controls carried out in the field of VAT and the SpD assessed the state of the administration of these taxes in the period prior to accession to the European Union and pointed out the need for further cooperation in this area.
Mutual cooperation will be further intensified in the control of the activities of financial or tax authorities in connection with the adoption of the new VAT Act.
One of the new obligations related to the supply of goods to other Member States of the European Union is the submission of so-called 'goods'. recapitulative statement.
This report must be submitted by all VAT payers who have made the supply of goods to another Member State to a person registered for VAT in another Member State.
Tax authorities are obliged to enter recapitulative information data into the VAT Information Exchange System (VIES) to which tax authorities from the Member States of the European Union have access.
The tax authorities and tax authorities can then compare these data with the data given in the VAT returns filed.
This system is also used to verify the validity of the VAT registration number of persons registered for VAT, to verify the eligibility of the VAT exemption applied for the supply of goods to another Member State and to check the proper taxation of goods.
The implementation of parallel control actions showed the possibilities of cooperation between the SAO and the SAO SR.
The results of these control actions will be confronted with the outcomes of the forthcoming control actions, which will focus, inter alia, on the verification of the VIES system, which is intended to prevent tax evasion in the so-called "tax authorities". 'intra-Community supplies'.
Given the importance of VAT and the SpD for budgetary revenues, control activities need to focus primarily on monitoring and identifying risk areas in order to reduce the scope for tax evasion in indirect taxes.
Communiqué
This report was prepared in Czech, English and Slovak and signed by the Vice-President of the Supreme Audit Office and chairman of the Najvyššie Control Office of the Slovak Republic.
Report on the results of inspections in asylum facilities in the Czech Republic and slovakia
State assets and funds intended to secure the activities of the Refugee Facility Administration of the Ministry of the Interior
Control Action No 04/23 "State assets and funds intended to secure the activities of the Refugee Facility Administration of the Ministry of the Interior"
Control Action No. 15/2004 "Control of the economy with the assets of the sting and financial prostrieds intended for the rationing of asylum and temporary shelter cudzincom in the SR"
1. Introduction
Population migration is one of the phenomena that are of a global character and have become an inseparable part of the current development stages of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic.
Its cause is, in particular, the escape of citizens from their country of origin or last residence from persecution, in particular on grounds of racial, religious, national, political, as well as the consequences of military conflicts and ethnic cleansing.
Their aim is to gain asylum and integrate into society, especially in one of Europe's advanced democratic countries.
A large group is also made up of foreigners, whose reason for migration is unfavourable economic and living conditions.
Migration is not a new phenomenon.
The adoption of the 1951 Geneva Agreement and the 1967 New York Protocol on the legal status of refugees, whose acceptance by the governments of the signatory countries had undertaken to apply them in their foreign policy orientation, has already been established.
The Czech and Slovak Federal Republics ratified the New York Protocol in 1991 and the Geneva Agreement in 1992.
After the split in 1993, both the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic declared their position on the refugee issue by continuing to comply with the adopted international documents and confirming their binding nature within the framework of national legislation by a legal act.
Both republics have also enshrined asylum in their constitutional laws.
Parallel checks carried out by the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Najvyšší control office of the Slovak Republic, the results of which include a joint final report, were focused on the asylum process and related issues.
Cooperation between the Supreme Audit Offices of the two countries was carried out on the basis of the 'Cooperation in Control Agreement' ('the Treaty') concluded in April 2004.
In the Treaty, the two Parties undertook to provide each other with information on the legislation governing asylum procedures in the State of the other Contracting Party, selected statistics on the number of asylum seekers and the results of the asylum process, as well as information on asylum facilities.
The aim of the parallel control action was to type the same problem circuits and to highlight the consequences of this for population migration.
The cooperation consisted of the unification of the programme of control actions, the exchange of information to the extent laid down by the Treaty and the preparation of a joint final report on the outcome of the checks.
At the first joint meeting, which took place on 5-4 June 2005, the European Union adopted a report on the european union's role in the 2007-2014 until 7.4.2004, the same areas of controlled issues and control procedures in the preparation of control actions were established.
At the second meeting, which took place on 28 and 28 June 2006, the European Union decided to take the to 30.6. 2004, the common points for the control action programme were specified.
At the third joint meeting, which took place during the control action of 8.11. until 10.11.2004, the experience of ongoing checks was exchanged.
The forms of outputs from the checks have been specified and the structure and content of the joint final report drawn up on 14.2 have been specified. to 17.2. 2005 at the last joint meeting.
The checks were carried out in parallel between September 2004 and January 2005.
In the Czech Republic, the inspection was carried out by inspectors of the Department of Defence and Security and selected territorial departments.
The persons audited were the Ministry of the Interior (hereinafter referred to as the Ministry of the Interior) and the Administration of Refugee Facilities of the Ministry of the Interior (hereinafter referred to as "SUZ").
In the Slovak Republic, it carried out a review of the sectiona of the defence, vnútra and štátnych úradov.
The audited entity was the Migration Office of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs of the Czech Technical Party (hereinafter referred to as the "MÚ").
The period audited was 2001, 2002, 2003 (hereinafter referred to as the audited period).
In some cases, statistical data over a longer period of time are also used in the joint report.
2. Recapitulation of the results of the inspection
2.1. Evaluation of control activities
The subject of parallel checks was: - asylum process, - asylum facilities, - management of funds and state property, - internal control system.
The mutual exchange of experience gained between the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Najvyššší control office of the Slovak Republic took place at the stage of preparation and implementation of control actions.
This exchange made it possible to evaluate the documents submitted more thoroughly, to analyse the causes of the identified differences in the security of the asylum process.
Thus it was possible to focus on the decisive problems affecting the activities of asylum facilities.
In the end, this positively affected the quality of the inspection activity.
2.2 Summary of the results of the inspection
The harmonisation of the asylum law of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic with European Union documents ('the EU') has been the subject of the European Commission's evaluation reports on the readiness of both countries to join the EU.
The adoption of legislation in this area continues after both countries have joined the EU with a view to further harmonisation with EU law.
The number of asylum seekers in the Czech Republic increased significantly in 2001.
In the Slovak Republic, the number of applicants has a continuously increasing trend, with a significant increase in applicants in 2001.
The Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic provide financial and material security to asylum seekers within the meaning of international agreements.
The state budget of both countries allocates the necessary funds for this purpose.
The amount of expenditure drawn from the state budget of both countries is mainly affected by the number of applicants, the duration of the asylum procedure until the granting or non-granting of asylum, as well as the state of health of the applicants.
The amount of some of the benefits collected is comparable in both countries.
The Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic set up asylum facilities in which they gradually created suitable conditions for the stay of the participants in the granting of asylum proceedings.
In asylum facilities, accommodation, meals, health care and basic material equipment and hygiene supplies are provided to asylum seekers during their stay.
At the same time, courses are organized within the leisure activities and applicants are created conditions for cultural and sports activities.
Asylum facilities include reception centres and residential centres, in the Czech Republic as well as integration centres.
The cost of one stay day depends on the occupancy and amenities of the resort and is comparable in both countries.
In the Czech Republic, the capacity of asylum facilities is essentially stabilised.
In the Slovak Republic, it is expected to increase by almost 1,000 places in the next two years.
The aim is to create conditions for applicants, the increasing number of which are expected to continue in the coming years in the context of the application of the Dublin Convention.
In the Czech Republic, the highest part of the approved budget expenditure was spent on the security of services. The decisive expenditure of this item was the expenditure on accommodation and catering of applicants in asylum facilities operated under contract, the cost of healthcare provided to asylum seekers and the cost of a permanent security service ensuring the protection of asylum facilities.
Expenditure on salaries, payments for work carried out and insurance premiums also accounted for a significant extent in total expenditure.
In the Slovak Republic, the budgetary management of the migration policy and the asylum process has been marked by many budgetary measures that addressed legitimate requirements related to the increase in the number of asylum seekers.
Expenditure on wages, salaries and insurance premiums, expenditure on materials and services and expenditure on security services were decisively involved in the utilisation of current expenditure.
The results of the inspection in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic highlighted some similar shortcomings that did not have a major impact on the financial management and management of the state's assets.
These were shortcomings, in particular, in the area of the use of state budget funds, contrary to the purpose for which they were determined by the State Budget Act, when actions with the technical appreciation of tangible fixed assets were covered by current expenditure.
The accounting law in the field of inventory and non-compliance with the chart of accounts was also violated.
Furthermore, minor deficiencies in the management of the state's property were found in the Czech Republic when it was transferred to another person without a contract.
Failure to report changes in the land register data violated the Land Register Act and the transfer of waste for disposal to a person who was not a person authorised to dispose of the waste was violated.
Furthermore, deficiencies in the granting of excessively high advances for the collection of electricity and natural gas, deficiencies in the procurement and management of state property were found in the Slovak Republic when its records were not sufficiently secured and the method of disposal of unnecessary assets was not established.
The internal control system has been ensured in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic within the meaning of the applicable generally binding legislation governing the way financial control is carried out.
No deficiencies were identified in the written documentation submitted.
Despite some of the shortcomings identified, the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Najvyšší control office of the Slovak Republic positively assess the suz and the IO's progress in the provision of services for asylum seekers.
Building on the lessons learned during the inspection, the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Najvyšší Control Office of the Slovak Republic note that despite the significant increase in the number of asylum seekers in recent years, the relevant organisational units of both countries have managed the tasks related to the care of asylum seekers at an appropriate level.
The evaluation indicates that the system is functional and stable.
The results of the inspection were discussed with interested statutory representatives of the relevant organizational units of the state on the Czech and Slovak sides.
Based on the results of the inspection, we recommend that the positive methodological experience of the inspection be used in other joint control actions within the framework of the international cooperation of the SAIs.
3. Legislative framework
In both the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, asylum law is based on the 1951 Geneva Convention (Convention on the Status of Refugees and the 1967 New York Protocol).
The first legislation was implemented by Act No. 498/1990 Coll., on Refugees.
In the Czech Republic, from 1 January 2005, the 1. 2000 effective Act No. 325/1999 Coll., on Asylum and amending Act No. 83/1991 Coll., on the Police of the Czech Republic.
This Act has been amended five times (Act No. 2/2002 Coll., Act No. 217/2002 Coll., Act No. 320/2002 Coll., Act No. 519/2002 Coll. and Act No. 222/2003 Coll.).
There are currently two other amendments to Act No. 325/1999 Coll., on Asylum, and the adoption of further amendments will be linked to European legislation.
At the time of the creation of Act No. 325/1999 Coll., on asylum, the area of asylum was part of the 3rd Amendment. and asylum documents were political documents in terms of binding nature.
Already in the framework of the adoption of this law, it was an effort to make it as compatible as possible with EU law.
A significant change for asylum policy within the EU was the transfer of asylum from 3. until 1 January 2005. the right of asylum has become part of Community law since 1.5. 1999 under the Treaty of Amsterdam.
This shift has created the need to create adequate legislation, i.e. to create adequate legislation. to develop legal instruments in appropriate legal commitment.
The compatibility of Czech asylum law with EU documents has been the subject of regular evaluation reports from the European Commission.
Key Community rules in the field of asylum were adopted shortly before or after the Czech Republic's accession to the EU and their transposition period at the time of the inspection of the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic has not yet expired.
Once they have been implemented into the Czech legal order, the Czech Republic will be obliged to notify the European Commission of the transposition.
In the Slovak Republic, the procedure for granting refugee status and determining the obligations of foreigners who have applied for refugee status or who have been granted temporary shelter in the Territory of the Slovak Republic has been established with effect from 1.1.1996 by the Law of the National Council of the Slovak Republic No. 283/1995 Z. z., on refugees.
Since 2003, the Law on Refugees has been replaced by Law No 480/2002 Z. z" on asylum and on the amendment and addition of certain laws, which incorporated the harmonisation of the legislation of the Slovak Republic with council of Europe Directive 2001/55/EC of 20 June 2001. 7. 2001 on minimum standards for the provision of temporary protection in the event of a mass influx of displaced persons and on measures to promote the balance of effort between Member States in the reception of such persons and the resulting consequences.
Following two amendments to Act No 480/2002 Z z., on asylum, in 2003 and 2004, a third amendment was approved at the beginning of 2005, which means further harmonisation of the law of the Slovak Republic with EU legislation on migration and asylum.
Its important elements are, for example, the establishment of an obligation for asylum seekers to attend a course on the basis of slovak language during their stay in the integration centre, the appointment of a guardian by the courts for minors, if they are staying in the territory of the Slovak Republic without a legal representative, allowing applicants to enter into an employment relationship in certain circumstances, as set out in the amendment to the Law.
The harmonisation of Slovak law with EU law in the field of migration and the asylum process was evaluated in regular reports by the European Commission on the readiness to join the EU.
In 2002, the report highlighted the lack of staffing capacity of the IOC, which did not correspond to the increased number of asylum seekers.
4. Asylum process
In the Czech Republic, since 1990, matters relating to refugees have been covered by the MV.
With effect from 1 January 2005, the 1. 1996, the MV established an organisational unit of the State of SUZ. The reason was the separation of the administration's performance in the area of the asylum procedure, which is carried out through the Department of Asylum and Migration Policy of the Ministry of Asylum, from the provision of services to asylum seekers.
The task of the SUZ is to provide accommodation, catering, health and other services for the MV to the parties to the granting of asylum proceedings and asylum seekers.
In the Slovak Republic, it performs decisive tasks in the field of the IOC asylum process, in particular from the point of view of the financial and material-technical security of the asylum process to the extent defined by specific rules.
Priority tasks are issues related to the decision-making of applications for asylum granted to foreigners in the first stage of the administrative procedure and the comprehensive operation of asylum facilities in the areas of accommodation, catering, health, financial and material security of asylum seekers.
In addition, it is preparing a concept for the migration policy of the state.
The results achieved in the development of the asylum system in the Slovak Republic in recent years have significantly influenced cooperation and support from the Office of the United Nations High Commissioner for Refugees (UNHCR).
His financial contribution to the reconstruction of the housing fund for asylum seekers was a particular contribution.
The UNHCR also co-financed social, cultural and sports activities for applicants.
4.1 Development of the number of asylum seekers and results of the asylum process
The evolution of the number of asylum seekers in the Czech Republic is shown in the graph.
There was a significant increase in 2001 due to the Kosovo crisis, and in 2003 there was an increase in the number of refugees from Chechnya.
An overview of the results of asylum procedures in the Czech Republic is given in Table 1.
A total of 394 cases were granted asylum during the audited period, including 83 in 2001, 103 in 2002 and 208 in 2003.
In the audited period, a total of 22,731 cases were not granted asylum and in 22 636 cases the asylum procedure was stopped.
Number of parties to 1.1. includes both persons to whom no decision has yet been taken and those to whom the decision has not been transmitted.
It also includes persons who have been excused to miss the time limit for lodging an appeal or who have had the previous decision annulled and have not yet been issued a new one.
In the Slovak Republic, the number of asylum seekers is on a steadily increasing trend.
If 96 applicants were registered in 1993, in 2003 it was already 10 358.
There was a significant increase in the number of applicants in 2001, when 8 131 applicants were registered, an increase of 423% compared to 2000, in which 1,556 people applied for asylum.
Data on the results of asylum procedures in the Slovak Republic during the audited period are given in Table 2.
A total of 49 asylums were granted in the audited period and the number did not exceed 0.22% of the registered number of applicants in each year.
Asylum was not granted in 860 cases.
The asylum procedure was stopped in a total of 23,088 cases.
By staying outside the asylum facility without authorisation, the majority of applicants voluntarily left the asylum procedure before it was closed.
In 2002, it was more than 82% of the total number of registered applicants and more than 94% in 2003.
The length of stay of one applicant in one of the asylum facilities, converted into an average number of days, was 13 days in 2001, 18 days in 2002 and 19 days in 2003.
The findings of the Ministry of Y MÚ also show that for the majority of applicants entering the asylum process in the Slovak Republic, it is about finding better living conditions, i.e. the so-called 'asylum process'. economic migration, which does not have a foothold in documents adopted by the international community, to which the Slovak Republic has also signed up.
In these cases, the asylum system is used by the applicant for purpose.
An application for asylum based on economic reasons, such as finding employment or better living conditions, is not a reason to grant asylum.
Such a request should be made in accordance with the provisions of § 12 ods. Article 1(1)(b) (a) Act No 480/2002 Z. z., on asylum, is assessed as manifestly unfounded and should be decided within 30 days.
Internationally recognised principles have not yet been established to identify economic migrants, distinguishing them from those persecuted in the country of origin and allowing the asylum process to be accelerated.
In view of these facts, it can be concluded that the Slovak Republic is a transit country in terms of international migration and western European countries have been and remain the target countries of migration.
After accession to the EU, the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic acceded to the Agreement determining the State responsible for examining asylum applications lodged in one of the Member States of the European Communities (Dublin Convention).
The Convention prevents multiple special purpose applications for asylum in multiple EU countries from being submitted.
Applicants return to the country of first registration after positive identification in EURODAC.
The Slovak Republic is part of the outdoor border of EU countries, so the application of the Dublin Convention may result in an increase in the number of applicants who will need to create conditions for residence in the Slovak Republic until a decision on granting or not granting asylum is granted.
4.2 Withdrawal of funds
The Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic are obliged to provide financial and material security to asylum seekers within the meaning of international agreements and the national legislation based there.
The state budget of both countries allocates the necessary funds for this purpose.
The amount of expenditure drawn from the state budget is mainly affected by the number of applicants, the duration of the asylum procedure until the final decision on granting asylum and also their state of health.
The increasing number of people entering the asylum process has a direct impact on the higher absorption of statutory benefits for applicants, such as food expenditure, pocket money, expenditure on basic material equipment, other material equipment and other social contributions.
The amount of some of the benefits collected is comparable in both countries.
In the Czech Republic, in the controlled period, the subsistence allowance was CZK 58 per person per day, pocket money czk 12 per person per day and CZK 6 per child up to 15 years of age.
The cost per asylum seeker per stay day was on average CZK 351 in 2001, CZK 383 in 2002 and CZK 345 in 2003.
In addition to pocket money, asylum seekers staying in residential centres with independent cooking and applicants staying in private outside the asylum facilities may be granted a contribution up to the minimum living wage.
Law No. 325/1999 Coll., on Asylum, as amended, grants, inter alia, in § 84 to municipalities the right to a contribution to cover the costs incurred in connection with the asylum facility in its territory.
The amount of the contribution was determined annually by government resolutions and in the audited period it was CZK 7 per person per stay day.
At the same time, municipalities are granted a contribution to cover the non-investment costs of primary schools frequented by asylum seekers.
The amount of the allowance was CZK 120 per pupil per month in the controlled period, provided that in a given month the person attended the school for at least 10 days.
In the Slovak Republic, in the controlled period there was a meal allowance of 70 Sk per person per day, pocket money 12 Sk per person per day and 8 Sk per child up to 15 years of age.
The cost per asylum seeker per stay day was on average 442 Sk in 2001, 447 Sk in 2002 and 445 Sk in 2003.
In accordance with Act No 480/2002 Z. z., the municipalities in whose territory the asylum facility is located is granted a contribution for the partial reimbursement of the costs incurred by the municipality in connection with the establishment and activities of the asylum facility.
So far, municipalities have only partially used the possibility to apply for a contribution, which is set at SK1 500 per bed per calendar year.
National legislation in both countries for issuing an asylum decision sets a 90-day period from the start of the asylum procedure and at the same time allows, in justified cases, an extension of that period.
The most common reason for the extension of the asylum procedure, which affects the amount of expenditure of the state budget, is to appeal against the decision not to grant asylum.
In the Czech Republic, the highest number of final decisions was issued between 90 and 180 days (31.54%).
The second highest number was within 90 days of the date of application for asylum (17.61%).
In total, 73% of asylum procedures launched in 2001-2003 were finalised within one year of their initiation.
Within two years of the start of the asylum procedure, 92% of asylum applications were finalised.
In the Slovak Republic, according to the data of the IOC, up to 90% of applicants who have not been granted asylum use the legal option of extending the time limit by bringing an appeal to court.
In some cases, it was an extension of more than a year and the proceedings were not closed in court at the time of the inspection.
Some benefit in shortening the asylum procedure is expected from the establishment of joint offices of the Ministry of Parties and the Úradahraničnej and Cudzineckej polecie Policajného zboru in reception centres in Adamov-Gbeloch, Opatovskej Novej Vesi and in Liptovský Vlachoch, which was carried out during the period of inspection since 1.10.2004.
This envisages simplifying procedures and reducing the time limits between the two components of the asylum process.
5. Asylum facilities
The Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic set up asylum facilities in which they gradually created appropriate conditions for the provision of services to the parties to the granting of asylum proceedings.
In asylum facilities, accommodation, meals, healthcare, pocket money and basic material equipment and hygiene supplies are provided to asylum seekers during their stay.
At the same time, courses are organized in the context of leisure activities and conditions are created for cultural and sports activities.
5.1 Asylum facilities in the Czech Republic
SUZ manages and operates asylum facilities and is responsible for managing the state's assets in the premises of the Vyšní Lhota reception centre, the reception and residence centre Červený Újezd, the residential centres Bělá-Jezová, Zastávka u Brna, Kostelec nad Orlicí, Havířov and the premises of the integration asylum centres Jaroměř and Zastávka u Brna.
At the beginning of 2002, a reception centre was set up in the transit area of Prague-Ruzyně Airport.
SUZ also provides the operation of asylum facilities in Stráž pod Ralskem, Seč, Bruntále, Zbýšov and Kašava, which are operated by a legal person on the basis of § 80 para. 3 of Act No. 325/1999 Coll., on Asylum.
The total accommodation capacity of reception centres is 747 seats and the total accommodation capacity of the residential centres is 1,977 seats.
Reception centres are closed facilities, which asylum seekers may not leave until the prescribed medical examinations and basic admissions operations referred to in Act No. 325/1999 Coll., on asylum.
A violation of the obligation to stay in the receiving centre is assessed as a misdemeanor.
The residential centres where asylum seekers come from reception centres are used to accommodate asylum seekers until the decision on their application for asylum is taken into force.
Under certain conditions, asylum seekers have the possibility to leave the residence centres or to leave the centres. to stay in private.
Asylum seekers shall have the right to free accommodation, food, other services and allowances in reception and residence centres where they are reported to stay, provided that they have endured the acts necessary to establish their financial and property conditions, and these ratios are such that they cannot be fairly requested or partially paid for those services.
Integration asylum centres are used for temporary accommodation of persons who have been granted asylum.
Clients are accommodated in the centre on the basis of an accommodation contract, which is usually concluded for 6 months with the possibility of an extension until they manage to secure adequate housing for them, or they will secure it themselves within the framework of the state integration program.
In the integration centre, clients pay all the costs of accommodation and eat individually.
Persons granted refugee status have the same rights and obligations as Czech citizens and have the same access to social security.
5.1.1. Costs of asylum facilities
For comparison, asylum facilities were chosen as the best telling indicator of the cost per physical stay day.
It is based on the de facto number of persons who have actually been provided with services provided by an asylum facility on a daily record.
In Table 3 and in the graph, the facilities operated by SUZ are designated as own and facilities operated by legal entities pursuant to Section 80 of Act No. 325/1999 Coll., on Asylum, as contractual.
The cost of one stay day in its own asylum facility operated by SUZ is falling as the fulfilment of these facilities increases. This is because the fixed cost of running the premises is calculated into more asylum seekers.
The total cost of providing services for asylum seekers is increasing directly in proportion to the increasing number.
In 2001 and 2003, there were accommodation for applicants in crisis capacity in their own asylum facilities.
In part of 2003, extraordinary accommodation capacity in residential containers (320 beds in total) was even used to address the capacitive crisis of asylum facilities caused by the mass arrival of Asylum seekers of Chechen nationality from Poland.
This capacity was provided by renting 80 residential and 6 sanitary containers.
The expenditure per applicant per per stay day was then lower in those years.
However, it is not possible to maintain a long-term high filling of these devices.
Account should be taken of the risks of an unexpected influx of refugees and the associated requirement for the need for higher accommodation capacity.
At the same time, it is not possible to carry out some repairs, maintenance and investments at fully occupied accommodation capacity.
The form of asylum facilities operated by contract allows the adoption of operational solutions in the capacity of asylum facilities, if necessary.
5.2 Asylum facilities in the Slovak Republic
Asylum facilities are reception centres and residential centres.
The Ministry of Reception has adamov-gbely, rohovce, Opatovská Nová Ves and the residential centre Brezová pod Bradlom in its administration.
The total capacity of reception centres is 470 seats and the residential center 100 seats.
The growing number of asylum seekers was dealt with by the Ministry of 100 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 00
According to the concluded contract, the lease also provides the provision of services related to the operation of the centre.
In this form, the Ministry of 150 000 addressed the lack of its own staff.
The residential centre was also temporarily established in 2002 and 2003 in rented premises in Jazierciach with a capacity of 160 seats.
Reception centres had occupancy rate of between 57% and 62% in the controlled period, on average from 33% to 50% in residential centres.
Occupancy changed by the time of year and was the highest in the last months of the year when it applied for asylum for a much larger number of applicants compared to other months of the year.
Further increase of accommodation capacity by about 450 seats will be possible after reconstruction of resorts in Opatovskej Novej Vesi and Vlachoch.
After the completion of the centre in Humennom in 2006, the number of seats will increase by an additional 550 people.
5.2.1. Costs of asylum facilities
Data on the amount of the costs of operating the asylum facilities are given in Table 4.
Their analysis shows that the operation of an asylum facility by another body providing premises and ensuring the operation of the facilities, including the related activities, is one way to secure, at reasonable costs, the tasks resulting from the residence of asylum seekers in the Slovak Republic.
6. Management of funds and property of the State
6.1 Analysis of economics
In the Czech Republic, in 2001, suz's approved budgeted expenditure was increased by 13 budget measures by 103 077 ths. Czk.
Of which 89 979 ths. Czk (87.29%) are earmarked appropriations. The bulk was intended to deal with the consequences of the Kosovo crisis (44 538,000. and the provision of healthcare provided to asylum seekers (CZK 38,870,000) (czk 100,
In 2002, SUZ expenditure was increased by 20 budgetary measures by 88 362 ths. Czk.
Of which 62,282,000 were 100,000. (70.48%) were earmarked appropriations, of which the bulk (53 200 ths) czk) was intended for healthcare provided to asylum seekers.
In 2003, SUZ expenditure was increased by 14 budgetary measures by a total of 88 078 ths. Czk.
Of which 82 000 ths. Czk (93.09%) the purpose-built funds released from the General Treasury Administration.
Amount 51 000 ths. Czk 24,000 was intended for healthcare provided to asylum seekers. czk to deal with the influx of Chechen refugees and CZK 7,000,000 Czk for the humanitarian evacuation programme of disabled residents of the Republic of Iraq.
An overview of the drawdown of selected SUZ expenditure in the audited period is given in Table 5.
It is clear from the above overview that the highest proportion of expenditure was spent on the provision of services.
The amount of expenditure incurred to purchase services ranged from 37.07% to 38.23% of total expenditure.
The heated expenditure under this heading was the costs of accommodation and catering for applicants in asylum facilities operated under contract, the cost of medical treatment provided to asylum seekers and the cost of a permanent security service providing security at individual asylum facilities.
Suz's total expenditure accounted for salaries, work and insurance premiums (23.99% - 24.97%).
Last but not least, purchases of material (approximately 14%) accounted for the total expenditure of SUZ, with the highest share of such expenditure was food purchases (7.61% ? 9.83% of total expenditure).
In the Slovak Republic, the MÚ's budgetary management for securing the migration policy and the asylum process was marked by more budgetary measures to address legitimate requirements related to the increase in the number of asylum seekers.
In particular, the draft and breakdown of the budget in the expenditure part was characterised, in particular, in 2001 and 2002, by an imbalance between the requirements of the IA, which were based on an increase in the number of asylum seekers and the financing needs of their legal entitlements, and the resources provided, in particular in the main category of current expenditure.
The administrator of the budget chapter dealt with the disproportion during the year with several budgetary measures, which increased the limit of current expenditure in 2001 by 41,8 % and in 2002 by up to 71,7 %.
An overview of the use of selected expenditure by the Ministry of 30 June 2005 in the audited period is given in Table 6.
Expenditure on wages, salaries and insurance premiums ranging from 24.47% to 30.51% and material and service expenditure ranged from 21.04% to 38.82% of total expenditure.
More than 10% were spending on security services and from 3.92% to 7.20% of food purchases.
Spending on accommodation and catering services was another significant part of the share from 10.82% to 26.96%.
A relatively low share in the range of 1.03% to 6.25% was capital expenditure.
6.2 Identified deficiencies
The results of the inspection in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic pointed to some similar deficiencies which did not have a major impact on the management of the state's funds and assets.
These were shortcomings, in particular in the following areas: (a) the use of state budget funds contrary to the purpose for which they were intended by the State Budget Act when actions bearing the technical appreciation of tangible fixed assets were covered by current expenditure; b) violation of the Accounting Act in the field of inventory and non-compliance with the indicative chart of accounts.
Furthermore, minor deficiencies in the management of the state's property were found in the Czech Republic, when it was left for use by another person without a proper contract; failure to comply with the deadline for reporting changes to the land register data has violated the Land Registry Act; the waste law has been violated by the transfer of waste for disposal to a person who was not the person authorised to dispose of the waste.
Furthermore, deficiencies were found in the Slovak Republic in the provision of excessively high advances for the collection of electricity and natural gas, deficiencies in the procurement and management of the State's assets when its records were not sufficiently secured and the method of disposal of unnecessary assets was not demonstrated.
7. Internal control system
In the Czech Republic, suz was at 1.7. 2002 introduced an internal control system within the meaning of the provisions of Act No. 320/2001 Coll., on financial control, determining the competences of individual employees responsible for carrying out preliminary, interim and follow-up checks.
At the same time, an internal audit system was established and an internal auditor of the SUZ was appointed.
Every year, the SUZ is issued a plan of financial, socially and operationally technical controls aimed at comprehensive verification of the management of funds and state assets in individual asylum facilities managed by the SUZ.
In 2002, 42 management controls were carried out and 54 were carried out in 2003.
In the Slovak Republic, the direct exercise of control activities in the departments and organizations of the Ministry of the Interior of the Slovak Republic in terms of compliance with generally binding legislation and internal regulations is ensured by the Office of the Minister's control.
Within the period audited, the implementation of the tasks in the asylum policy section was not carried out.
The internal control system of the Ministry of Cul is mainly aimed at carrying out preliminary and continuous financial control under Act No. 502/2001 Z. z., on financial control and audit.
The exercise of financial control is also governed by the internal regulations of the Director of the Ministry of Parties.
The substantive focus of the control activity as part of the management of the various departments was established in the framework of the annual plan of the Ministry of 100000.
The directors of the trade unions were responsible for carrying out the control in this area.
According to the written documentation submitted, no deficiencies were found.
Since the end of the regulation of the Ministry of the Interior of the Slovak Republic No. 28 of 23. 4. 2004, the MÚ is obliged to handle and investigate complaints under the Complaints Act.
In the next period, you will need to resolve the organizational security of this task.
Communiqué
This report was prepared in Czech, English and Slovak and signed by the Vice-President of the Supreme Audit Office and chairman of the Najvyššie Control Office of the Slovak Republic.
Joint report on parallel controls on expenditure on the construction of the Prague – Dresden motorway
Introductory word
Without the existence of trans-European transport networks, a modern, dynamic and, above all, a united Europe would hardly be imaginable.
High-quality transport networks are a prerequisite for maintaining and raising the standard of living for Europeans.
Creating conditions for fast, safe, reliable and inexpensive transport of persons and cargo is an important task for the state administration.
It is a very demanding task both in organizational and technical terms and in financial terms.
European efforts for sustainable mobility often and hard to find compromises with Europe's interest in maintaining a healthy and human-friendly environment.
Construction of transport infrastructure, thanks to the necessary measures for the benefit of the environment, constructions are financially demanding.
The government's considered procedures and decisions in the preparation and acquisition of transport works can bring significant savings in public financial resources that can be used differently for the benefit of citizens.
One of the tasks of the audit institutions is to actively identify weaknesses that have led to less than achievable cost-effectiveness, efficiency and effectiveness of expenditure on transport infrastructure construction.
Control institutions should not only draw the attention of the government to the shortcomings identified, but recommend measures that will improve the situation, for the benefit of citizens, for the benefit of Europe.
Short summary
In 2005 and 2006, the two supreme audit institutions of the Federal Republic of Germany and the Czech Republic (germany and the Czech Republic) the Bundesrechnungshof (hereinafter referred to as "BRH") and the Supreme Audit Office (hereinafter referred to as "SAO") carried out parallel checks on expenditure on the construction of the Prague – Dresden motorway (highway D 8 in the Czech Republic and the A17 motorway in Germany).
The motorways are connected by a border bridge co-financed by the two countries.
Thanks to cooperation with the SAO, BRH was able to carry out a thorough inspection of the effectiveness of the funds spent on the construction of the border bridge.
On the basis of close cooperation with BRH, the SAO obtained the necessary data on the amount of German costs for bridges and tunnels for comparative purposes.
In 2000, the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany concluded a contract for the construction of a border bridge.
According to the construction procedure, the completion date was finally scheduled for the end of 2006.
However, during the award of the contract, the Directorate of Roads and Motorways of the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the "ŘSD") made errors which led to an extension of the competition period and a reduction in the time for construction.
The contract with the contractor was thus signed later than expected.
The contractor agreed to build the bridge in less time and ensure its completion in 2006.
As a result, however, the ŘSD had to accept a significant increase in the price of the bridge.
In the framework of the joint control work, the prices of bridges on motorways D 8 and A 17 were compared, on the basis of the conversion into m2 of the area of the bridge structure.
Statistical analysis of prices made it possible to identify bridges with high cost per m2 area.
Analysis revealed that the border bridge was the most expensive bridge in a group of large bridges over 100 metres long.
The price increase could also be attributed to the delay that occurred during the procurement procedure.
When analysing the costs of building tunnels, the inspectors found that the prices of tunnels on the D 8 motorway were significantly higher than those of comparable tunnels in Germany.
BRH and the SAO now have a database of bridge and tunnel prices that they will be able to rely on in future efficiency checks on the means used for transport infrastructure purposes.
For the construction of bridges, both control institutions recommend: standardization of bridge constructions and the use of composite steel-concrete and special structures only in cases where prestressed reinforced concrete bridges are not adequate.
One of the main features of the collaboration was her team spirit and informality.
During the parallel inspection, the inspectors participated in their specific knowledge and skills.
Introduction
This report informs about the progress and results of parallel checks on the funds spent on the construction of the motorway connecting Dresden and Prague (D 8 in the Czech Republic and A 17 in Germany).
The controls focused on the cost-effectiveness, efficiency and effectiveness of the expenditure incurred.
Parallel checks were carried out by BRH in Germany and the SAO in the Czech Republic.
Parallel checks took place in 2005 and 2006.
The SAO checked the cost-effectiveness, efficiency and effectiveness of expenditure of approximately CZK 20 billion including VAT (approximately €690 million) on the border section of the D 8 motorway, which has the number 0807.
Of this amount, €64 million from European funds (ISPA) was to be used as planned.
In addition to parallel checks carried out together with the SAO, BRH inspected the preparation and construction of the A17 motorway in 2003 and 2005.
The funds spent on the construction of all three sections of the A17 motorway amounted to around €670 million, of which €277 million will be co-financed by European funds (EFRE).
The motorway from Prague to Dresden is part of the trans-European transport corridor IV. Dresden – central and southern part of Eastern Europe – Istanbul.
The D 8 motorway runs from Prague via Ústí nad Labem to the state border.
The A17 motorway runs from the Czech/German national border to Dresden.
At the time of the inspection, border sections of both motorways were under construction.
These sections were put into operation on 21 December 2005. They shall forthwith inform the Council of their information on the
On the German side, the motorway is completed all the way to Dresden, while the Czech side of the D 8 motorway is not completed, because section No. 0805 in the length of 16.4 km through the Czech Central Mountains between Řehlovice and Lovosice is still in the preparatory phase.
According to the plan, section No. 0805 between Prague and Ústí nad Labem is to pass through the protected landscape area of the Czech Central Mountains.
According to forecasts made in the Czech Republic in 2001, in 2008, on the border section no. 0807 of the D 8 motorway, the traffic intensity should be 22,940 vehicles per day.
According to German forecasts, in 2010 the traffic intensity at the Czech border will amount to a total of about 25,000 vehicles per day.
In 2000, Germany and the Czech Republic concluded a Treaty between the Federal Republic of Germany and the Czech Republic on the connection of the German motorway A17 and the Czech highway D 8 to the common state border by the construction of a border bridge.
Both states are involved in the construction of the bridge, so the control of the construction of this bridge was an important aspect of parallel checks carried out by the two control institutions.
Cooperation between BRH and SAO
Since mid-2005, the two supreme audit institutions have negotiated close cooperation in controlling the construction of a motorway connecting Prague and Dresden.
Both parties had serious reasons for such cooperation:
1.
SRN is financially involved in the construction of the border bridge.
Its planning and construction rests on the ŘSD.
Therefore, BRH itself did not have the opportunity to carry out a check on this construction project.
2.
The SAO did not have the comparative database needed to assess whether the funds were used economically as regards the overall level of costs for bridges and tunnels on D 8.
3.
The SAO needed to make sure that the expenditure was effective, taking into account the main technical parameters of the motorway, in particular the arrangement of bridges and tunnels, which should allow for the same quality of driving on both sides of the border.
Following the preparatory negotiations, on 4 December 2005, the Commission decided to consult the European Economic and The agreement on coordinated control of highway D 8/A 17 was signed by the Presidents of the two SAIs.
Joint working meetings between BRH and SAO inspectors took place throughout 2006 at an interval of approximately six to eight weeks.
The negotiations addressed current problems and tasks, in particular the preparation of a uniform methodology for controlling the prices of bridges and tunnels, the exchange of findings from the border bridge construction control and the preparation of joint reports.
An important feature of cooperation was the continuous exchange of information.
While BRH carried out most of the work on comparing the technical parameters of bridges and tunnels and the procurement procedure, the SAO has for the most part prepared a methodology for controlling the prices of bridges and tunnels.
The applicable legal standards for control in the state administration differ in both countries in the way of closing control actions.
For these reasons, the two SAIs have drawn their own control conclusions on their findings obtained during their checks.
This report reflects the results achieved in parallel checks.
Cooperation will end with the signing of the final communiqué in the first half of 2007.
Construction of the border bridge
In the 2000 treaty, the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany agreed on the date of completion of the construction of the border bridge as far as possible in 2005.
The two sides then agreed to postpone this deadline until the end of 2006.
ŘSD was an investor.
SRN is financially involved in the construction of the bridge from 42.13%.
In the period up to 1999, the ŘSD proposed that the border bridge have a pre-stressed reinforced concrete structure.
In 1999, in agreement with its partners in Germany, the ŘSD agreed to a coupled steel-concrete structure.
This decision was justified by a reduction in the number of double pillars from seven to five and the subsequent ecological benefit of such a solution for the valley.
In addition, comparative calculations carried out by the SSD stated that a coupled steel-concrete structure should be a less costly option.
But there was a mistake in the calculations.
It stated that the new coupled steel-concrete structure would be only 397 m long.
In fact, it is 5% longer.
During the award of the contract for the border bridge, the ŘSD made serious errors.
It has not prepared a custom-made dossier which adequately describes the assessment criteria and the sub-criteria for comparing tenders.
This error led to the assessment and evaluation of tenders and the Director-General's assessment of the offers subjectively and problematic.
The unsuccessful tenderer challenged the results of the contract procedure.
A subsequent investigation by the Office for the Protection of Competition resulted in the contract for the award of the construction contract being signed later than originally envisaged.
This meant that the summer construction season 2004, after evaluating the bids, was wasted and the time reserved for construction was reduced.
The construction company agreed to build the bridge in less time, but at the cost of a substantial increase in costs.
The procedure offered included double assembly of the bridge upper, a change in the construction of the pillars and the establishment and equipment of assembly areas.
In addition, the construction company was not able to get the originally proposed type of steel within the necessary deadline.
The new type of steel – at a cost of approximately €4 million, which had to be fully paid by the ŘSD – allowed the time to be carried out of the anti-corrosion protection, which in turn allowed the total construction time of the border bridge to be reduced.
Compared to the net price of €18.3 million offered in the tender, the total cost of building the border bridge will increase considerably as a result of the accelerated procedure and other adjustments in funding.
The reduced time reserved for works led to an increase in the price of about €5.9 million.
At present, the net cost amount is around €25.9 million, without taking into account automatic price increases (as of October 2006).
Comparison of bridge and tunnel prices
The two highest audit institutions analysed the prices of bridges on the D 8 and A 17 motorways in order to identify bridges whose price was too high and to compare the prices of bridges on the German and Czech sides.
The analysis was based on methods of mathematical statistics.
Furthermore, tunnels on D 8 were compared with similar tunnels on motorways in Germany (A 71, A 38 and A 4).
There are no similar tunnels on the A17.
In preparing this part of the inspection, it was important to identify accurately the relevant prices.
The two highest audit institutions have established the following principles for the comparison of bridge prices: based on the actual price paid for the bridge, excluding value added tax (VAT rates vary in the Czech Republic and the SNR and are subject to change); do not take into account the prices for the special foundations of the bridge; recalpose the prices in CZK to € at the European Central Bank rate applicable at 30 June 2006. 12. 2005 (CZK 29 = € 1).
On the D 8 and A 17 there are bridges of various structures (steel-concrete, prestressed reinforced concrete, composite steel-concrete and steel) and various sizes.
In order to ensure the homogeneity of the structures examined, the bridges were divided into groups according to the type of structure.
Within these groups, the size of the bridge was also taken into account in the analyses.
By far the most common type of structure were concrete bridges on both sides of the border (20 bridges on D 8, 36 bridges on the A 17).
The analysis focused mainly on this group of bridges, as the numerousness of the file allowed the use of mathematical and statistical methods with a high degree of reliability of results.
Inspections found that the prices for m 2 concrete bridges on the D 8 and A 17 depend on the size of the bridge (its length, area): the larger the bridge, the lower the price per m2 of the bridge structure.
For German bridges, the price dependency on size was stronger than in The Czech bridges (see charts below).
Two concrete bridges on the A 17 and four on the D 8 have been identified, the price of which is significantly higher.
To locate these bridges, a method was used to detect atypical values in a set of numbers and a regression analysis that takes into account the dependence of the bridge price on its size (for determining atypically expensive bridges, the standard distance from the regression curve is upwards).
However, information on the atypically high price of these bridges should only be considered as an indicator of which bridges need to be targeted.
In order to draw a generally applicable conclusion, the causes of the high price should be analysed in each identified case.
One such cause may be ineffective administrative measures, or environmental requirements or any other acceptable reason.
Given that Czech concrete bridges are on average longer than German (see table below), the proven negative dependence of the price of the bridge on its length could lead to the assumption that Czech bridges should be cheaper.
The hypothesis of lower prices of Czech concrete bridges is also supported by lower labour costs in the construction industry in the Czech Republic compared to Germany.
On the contrary, the results of the analysis show that the prices of concrete bridges on the D 8 are higher than at A 17.
Two possible causes of this condition have been identified during the joint negotiations:
1.
In Germany, most bridges are awarded as separate orders.
Such an award allows small and medium-sized regional companies to take part in the contract competition.
In the Czech Republic, many bridges are awarded as part of the contract for part of the highway route, which is several kilometers long.
Small and medium-sized companies do not participate in such competitions because the contract is too big for them.
2.
In the Czech Republic there is more variability in bridge structures than in Germany.
In this context, the SAO found that the type of construction of the bridge was decided long before its construction.
The decision shall be taken at the time when the ŘSD translates the application for a territorial decision.
At this time, the ŘSD selects bridge types from several variants, but economy plays a smaller role in decision-making.
A general conclusion on the prices of bridges in the Czech Republic and Germany could only be expressed on the basis of a thorough analysis of the construction market in both countries, which would, however, go beyond this control action.
The border bridge is the most expensive coupled steel-concrete bridge on D 8 and A 17.
In the case of tunnels, it was found that the prices of tunnels on D 8 are twice as high as those in Germany.
However, the comparison of the main structural and technical parameters of the tunnels on the D 8 with the tunnels in Germany did not show any significant difference.
Significant price differences could be attributed to the fact that there is no real competition in the field of tunnel construction in the Czech Republic.
However, a small number of tunnels did not allow for the general conclusions to be drawn.
The efficiency and efficiency of the construction of the Dresden motorway – Prague
The independent Czech Republic was established in 1993.
In the same year, the government approved the concept of the development of the motorway network.
The D 8 motorway was to be gradually extended from Prague to the border with Germany.
Section No. 0805 through the Czech Central Mountains was to be acquired before the frontier section No. 0807.
The Czech Republic acquires the D 8 motorway as part of the programme financing.
In programme No. 327 220 "Construction of the D 8 Motorway Prague – Ústí nad Labem – State Border of the Czech Republic/Germany" set two objectives for the construction of the D 8 motorway:
1.
improve the connection of Prague and Ústí nad Labem – national goal;
2.
improve the connection between Prague and Berlin under IV. trans-European transport corridor Berlin-Istanbul – an international objective.
According to the programme, the construction of a section leading through the Czech Central Mountains was to be completed in June 2008 and the construction of the border section No. 0807 in June 2007.
It should be added here that the completion date is not identical to the date of commissioning.
The SAO found that the preparation of the construction of a section leading through the Czech Central Mountains is now at the stage of an official zoning decision.
Environmental activists have challenged the decision with lawsuits.
Actions are not finalised.
It cannot therefore be ruled out that the section leading through the Czech Central Mountains will be completed a few years later than stated in the programme documentation.
In the summer of 2006, the Czech Ministry of Transport proposed to postpone the completion date of section No. 0805 to 2010.
As a result of these facts, the construction of the border section did not achieve the national objective – improving the connection between Prague and Ústí nad Labem.
The ŘSD carried out an estimate of capital expenditure for frontier section D 8 No. 0807 and section No. 0805 through the Czech Central Mountains in the years 1999 – 2001.
The estimate for these capital expenditures included in the investment costs is about €639 million combined for both sections No 0805 and No 0807.
Table 2: Results of economic assessment (EIRR = internal rate of return)
All the highways under consideration and expressways opened, both sections D 8 opened in 2007.

The economic analysis carried out in 2001 was based on the assumption that the border section and the section across the Czech Central Mountains would be completed on time.
At the time of inspection, however, it is clear that the section through the Czech Central Mountains will not be opened at the original date.
This will reduce the above EIRR values.
Costs for both sections excluding VAT, as at 31 December 2004, are not payable to the total amount of the total amount of the taxable amount of the total amount of the taxable amount of the year. 12. 2005, were €897 million, i.e. €897 million. higher by 27,4 % than the level of costs worked by the economic analysis in 2001.
However, there is a risk that section 0805 will be routed on a different, more costly route, which would affect the above-mentioned threshold of economic viability.
Economic analysis has shown that the construction of both sections of the motorway is economically viable at a traffic intensity of at least 18 000 vehicles per day in 2010.
The forecast for 2008 was 22,940 vehicles, but a study dealing with the issue of bypass routes for a missing section through the Czech Central Mountains calculates a traffic intensity of 12,600 to 13,750 vehicles per day, which pushes the investment below the economic viability threshold.
With the higher load on the round routes for the missing section through the Czech Central Mountains, there is a high probability of congestion and thus an increase in external costs, which was not calculated in the original economic analysis.
The above reduction in revenues and cost increases mean that the eirr was not achieved as low as the construction of the border section D 8.
Construction of the D 8 border section is therefore inefficient.
There was also a similar cost overrun during the construction of the A17 motorway as in the case of these two sections on the D 8.
As part of the overall economic assessment of the Federal Road Development Plan for Long-Distance Transport for 1992, the Federal Ministry of Transport of Germany calculated the cost of about €320 million.
The resulting cost-to-income ratio was then 4.6.
In the meantime, however, costs have soared to about €670 million, and the cost-to-income ratio has more than halved.
In addition to parallel checks carried out together with the SAO BRH, in 2003 and 2005, he inspected the preparation and construction of the A 17 motorway.
The BRH found that the competent approval state authority requested a field tunnel for section 3 A 17, which was not needed.
During the inspection action, BRH managed to convince the Federal Ministry and the German Road Construction Administration that the tunnel was not necessary.
The result was to achieve savings that amounted to around €10 million and €0.15 million in annual operating costs alone.
When assessing the first section A 17 BRH, it found that the construction project was not properly prepared.
This is illustrated by the following example:
At the preparatory stage, the road construction administration did not carry out a survey of the conditions of the bedrock in the Dölzschen rocks, because the site was difficult to access.
This was carried out only after the tunnel punching machine hit the rock.
Tests showed that the rocks inside were more weathered than anticipated during the selection process.
Therefore, costly measures such as mooring, injection and stone-falling protection nets had to be taken, which required about €3.3 million.
The Directorate of Roads and Motorways had to bear the costs not only of other emergency operations, such as safety measures in the Dölzschen rocks, but also of measures that would not have been needed if the construction project had been properly prepared first.
Expenditure of this kind includes costs associated with the interruption of construction operations (€3.2 million), additional training of drilling workers (€0.5 million) and rising wages and expenditure on goods due to project overruns (€7 million).
The cost overruns thus amounted to around €10.7 million, which did not correspond to any added value.
On the basis of the lessons learned from this and other audited projects, BRH requested the Federal Ministry to apply stricter guidance in its supervision of road construction work.
In doing so, the Federal Ministry should give the Directorates of Roads and Motorways the necessary impetus to implement quality assurance systems.
The benefits of cooperation for BRH and the SAO Cooperation fulfilled the intention of both control institutions.
BRH gained control knowledge about the preparation, assignment and progress of the construction of the border bridge.
Both supreme audit institutions have built a database of bridge and tunnel prices on which future controls will be able to be relied on.
The SAO found that the main building and technical parameters of the bridges, tunnels and the route of the D 8 motorway are no different from the parameters A 17.
The inspectors of the two institutions involved in the cooperation have gained new experience, which they can use in further checks.

Coordinated control of funds to finance projects implemented under the Operational Programme for Cross-Border Cooperation Czech Republic - Republic of Poland 2007-2013
Introduction
The developing community of the people of Europe is the driving force behind cross-border cooperation as an integral part of the wider territorial cooperation that has been part of our lives for the last 20 years.
Let us therefore give this Community an introductory word on this joint report of the two Supreme Audit Institutions of neighbouring countries:
"185 million EU citizens (i.e. 37% of the population) live in border areas.
These areas are usually underdeveloped and peripheral areas, often a relic of darker parts of Europe's history.
The main objective of cross-border cooperation is to help to alleviate the existence of borders as administrative, legal and physical barriers and to further help to develop the napping potential of border regions.
The programmes cover different border regions: some cover coastal areas, other inland borders within the EU or borders shared with candidate countries.
Most of the programmes are bilateral, but some include more than two neighbouring countries."
The programmes last for seven years and a total of EUR 5.7 billion is earmarked from the EU budget. Eur.
