The procurement phase in which potential tenderers can draw up tenders on the basis of the tender documentation they have received begins with the publication of information on the procurement procedure and/or a call to tenderers.
By the date of opening of the envelopes, any tenderers may submit their tenders to the contracting authority in order to apply for the award of the contract.
Requirements of European law and the prevention of corruption
EU law does not prescribe specific requirements at this stage of the procurement procedure.
The contracting authority shall comply with the national rules governing this stage of the procedure and prevent potential manipulation.
Those provisions shall apply in particular to the organisation and control.
Provisions of German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
The principle is that tender documents on the basis of which potential suppliers make their tenders must always be sent by the contracting authority.
Design offices that are involved in the management should not fulfil this role.
The contracting authority shall ensure that all candidates have received the same information during this phase of the procurement procedure.
In the event of confusion in the procurement documents or where further questions arise, information may only be supplied to tenderers by the contracting authority.
The design offices responsible for drawing up the procurement documents may not provide any information.
During this whole phase, any contact between the design office and the applicants must be avoided.
They must remain anonymous throughout the course, as allowing contact with them can adversely affect the competition.
Tenders sent by post or submitted directly must be submitted in a closed envelope.
The e-mailed tenders must be encoded.
Different provisions
In Germany, the contracting authority may entrust insured suppliers of external services with printing and circulating documentation, and their employees must be obliged to comply with confidentiality.
In Germany, the tenders received must be marked with an indication of the date of receipt and transmitted directly and immediately in their original state (sealed) to the official responsible for their safekeeping.
This worker must not be involved in any way in the procurement procedure.
Received menus must be locked until the envelopes are opened.
In the Czech Republic, the received offers are marked with a serial number.
The contracting authority shall issue a report with details of the competition, including the number of the tender and information on the preparation of the tender and its receipt.
There are no specific regulations on the safekeeping of tenders.
Main control findings
BRH
BRH checked the assignment of the administrative building.
Sending tender documents
The audited contracting authorities of the building administration sent out the tender documents either directly or commissioned an external company to print and distribute it.
Self-employed persons did not send any documentation.
Information provided to tenderers
For the part of the procurement documents relating to the questioning and obtaining of information, the contracting authority has not followed the rule on separate planning from the procurement procedure.
Contrary to the relevant regulations, he often did not include in the documentation the names of his contact staff, but rather the staff of the project management department.
Some tender notices even included the names of companies or self-employed persons who participated in the preparation of the tender documents.
In rare cases, applicants who raised questions during the procurement procedure did not receive identical information.
Marking offers
For contracting entities, all accepted tenders have been stamped and received.
However, in some cases in the negotiated procedure, tenders were accepted by self-employed professionals, thus violating the rule of one construction of the prevention of corruption.
Custody of the tenders
Once marked, not all tenders were passed on directly and without delay to the official assigned to keep them in custody locked the tenders in a steel cabinet.
For one contracting authority, the tenders were temporarily placed in the open bin of the mailroom to which all employees had access.
Another contracting authority placed a mailbox in the corridor without constant supervision, and part of the bids thrown into the mailbox remained there overnight.
The opening of the box was wide and unsecured, making it accessible not only to the staff.
Sao
The SAO did not identify weaknesses in this area.
Summary
Rules are laid down in both countries to prevent contacts, in particular, between interested companies and design offices working together in the procurement procedure throughout the process.
Equal treatment is ensured by sending the same information to all tenderers.
Rules for the prevention of manipulation and corruption are appropriate for receipt, safekeeping and confidentiality of tenders.
In Germany, the relevant requirements are somewhat more elaborated than in the Czech Republic.
In Germany, the collected control records showed infringements in some areas.
These irregularities can be easily corrected.
Opening envelopes
Opening envelopes
During the opening of envelopes, the menus that have been closed so far are opened, their contents are read and published.
The period for which the tenderer is bound by his tender begins at the time of expiry of the period for the submission of envelopes or their opening and ends with a deadline specified by the contracting authority.
Requirements of European law and the prevention of corruption
European legislation does not contain any specific provisions on the opening of envelopes.
However, national rights and regulations contain extensive requirements to protect tenders and competition during this sensitive phase of the entire procurement procedure.
The principles of "more eyes", transparency and credibility of the envelope opening process are intended to prevent manipulations and modifications of tenders already submitted.
Provisions of German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
The opening of envelopes must be carried out by several persons appointed by the contracting authority.
Compliance with the "multiple eyes" principle is intended to prevent individuals from secretly manipulating offers.
Applicants may be present at the opening of envelopes.
When opening, all envelopes must be put before the Chairman of the Commission and opened one by one.
Late offers received must not be taken into account.
In order to ensure transparency when opening envelopes, this phase, including conclusions(s), must be recorded in writing. The record must include, but are not limited to, the names of the tenderers and the prices offered.
The enrollment must be read and signed by the group leader.
The registration may also be signed by the candidates present.
Different provisions
In the Czech Republic, a commission is set up for the opening of envelopes.
The participation of independent experts shall be accepted.
The members of the Commission may also be entrusted with the task of discussing the subsequent stages of the procedure, i.e. in the case of the commission. evaluation of tenders.
In Germany, the opening of envelopes takes place in the presence of a manager and a writer.
The manager shall be an employee of the contracting authority.
The manager and, in the case of civil engineering, shall not be involved in the preparatory phase (production of tender documents), shall not decide on the award of the contract and shall not be members in the subsequent processing (procedure) of the contract.
German regulations require that the envelope opening minutes contain not only bid prices, but also all information on discounts and special (unusual) signs, e.g. damaged envelopes when receiving or late in the offer.
In the Czech Republic, in addition to the tender prices, the entry must include an indication of the language of the tender and the signature of the tenderer.
German regulations require that all parts of open envelopes be marked to avoid subsequent changes.
Tenders, usually marked in the form of perforation with a date, must be kept confidential (secret) after the end of the envelope opening and may only be made available to persons who further process them.
There are no similar measures in the Czech Republic.
If a single offer is received in the Czech Republic, the envelope must not be opened and the tenderer must be informed without delay.
In Germany, they do not have this adjustment and, if a single offer is accepted, it is open and evaluated.
Main control findings
BRH
The principle of cross-checking
During the opening of the envelopes, the contracting authorities adhered to the principle of four eyes.
There were always managers and writers who were not assigned another role.
However, in rare cases, in small negotiated procedures, natural persons opened up tenders sent to them without the participation of the contracting authority.
The opening process of envelopes
the opening of envelopes did not always document the progress.
In some cases, tenders submitted late were not marked and in some cases signatures were missing.
Marking incoming offers
Contracting entities marked the tenders with a date perforation, which was in accordance with the requirements.
Some of them have mislampered offers in the past, but after brh alerts they changed the practice.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
Sao
Time limit for receipt of tenders
In the repair of the roads, for one event, the tenderer's tender was handed over to the contracting authority with a monthly delay, and it nevertheless accepted it.
Summary
Essential parts of the provisions for opening envelopes are identical in both countries, taking into account the 'more eye' principle and the principle of transparency, thus making it possible to substantially reduce the risk of corruption and manipulation.
German rules are more complex compared to the Czech Republic, especially the requirements for precise documentation of the procedure.
Marking, safe storage and respect for the confidentiality of tenders substantially limit the possibility of subsequent changes in the tenders submitted.
In addition, the workers responsible for opening envelopes shall not carry out any other activities related to the contract to be awarded.
Despite the detection of some irregularities, the findings confirm that the rules for opening envelopes are largely applied.
Assessment and evaluation of tenders
The contracting authority must review and evaluate tenders received within the time limit set.
At the same time, it must award the contract to the tenderer who best meets the award criteria in the tender.
Requirements of European law and the prevention of corruption
EU law provides for a process of assessing and evaluating tenders in a few steps:
The first step is to check the suitability of the applicants.
They must have a good economic and financial position and the required professional and technical knowledge and skills.
Applicants who have ever been convicted of bribery or defrauding must always be excluded from the procurement procedures.
Tenders of undeciced tenderers must be evaluated in terms of the correctness, technical suitability and value for money on the basis of the previously published procurement criteria.
The contracting authority must identify the most economically favourable tender and in particular examine all significantly low prices.
Review and evaluation is particularly sensitive and susceptible to manipulation.
For example, tenderers may be excluded without a legitimate reason, or tenders that do not meet the requirements may be left in competition.
The outcome of the evaluation may be incorrectly influenced by the preference of a tenderer or its disadvantage, thereby preventing the selection of the most economically advantageous tender.
The contracting authority must therefore take specific measures when selecting the persons included in the process and shall ensure that they meet the requirements for integrity and technical knowledge.
They must also make sure that the whole process and the decisions taken are transparent and credible.
Provisions of German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
In accordance with EU requirements, the relevant provisions in both countries require the review and evaluation of tenders in successive steps.
During the evaluation, the requirements for proving the suitability of tenderers, the evaluation criteria and their weights specified in the notice or in the tender documents shall not be amended.
The criteria laid down for assessing the suitability of tenderers cannot be further applied.
Further evaluation can only be carried out on the basis of evaluation criteria.
The tenders submitted must first be examined from a formal point of view whether or not they are complete or not include suspicious elements which could encourage manipulation.
Where tenderers are excluded from further examination and evaluation of tenders submitted by them, they shall be informed without delay.
Where, as a result of the evaluation of tenders, the quotation price is found to be disproportionately low, it must be given to the tenderer concerned the opportunity to comment on the situation before any withdrawal of the tender.
The reasons for the decision must be transparently documented.
Different provisions
In Germany, tenderers must remain silent and only the beneficiaries can participate in the evaluation of tenders.
Only the contracting authority may examine the mathematical accuracy of tenders.
Only employees who are not included in the decision-making phase of the supplier's selection or the project implementation phase may be entrusted with the evaluation.
There are no precise provisions on who can carry out further reviews and evaluations.
If external companies are entrusted with reviewing and evaluating tenders, they must be aware that the offers are confidential and respect this fact.
They may only make proposals to the contracting authority for a decision.
In the Czech Republic, tenders must be reviewed and evaluated by a commission appointed by the contracting authority, which draws up a report with a proposal for the conclusion of a contract.
However, in both countries the final decision depends on the contracting authority.
Where, in Germany, the documents and declarations required in connection with the submission of tenders are incomplete, the tenderers concerned must subsequently submit the required documents within six days.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
If tenderers fail to comply with this obligation, their tenders must be excluded.
In the Czech Republic, the contracting authority may decide whether to give the applicant the opportunity to supplement the missing documents.
If the candidate does not prove them, they must be excluded.
In Germany, it is necessary to examine not only the total price, but also the unit prices.
Where the price structure of the tender shows that the prices for parts of the overall project have been estimated disproportionately high or low, tenderers must be asked for an explanation.
If they do not provide explanations and if the contracting authority can demonstrate that the tender contains compensatory prices, such tenders must be excluded.
This is intended to prevent tenderers from submitting price calculations on the assumption that substantial quantitative changes will be made to each part of the overall project, which can lead to a significant increase in project costs.
In the Czech Republic, the total price of the work is evaluated and the prices of the individual parts are not examined in detail.
Valuation compensation is not the reason for excluding the offer.
In Germany, a contract cannot be awarded to a tenderer offering a disproportionately high or low price.
Where one or more tenders differ in price by 10 % or more from the price estimated by the contracting authority or from other tenders, tenderers must demonstrate that their tender has been credibly and convincingly calculated.
If they are unable to do so, the contracting authority should exclude them.
In the Czech Republic, the procurement procedure may be cancelled after a price review if only tenders with disproportionately low prices have been received and the tenderers have not justified those prices.
If the price of the tender is substantially higher than the contracting authority's estimate, this is not the reason for refusing to award the contract to the tenderer concerned (unlike the German procurement law).
Where there is a suspicion in Germany of conduct intended to restrict competition, the contracting authority shall immediately report this fact to the competent superior authority.
It must decide on the next procedure and whether it is appropriate to inform the antitrust office or law enforcement authorities.
It must also approve (e.g. when the contract exceeds €50,000 and the contract has not been awarded to the tenderer with the lowest bid), whether the contract will be awarded when the contract is discussed or whether the procurement procedure will be cancelled.
Czech rules do not regulate this area.
Main control findings
BRH
Fitness check and procurement criteria
Most of the procurement procedures examined were in line with the relevant requirements.
In the case of certain recommendations of potential suppliers made by self-employed persons, the contracting authorities themselves did not check the suitability of tenderers.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
In some cases, there was insufficient documentation as to whether the contracting authority had taken into account all published evaluation criteria or whether the selection decision was based solely on the price criterion.
Selection of interested parties and confidentiality of tenders
Some contracting authorities used the services of unauthorized persons, such as self-employed persons or building authorities.
They were incorporated into the planning or implementation process of construction projects, performing functions which were to be held exclusively by the contracting authority.
The contracting authorities have tried to justify this fact by their lack of human resources in the sector.
In some cases, they used self-employed professionals to review the service offers of persons who were not formally bound to maintain the confidentiality of tenders and to carry out with due care the fulfilment of their obligations under the contract.
As regards contracting entities, as a rule, there was no evidence as to whether the offers in the custody of self-employed professionals were only available to designated persons.
Review and mathematical check of offers
Some contracting entities have submitted open envelopes for further examination to self-employed experts without first carrying out the prescribed examination of tenders and a mathematical examination and without documenting the results of those examinations.
In the event of any intention of manipulation, third parties may have made changes to tenders which could not be identified by the contracting authority.
The examination of the documents revealed a number of cases where unusual elements in the tenders were not adequately identified or where price and product data were missing.
Performance audits
A model inspection by one contracting authority revealed that in 75 % of the procurement procedures, the most advantageous tenders deviated by more than 10 % from the pre-estimated costs.
One of the 20 procurement procedures was cancelled due to inadequate tender prices.
In many cases, there was no evidence or sufficient documentation on the examination of tenders or negotiations with tenderers for further clarification.
In many cases, detailed information was also also missing e.g. the unit prices of the most important invoiced items.
Changes in market prices or an increase in material costs were often cited as the reason for the deviations.
The contracting authorities argued that identifying and proving compensatory prices was difficult.
In the case of one call for tenders made by an entity outside the ordinary contracting authorities, a 66 % lower price was offered compared to the original cost estimate.
Data on closer examination of the cost or on the determination of the reasons for the deviations were not recorded.
In clarifying this question, the contracting authority found no indication of price dumping on the tenderer to whom the contract would eventually be awarded.
It was therefore not clarified whether the initial cost estimate was excessive or whether the price offered was too low.
Later, the contracting authority rated this tenderer as a 'low-cost company' which was unable to meet either the quality requirements or the deadlines.
In another procurement procedure, the contracting authority awarded the contract to a tenderer whose price was 35 % higher than the original cost estimate.
The contracting authority did not cancel the procurement procedure and put forward an unfounded argument that the tenderer could be presumed not to base its pricing on a disproportionately high cost.
Suspected irregularities
One contracting authority found two cases of irregularities, and these were reported to the company responsible for technical supervision.
In one procurement procedure, two tenderers submitted tenders containing an identical price calculation, which led the contracting authority to exclude both tenders.
The checks did not show any substantial deficiencies in the application of the other provisions.
Sao
Verification of suitability
For many construction projects, such as the construction of a building site, the university buildings, roads and railways, contracting entities have not excluded tenderers from participating in the procurement procedure, even if they have not complied with the requirements of the contracting authority referred to in the specifications, or have failed to provide the qualifications to the required extent, or, on the contrary, one contracting authority has failed to substantiate or explain the reason for the decommissioning of the candidate who complied with the requirements.
Guest
In the case of the construction of a waste water treatment plant, the individual evaluation criteria of the procurement procedure for the contractor were established, but the contracting authority did not respect them during the procedure.
For actions in the field of railway infrastructure development, the weighting of the award criteria at the start of the management was not determined at the start of the evaluation criteria, but only at the beginning of the evaluation.
For the road repair project, the evaluation of the criterion of 'reduction of construction time' was not correct.
For second and third place bidders, the evaluation incorrectly indicated a greater reduction in construction time than indicated in their tenders.
Documentation of the reasons for the selection of the candidate
For the three housing promotion actions, the contracting authority has not demonstrated on the basis of which criteria it has assessed the tenders received and how it has selected the most suitable of them.
The correctness of the selection of small-scale procurement suppliers associated with the construction of a road circuit with an estimated price of up to CZK 500,000 is correct.
Czk could not be verified because the suppliers were selected only on the basis of telephone consultations on the price and date of performance, but documents on these negotiations were not produced.
Summary
In both countries, the rules for verifying and evaluating offers correspond to EU requirements.
However, they differ in view of the specific management steps and the selection of individuals involved in the procedure.
Unlike in the Czech Republic, these procurement process steps in Germany are governed by stricter and more detailed requirements, especially as regards the application of the cross principle and the protection of tenders.
The same applies to the rules for verifying the appropriateness of the prices offered.
In both countries, in some cases, controls found that the substantial steps of the process in verifying and evaluating tenders were not documented at all and, if so, only partially.
The absence of control tools and transparency in decision-making during the review and evaluation of tenders makes it possible to manipulate.
The checks have shown serious defects, such as the transmission of tenders to third parties without prior appropriate examination and documentation of tenders by the contracting authority.
Where contracting entities entrust a third party with the performance of functions related to the screening and evaluation of tenders, appropriate measures and increased control of measures against increased possibility of manipulation shall be necessary.
In checking the eligibility of prices, the German contracting authorities audited did not use a complete set of available instruments in all cases and did not deal with their own price structure.
In the Czech Republic, weaknesses were found in the evaluation of the suitability of tenders and the use of evaluation criteria.
Completion of the procurement procedure
After review and evaluation of tenders, the procurement process shall be completed by the award of the contract or by the cancellation of the procedure.
Requirements of European law and the prevention of corruption
In the case of a European procedure, all tenderers must be informed in advance of the award decision.
Suppliers shall have the opportunity to review the decision taken within a limited period of 10 or 15 days and to request its review, if appropriate.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
The 10-day period applies to electronic submissions and 15 days to other submissions.
The contract shall not be concluded before the expiry of that period or before the decision of the review procedure.
If the review body rejects the complaint and confirms the decision, candidates and tenderers shall be given the opportunity to have the fairness of the application of the procurement law reviewed by an independent court.
This measure ensures that no contracting authority will be able to circumvent the legal protection of suppliers by the prompt implementation of the procurement procedure decision.
The contracting authority shall properly document the progress of the procedure.
Provisions of German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
Both countries implemented management information obligations.
In both countries, the final decision on the outcome of the procurement procedure rests with the contracting authority.
However, it cannot arbitrarily deviate from the results of a properly carried out examination and evaluation.
The contracting authority is to conclude the contract within the specified time.
This is due to the fact that the tenderer is not bound by his tender after the expiry of that period.
The content of the contract must not deviate from the winning offer.
Unsuccessful tenderers should be informed of the result in a timely manner, stating the reason why their tender was not accepted.
The cancellation of a procurement procedure is permissible only if certain conditions are met, e.g. by the commission of a contract procedure. if the prices in the tenders do not conform to the specifications.
Different provisions
In the Czech Republic, the mandatory waiting period before the conclusion of the contract of 10 or 15 days applies to European and national procedures.
In Germany, the equivalent provision applies only to European procedures.
In all other proceedings in Germany, tenderers may not be informed of the award of the contract before deciding on its EU provisions and the award of a review.
In the Czech Republic, the procurement procedure must be cancelled if a single tender has been received or only one tender has met the requirements for its consideration and evaluation.
In Germany, a contract must be awarded even if a single tender has been received, provided that the tender meets the conditions laid down in the tender documents and is cost-effective.
Main control findings
BRH
Checks found few irregularities in the completion of the audited procurement processes.
In some cases, European proceedings have received companies authorising letters before the notification period expires, which may invalidate the contract.
Also, in several open cases, the authorising letters of modification incompatible with the content of the tender, e.g. in the form of a tender, were included in the form of an open procedure. new deadlines.
In some cases, contracting entities have failed to meet the time limits for awarding the contract.
In one open procedure, the contracting authority selected the second most advantageous tender because the tenderer offering a price of more than 50 % lower no longer wished to fulfil the contract at the originally offered price.
Sao
In one case, during the reconstruction and construction of the higher education institution, the contracting authority did not conclude a contract for the work with the contractor in accordance with the draft contract contained in the tender of the selected tenderer.
For some road repair and maintenance events, the construction of a motorway and a road circuit, contracts were concluded later than required by law.
For construction modifications in former military raids, the contracting authority sent a notice of selection of the most suitable tender to all tenderers only after the legal deadline had expired.
Summary
Both countries have implemented EU rules on the termination of the procurement procedure.
The legal protection of failed candidates contributes to reducing corruption.
The Czech Public Procurement Act also includes the Institute of Legal Protection in cases of contracts below EU limits.
In both countries, it was found that a limited time limit for the conclusion of the contract had been exceeded.
This can cause adverse economic consequences and increase the risk of manipulation.
In the future, contracting entities should eliminate such deficiencies in the conclusion of the procurement procedure.
Documentation, notification, information obligations
The procurement process, with all its individual stages, relevant findings and decisions, including relevant justifications, shall be documented in a transparent manner.
The completion of the procurement procedure at European level must be published.
The data on procurement procedures are summarised in EU statistics.
Requirements of European law and the prevention of corruption
The obligation to document procurement procedures is in line with the fundamental requirement of the principle of transparency applied at EU level.
Only proper and time-relevant documentation on decision-making and justification guarantees transparency in the procurement process and, above all, guarantees effective legal protection of the interests of each tenderer in cases where the value of the contract exceeds European limits.
Appropriate documentation is also an essential part of anti-corruption measures, since the obligation to justify individual decisions in detail and their merits significantly reduces the scope for manipulation.
In the case of European procurement procedures, the contracting authority must notify the EU's Office of Official Publications within 48 days of the date of award of the contract.
The Authority publishes the notification in the Official Journal of the EU and the requirement of transparency is also fulfilled.
The contracting authority must summarise the relevant information on its procurement procedures and communicate them to the European Commission through the relevant national ministries.
On this basis, the European Commission publishes annual statistics to gain an overview of the development of the single market in the field of construction.
Provisions of German and Czech procurement law
Same or similar provisions
Both countries fully transposed the provisions of the European Law on Documentation and Notification Obligations into their national legislation.
The provisions on documentation and notification for the purposes of European statistics are almost the same in both countries.
Different provisions
In the Czech Republic, the obligation to notify the award of a contract does not only apply to European procedures, but also to national procurement procedures.
The notification period is only 15 days from the conclusion of the contract.
In Germany, the obligation to notify procurement procedures, in addition to those which are compulsory under European law, applies only to restricted procedures exceeding the 25,000 limit. € (625 ths. and direct proceedings exceeding the limit of CZK 15,000. € (375 ths. czk) incl. VAT.
Only the parties are informed below this limit.
Main control findings
BRH
Documentation
A large number of assignments have not been fully documented.
The notification did not contain all the necessary information, e.g. the reasons for supply specifications and national rules.
In the case of one procedure, the contracting authority did not explain why it had concluded a contract with a tenderer whose tender did not contain mandatory requirements.
In several cases, some required records were also missing.
Publication of the award of the contract
In the case of certain European procedures, the contracting authority made no errors in the publication of the notice.
In the case of several assignments, there was no evidence of publication of the notice.
Notification obligation
Statistically tested files included the required minimum of information and were created and sent on time.
Preliminary transparency
In most cases, the contracting authority published information on the outcome of the contract.
In the case of one contracting authority, the contract information was not disclosed due to a communication error.
It took the sponsor six months to notice the errors.
Consequently, the outcome of the proceedings was not disclosed during that period.
Sao
Documentation
For events related to the organisation of a major sporting event, significant deficiencies were identified in the documentation on the conduct of the procurement procedure, such as the award procedure. incorrect information on bid prices in the protocols from the evaluation committee meetings.
In addition, some documents about opening envelopes have not been signed.
Publication of the award of the contract
In the preparation of repairs and maintenance of roads, the construction of the motorway and the road circuit, the contract award notices were sent after the deadline or not published.
Summary
The provisions on documentation and notification and notification obligations include European requirements and are almost the same in both countries.
This generally ensures transparency of procurement procedures and final selection.
Czech notification obligations are somewhat stricter compared to German ones.
The checks revealed shortcomings substantially reducing the value of documentation as a means of preventing corruption.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
Contracting entities should continue to strengthen the transparency of their procurement procedures and fully comply with the notification and notification requirements.
Summary evaluation and recommendations
Parallel controls of the SAO and BRH were focused on two areas which are relevant to the procurement process in both the Czech Republic and Germany, namely the application of EU procurement law and the prevention of corruption.
EU legislation gives an opportunity for international competition within the EU with a view to creating a single European market.
Measures aimed at preventing corruption are not only intended to avoid or at least reduce corruption, but also to prevent financial damage and possible losses of confidence in the integrity of the government.
The findings of the two audit institutions – the SAO and the BRH – with regard to the application of the procurement law of the two countries and the comparison of its relevant provisions give an internal view of the common and distinct elements that can assist the two countries in further developing and applying that right.
Application of EU procurement law
Both countries transposed EU public procurement law into their national legislation.
In both countries, there is thus an important common basis for public procurement and fulfilment of the essential requirements in the field of: competition; equal treatment of candidates; transparency of procurement procedures.
Contracting entities reinforce these requirements in part by very large-scale measures.
The Czech Republic has applied provisions on public procurement requiring European management as well as to procedures that are below EU limits and is therefore governed by national legislation.
However, the checks have shown that contracting entities do not always fully comply with all relevant provisions of EU requirements.
German contracting authorities should continue to improve the quality of their procurement procedures in order to eliminate the irregularities mentioned, taking into account the implementation of EU requirements.
In the Czech Republic, the controls identified risks affecting economy and achievement of value for money.
This concerns, in particular, the incomplete definition of the subject-matter of the contract, which has resulted in additional works which have often been commissioned in breach of the law, the lack of definition of the intended price and the required qualification assumptions narrowing the possible range of tenderers and thus reducing competition, in particular in the field of transport constructions.
Prevention of corruption
Joint controls were not intended to detect cases of corruption.
This was because both BRH and the SAO do not have the tools to do so.
However, they can examine whether the competent authorities of both countries are taking measures to reduce corruption and manipulation in public procurement and how these measures are applied.
When it comes to preventing corruption, the two countries have focused on different aspects.
In particular, the German provisions give scope for widespread and unlimited competition, transparency and controls as a central element in the prevention of corruption.
In particular, Czech regulations monitor the strengthening of the transparency of procurement procedures.
BRH
In Germany, there are general principles for the prevention of corruption that apply to the entire federal administration.
These principles have also been incorporated between public procurement requirements and have been adopted to meet the specific needs of such procurement.
The relevant provisions specify, sometimes very precisely, ways of complying with the requirements for the prevention of corruption during the procurement procedure and for the selection of persons included therein.
In THE BRH's view, the principle of the preference for open procurement procedures and calls for participation is a particularly appropriate tool for substantially reducing the risk of corruption in public procurement, while reducing competition increases the risk of manipulation.
Risk analysis and adequate control (in particular the principle of cross-checking), transparency requirements, procurement documents and various organisational measures are also an effective mechanism for preventing corruption and manipulation.
The BRH therefore does not feel the need for substantial changes to the current provisions that public institutions must comply with when awarding public contracts.
Anti-corruption measures are widely applied in practice.
The irregularities found in some areas highlighted weaknesses in compliance with some requirements.
Therefore, contracting entities should provide their staff with further training, thus familiaring them with anti-corruption requirements and further raising their awareness in this area.
A significant proportion of the weaknesses identified relate to activities delegated by the construction administration to private entrepreneurs.
However, the absence of adequate controls in the delegation of powers increases the risk of abuse.
Activities prone to manipulation and corruption should therefore only be transferred to third parties if the administration can guarantee a sufficient degree of protection against unauthorised interference.
Sao
Anti-corruption strategies have been adopted at government level in the Czech Republic, which also have a significant concern in the area of public procurement.
The SAO's control actions took place during the period when one of the most important parts of this strategy was implemented, namely a significant change in the Public Procurement Act and the adoption of follow-up implementing regulations.
The adopted strategy and the new legislation can be effective steps to improve the situation.
For example, under the new rules, the contracting authority must justify the effectiveness of the contract, the determination of the projected value of the contract, the adequacy of the requirements for qualification assumptions, the establishment of the basic evaluation criteria and the method of evaluation of tenders and the proper substantiation and publication of everything.
Recommendations
Overall, both the SAO and BRH have a favourable opinion on the ways in which EU requirements are implemented.
Their broad application in practice has confirmed that EU requirements for competition, equal treatment and transparency form an appropriate basis for eu procurement.
The transnational model introduced in the EU can also serve as a basis for similar projects aimed at facilitating and promoting international competition.
Taking into account the great potential of material and intangible damages resulting from manipulation and corruption in connection with public procurement, both the BRH and the SAO insist that it is the obligation of the contracting authorities to continue measures against corruption and manipulation and to improve them where possible.
In particular, the organisational structures and procurement processes should be continuously monitored in terms of weaknesses and risks in order to identify and respond appropriately to corrective action.
Compared to practice in Germany, it has been apparent that the share of open procurement procedures should be increased in the Czech Republic, which give space to competition and substantially reduce the possibility of corrupt behaviour.
The award of contracts in parts may also have a positive impact on the price achieved in cases where this is permissible and appropriate for the contracting authorities. A higher number of applicants creates pressure on the price achieved.
The provision of his organisation also affects the conduct of the procurement procedure.
In Germany it is provided by special state organizations, while in the Czech Republic, with the exception of transport constructions, it is organised by the central authorities themselves or through contractual organisations.
Both the SAO and the BRH wish to further develop the knowledge in their work where appropriate and to address them with their parliament and government beyond their joint project.
Moreover, they are convinced that the principles of the procurement law and their implementation, as described in this report, will also be of interest at the level of the International Organisation of Supreme Audit Institutions (INTOSAI), as these principles and findings are of general importance for the effective fight against corruption and for the guarantee that public contracts are awarded under a well-functioning and honest competition regime and that value for money is achieved.
Annex
JOINT FINAL REPORT ON THE RESULTS OF PARALLEL CONTROLS ON EXCISE TAX ADMINISTRATION IN THE CZECH REPUBLIC
Joint final report
May 2017
Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic
Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic
Introductory word
The present joint report informs about the progress and outcome of international cooperation in parallel checks carried out by the Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic and the Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic, focusing on the management of excise duties in 2012-2015.
Cooperation between the supreme control institutions of both countries was carried out on the basis of a cooperation agreement between the SAO SR and the SAO CR in the performance of parallel controls aimed at the administration of excise duties, which was concluded in August 2015.
The topic of parallel controls was selected on the basis of the fact that the two EU Member States are based on common European legislation in order to determine how it is applied at national level, how the system of excise tax administration is set up and how the systems are different in the Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic.
The greatest contribution of the control actions carried out was the exchange of experience, the identification of differences and the identification of good practice.
Last but not least, the benefit was of finding that the international comparability of data on the performance and efficiency of excise duty management is very limited without parallel controls being carried out.
(Bangalore)
Karol Mitrík,
President
Chairman
Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic
Supreme Audit Office of the Slovak Republic
on the results of parallel checks of SPD administration in The Czech Republic
Summary and evaluation
The legislation on excise duties in the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic and their administration complies with EU law and significantly exceeds EU requirements.
Differences have been identified between the adjustment of excise duties in the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic, contributing to the effective administration of excise taxes by verifying the economic stability of applicants for the issue of permits and mandatory marking and dyeing of selected mineral oils and certain other oils; In The Czech Republic, the distribution of control marks is easier than in the Czech Republic and less burdens the tax authorities.
In the fight against leaks in excise duties, supervision of the movement of raw tobacco or tobacco raw materials, the implementation of the fuel distributor institute and the register of sellers of consumer packaging of alcohol have proven to be good practice in both countries.
Income from excise duties in the Czech Republic is growing more slowly than other tax revenues.
The EU's objectives of reducing labour taxation, introducing environmentally-friendly measures and reducing dependence on tobacco and alcohol have not yet been met in the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic, among others. also because indexation of excise duty rates is not in place in both countries.
This results in a reduction in the importance of excise duties on total tax revenues and, as a result of increasing purchasing power, a real reduction in the tax burden on excise duties.
The state has long supported the implementation of environmental measures financially, but these measures have a negative impact on excise revenues, which will thus need to be replaced by other revenue or a reduction in state expenditure in the future.
Administrative expenditure incurred for the administration of excise duties in the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic has been increasing for a long time, mainly due to wage growth, and their efficiency is declining.
In the Czech Technical University, this efficiency is also negatively affected by expenditure on the electronization of excise duty management (IT expenditure) and expenditure on the wages of employees carrying out permanent tax supervision in tax warehouses for alcohol.
The electronization of excise tax administration in the SR did not significantly affect the reduction in the number of tax authorities.
The SAO ČR and the SAO SR recommend that the FŘ SR reconsider the merits of the exercise of permanent tax supervision in tax warehouses for alcohol.
In the Czech Republic, the effectiveness of administrative expenditure was influenced by the fact that the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic did not apply procedures during the audited period which would lead to a reduction in the personnel demands of the administration of excise duties.
The number of comparable administrative tasks of tax administrations was similar in the Czech Republic in the individual years of the audited period, while the number of comparable tax entities in the Czech Republic is about a third lower than in the Czech Republic.
Tax administrations in the Czech Republic carry out administrative tasks mainly in the form of physical supervision of tax supervision, while tax administrations in the Czech Republic emphasize remote supervision and risk analysis.
The administration of excise duties in the Czech Republic is administratively more demanding than in the Czech Republic and more costly in relation to the ratio of the number of tax acts to the number of entities.
The electronization of excise tax administration in the Czech Republic took place in different areas.
In the Czech Republic, the administration of tax returns on excise duties is fully electronized, in the Czech Republic documents proving the taxation of selected products in free tax circulation are transmitted electronically.
Both methods of electronization support the effective management of excise duties, which is why the SAO CR and the SAO SR recommend that they apply them not only in both countries.
The total expenditure on the introduction of the EMCS system could not be compared as the FŘ SR provided data on expenditure only for the system upgrade in the period 2011-2015, but expenditure was also spent before that period.
The expenses incurred in that period only for the EMCS upgrade were about 20% higher in the SR than the expenditure incurred in the Czech Republic both for the introduction of EMCS and for the upgrade of this system in more than ten years.
The managers of excise duties in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic did not achieve comparable values of qualitative indicators when spending comparable expenses.
The level of supervision is comparable in both countries, but in the SR, the management of excise duties is significantly more resource-intensive.
The introduction of an electronic system for monitoring the movement of excise products (EMCS) made the management of excise duties more efficient, but in the SR to a lower extent, as significantly higher expenditure was incurred to implement the system and its modernisation than in the Czech Republic.
Basic information
The cooperation between the two audit institutions took place on the basis of the Cooperation Agreement in the implementation of parallel controls aimed at the management of excise duties of 18 December 2004. 8. 2015.
The SAO CR and the SAO SR have agreed to carry out parallel checks, which will primarily focus on the issue of excise tax administration and whose results will allow analysis, mutual comparison and evaluation of the facts found.
Common audit issues were agreed on which parallel controls were based.
Characteristics of the subject and objectives of parallel control:
The objective of the parallel controls was to compare the performance of excise managers, taking into account qualitative and quantitative indicators, and to identify weaknesses in the excise tax management process.
In particular, the following main audit questions should have been answered:
Did the managers of excise duties in the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic achieve comparable values of qualitative indicators when spending comparable expenses?
Has the introduction of an electronic system for monitoring the movement of products subject to excise duties (Excise Movement and Control System ( EMCS) made the management of excise duties more efficient and was the expenditure of its implementation spent efficiently?
Parallel checks were to identify the causes of significant differences affecting the efficiency and effectiveness of tax administration in the Czech Republic and The Czech Republic, especially in the area of regulation and in the setting of the organizational structure.

Legislation for excise duties in the Czech Republic and The Czech Republic
Excise tax administration legislation is divided into eu legislation (see Annex 1) and national legislation (see Annex 2).
Council Directive 2008/118/EC, on the general arrangements for excise duties and repealing Directive 92/12/EEC, defines excise duty and lays down the basic rules for the administration of taxes and the management of energy products and electricity, tobacco products, alcohol and alcoholic beverages.
This Directive allows for the imposition of taxes on consumption on other products.
Eu legislation provides, in particular, for minimum conditions for: the amount of tax rates for each type of product selected, the production, storage, processing and possession of taxable products, the incurring of tax, tax exemption and refund, the supervision of the transport of selected products between EU Member States, international cooperation and the keeping of registers on economic operators and tax warehouses.
EU legislation allows control procedures and institutes to be introduced at national level, provided that they do not distort competition.
Legislation of excise duties in the Czech Republic
Definition of legislation in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, the legislation on excise duties is concentrated in the Excise Tax Act (Act No. 353/2003 Coll.), which regulates the administration of mineral oil tax, alcohol taxes, taxes on tobacco products, taxes on beer, taxes on wine and intermediate products and taxes on raw tobacco.
This Law defines the forms of handling of products subject to excise duties, tax payers, authorisation procedures, conditions for the transport of products, tax returns and penalties for infringements.
The Law and subsequent decrees further regulate some other conditions for the treatment of mineral oils (mineral oil tagging), restrictions on the sale of spirits and tobacco products, monitoring the management of special mineral oils and storage of raw tobacco for a purpose other than the manufacture of tobacco products.
Taxes on other energy products (i.e. natural gas and certain other gases, solid fuels and electricity) are regulated in Parts 45 to 47 of Act No. 261/2007 Coll., on the stabilisation of public budgets.
In the Czech Republic, a number of provisions related to the administration of excise duties are included in special legislation. The Fuel Act No. 311/2006 Coll. and the Implementing Regulation regulate the conditions for the sale, supply, distribution of fuels and the keeping of the register of fuels placed into free tax circulation.
In Act No. 61/1997 Coll., on alcohol, and its implementing regulations, the conditions for the production, storage, registration and control of the production and circulation of alcohol are defined.
Act No. 307/2013 Coll., on mandatory alcohol marking, and the relevant implementing provisions provide for mandatory labelling of alcohol in consumer packaging, conditions for handling control tapes and conditions for the management of alcohol (i.e. for the production, processing, sale or other transfer, transport, transport, storage, acceptance, use, possession, import or export of alcohol).
Procedures for tax proceedings, which are not specified in special regulations, are regulated by Act No. 280/2009 Coll., the Tax Code.
Sanctions are imposed procedures under Act No. 500/2004 Coll., Administrative Code.
The conditions for issuing a trade licence (concession) for the operation of the trade "production and processing of fuels and lubricants and distribution of fuels" and "production, modification and sale of fermented spirit, spirit and spirits" are regulated by Act No. 455/1991 Coll., on trade (Trade Licensing Act).
The Czech Republic has used the right to introduce control procedures and institutes for the control of the transport of selected products in free tax circulation and to supervise compliance with the legislation in the handling of selected products for which excise duty has not been paid, as well as in the management of selected products for which the tax has already been paid.
This includes monitoring the treatment of special mineral oils and raw tobacco, the labelling of certain other mineral oils, the labelling of tobacco products and alcohol in consumer packaging.
The Czech Republic has also used the right to apply excise duty to other products and has introduced an excise duty on raw tobacco as one of the measures against tax fraud.
Structure of legislation changes for individual types of excise duties in relation to the subject of inspection in the Czech Republic
On the basis of the resolution of the Government of the Czech Republic of 3 December 2004 on the conclusion of the Agreement between the European Economic Community and the In 2012-2015, the Implementation of the "Zero Tolerance Plan on the Black Market for Spirits" was implemented in the Czech Republic, which introduced a number of measures against tax fraud on the excise duty on alcohol excise.
During the same period, there were also major changes in the legislation on mineral oil tax, tobacco tax and the criminality of the preparation of tax cuts.
Criminal law protection of tax revenues
With effect from 1 January 2005, the 7. 2016, the criminality of the preparation of the offence is introduced "tax reduction, fee and similar compulsory payments". The adjustment should allow police authorities to take more effective and timely measures to reduce tax fraud, e.g. to reduce tax fraud. operational search resources.
General provisions of the administration of excise duties
The issue of an authorisation for the handling of products subject to excise duty under the Excise Act shall be subject to the following conditions as from 1 January 2007. 1. 2015 conditional on: reliability; debt-free; economic stability; the right to pursue a trade enabling the pursuit of an activity related to the authorisation; situations where the claimant is not in liquidation or in bankruptcy.
The aim of the legislation was, in particular, to address the issue of tax arrears by reducing entities authorised to handle products subject to excise taxation.
The condition of economic stability now allows the tax administrator to take into account the financial situation of tax entities both in the context of the authorisation procedure and after the authorisation has been granted.
The purpose of this measure is to prevent entities that do not have sufficient financial revenue to properly fulfil their tax obligations to treat selected products.
To assess the economic stability of the proposer, indicators (profitability, liquidity, financial stability, activity, labour productivity) were established on the basis of which the financial analysis is carried out.
In addition to these indicators, it is also up to the administrative discretion of the tax administrator with regard to the individual conditions of the procedure.
The act provides for the periodicity of the verification of compliance with the condition of economic stability due to the timeliness of the data – the examination takes place once a year following the deadline for submitting the income tax return.
The tax administrator has the possibility to lay down other conditions necessary for tax administration.
If the holder of the authorisation does not fulfil the conditions, the tax administrator is entitled to revoke the authorisation or to revoke it with a delay.
Of the 2,609 entities for which the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic examined the condition of economic stability, 18.6% were found to be economically unstable with a high risk of arrears if the tax liability exceeded the amount of tax security (e.g. repeated beneficiaries).
The authorisation was revoked by 10 entities, the other applicants increased the tax security, capitalised their deposit into the company or documented the current accounting data, according to which they already met all the conditions for issuing the permit.
In addition to the applicant, the conditions of reliability and debt-free must be met by a natural person who is a statutory body or a member of it, or a natural person who, although not a statutory body of the applicant or a member thereof, carries out this activity (chaining of legal persons in the capacity of a statutory body or its member, so-called connected entities).
By the end of 2016, more than 30 000 linked entities had been screened.
Records kept under the Excise Tax Act (Sections 37 to § 40 and § 60 of Act No. 353/2003 Coll.) contain information on:
the type, name, code and quantity of goods produced, taken over, issued or dispatched, broken down by type of tax treatment regime (suspensive exemption scheme, importation, re-entry under the suspensive exemption procedure, export, free circulation, own consumption, loss);
the identifier (SEED ID) of the consignee or supplier of the selected products, the declarant, the date of occurrence of the event and the registration;
transport of selected products (e.g. means of transport, carrier, transport number);
the registration numbers of the related documents;
notification of the placing in consumer packaging of the consumer packaging marked with the control tape and the indication of its distribution.
The record of acceptance after transport shall be made without delay after its completion.
In the case of electronic records, the records must be kept or allow output in the format xls, xlsx, ods.
Alcohol
After 2012, the Czech Republic introduced a complex of measures designed to provide a detailed overview of the activities of the entities (see Annex 3, Scheme A) from the production of raw alcohol through marking with control tape to its distribution to the end seller or to an authorised user of exempt alcohol.
In the Czech Republic, the supervision of customs authorities and production equipment for the production of alcohol, which is not in operation, is subject to supervision.
The aim of the new legislation was to increase the overview of the processing of spirit alcohol and the production of spirit drinks and to identify persons handling alcohol in consumer packaging, to reduce the management of spirits to financially stable and reliable persons and to ensure constant supervision of the production and labelling of spirits.
The most important measures are: Records of production, income, stocks and the issue of alcohol contain information on the quantity of alcohol according to the individual stages of production and processing of alcohol, indicating the numbers of the documents.
Limiting the volume of consumer packaging, packaging material and limiting the number of packages with broken control tape at the point of final sale or issue to the consumer.
Consumer packaging means a container or other packaging with a volume of max. one litre or three litres if it is a container made of glass.
Spirit drinks in larger packages shall be considered as unmarked which are prohibited to be handled.
At the point of final sale to a natural person for his personal consumption, there may be a max. one consumer package with broken control tape or three if fitted with a one-way valve.
Compulsory registration of a person who lists alcohol in products in consumer packaging having at least 15 % of volume alcohol for free tax circulation and is: importer of alcohol, alcohol producer in the Czech Republic or tax warehouse operator under the conditional exemption procedure, provided that personal and technical conditions are met.
Personal conditions – reliability, integrity and non-expression of the prohibition of activity – must be met by the applicant and the person in the position of statutory body or responsible representative.
Depending on the expected amount of control tapes taken, the applicant must be deposited between CZK 100,000 and CZK 5,000,000 (i.e. approximately €3,700 to €185,000).
The technical conditions for registration are a suitable place for marking alcohol and the equipment of the marking point or tax warehouse by a camera tracking device with continuous operation and remote access of the tax administrator.
The registration markings of the control tape are introduced for the marking of spirit drinks with a capacity greater than 0,06 litres.
When carrying control tapes, the registration marking of the control tapes shall be indicated in the transport documents or the customs declaration on export.
Control tape until 30. 11. 2013 contained a 10-digit registration code which included a four-digit registration sampling number, a check-tape application code and a classification code according to the level of ethanol concentration.
Control tape from 1. 12. 2013 now contains two types of identifiers and the quantity of alcohol in consumer packaging expressed in millilitres of ethanol at 20 °C, rounded down to whole millilitres.
The records of the control tapes for the marking of spirit drinks shall contain daily entries of the individual methods of handling the control tapes according to the registration codes, as well as the documents on the basis of which the registration took place.
In the event of the destruction, loss or theft of specific control tapes, the holder shall notify the tax administrator by electronic means of the registration code of the control tapes concerned and their number on the following working day after the relevant fact.
Introduction of a new factual offence and the adjustment of the level of penalties imposed for infringements of the legislation in the handling of control tapes.
Penalties may be imposed up to or up to 10 times the amount of excise duty (e.g. if the control tapes in excess of 0,1 % of the total quantity of the individual order of the control tapes are not returned, if the control tape is not returned within the legal deadline).
Restrictions on the handling of control tapes only to registered holders who may not pass them on to another person, except to provide them to a foreign supplier for the purpose of labelling spirit drinks in consumer packaging manufactured outside the Czech Republic.
The exported control tapes must be placed on consumer packaging and re-imported no later than nine months after receipt from the tax administrator.
Mandatory registration of the distributor of alcohol in consumer packaging provided that similar personal conditions are met as for the person obliged to mark alcohol and with the obligation to deposit up to CZK 5,000,000 (i.e. about €185,000).
Definition of persons for the sale or purchase of alcohol in consumer packaging.
Authorised persons are obliged to sell alcohol in consumer packaging to other registered persons or final sellers, or they may sell it as a final seller.
They may acquire alcohol from other registered persons, the insolvency practitioner, the administrative authority, the organizational units of the State or unregistered persons in the execution of tax enforcement.
Notices of placing alcohol or sale in consumer packaging for free tax circulation, holders and distributors of alcohol are obliged to send immediately the following day after the relevant fact to the tax administrator through an information system maintained by the tax administration (ORO web client) or in compliance with the content in xml format.
The notification shall contain the number of control tapes used, the volume and type of consumer packaging, the volume percentage of alcohol, the European commodity code (EAN), the identification of the distributor or final seller, as well as the name of the product and the lot of production.
In 2014 and 2015, tax entities sent about EUR 10.5 million. Notification.
Compulsory concession (a specific form of trade licence) not only for the production and modification of alcohol, but also for the sale of alcohol in consumer packaging by an entrepreneur to a natural person for his personal use or other legal or entrepreneurial natural person for his own internal use.
Concessional trades can be carried out only after a decision has been taken by the Trade Licensing Office in compliance with professional competence and other conditions.
No prescribed professional capacity is required for the sale of alcohol.
The benefit to tax authorities is an overview of sellers and their premises and
trading to reliable entities.
In the Czech Republic, approximately 94,000 people were registered for the industry including the production, treatment of fermented spirits, beverage alcohol, spirits and other alcoholic beverages and sales in 2014. and in 2015 approximately 104,000 Concessions.
Compliance with legislation in the field of the treatment of products subject to excise duties in the Czech Republic is also ensured by: trade offices, State Agricultural and Food Inspection Offices, Financial Administration bodies of the Czech Republic, Czech Trade Inspection Authorities.
If it finds that there has been an infringement or a breach of the prohibition, it shall inform the consumer tax authorities without delay.
Mineral oils
The Czech Republic has established a comprehensive system of supervision (see Annex 3, Scheme B), to which mineral oils subject to excise duties, but also selected mineral oils excise unencumruected, which have been misused for tax evasion.
The system includes supervision from the production of mineral oil through storage, transport, tagging and dyeing of selected mineral oils, marking of certain other mineral oils up to delivery to the end consumer or user and in some cases the consumption of mineral oils.
The supervision of the customs authorities also includes the production of marking agents for the marking and management of mineral oils.
The marking and dyeing of selected mineral oils shall be subject to mineral oils listed under combined nomenclature codes 2710 19 25 (other kerosene), 2710 19 29 (other not elsewhere specified medium oils) and heavy gas oils 2710 19 41, 2710 19 45 and 2710 19 49, unless their tagging is prohibited.
The marking of some other mineral oils is subject to e.g. benzol, toluene, xylol and lubricating oils and other oils intended for purposes other than motor drive.
Mark and color selected mineral oils and some other mineral oils with a marker substance is possible only by the permission of the tax administrator.
