The most significant new measures since 2012:
Monitoring of the management of special mineral oils, which is a group of mineral oils under combined nomenclature codes 2710 19 71 to 2710 19 99 (i.e. lubricating oils and other oils intended for purposes other than motor drive) whose kinematic viscosity at 40 °C is less than 12 mm2. s-1 inclusive and have at least one of the following characteristics: the flash point is less than 150 °C, at least 20 % of the volume, including losses up to 350 °C, shall be distilled during the distillation test.
These mineral oils were used as an admixture for finished fuels, in particular diesel, or were directly used or sold to drive engines, because the physical properties are very similar.
Entities handling the mineral oils monitored in bulk or in packages exceeding 220 litres must register with the tax administrator.
In order to issue the registration, the personal conditions of the applicant, the statutory body and the responsible representative must be fulfilled, which shall apply throughout 2 With the exception of beer, fruit wines, other wines and mead and fruit spirits obtained by burning.
(3) Council Regulation (EEC) No 2658/87 of 23 July 1987 on the common organisation of the market in agricultural products (3), as last amended by Regulation (EC) No 1255/2000(4), is to be incorporated into the Agreement They shall forthwith inform the Customs Authorities of the member state in which they are hereinto.
4 E.g. when mineral oil is used as fuel (except for water navigation, in the absence of private recreational craft) or as a fuel manufacturing component, if the marking is a defect in their use.
Registration.
As at 30 June 2004, the 11. 2016 the register of persons handling special mineral oils contained 54 valid registrations, four marketing authorisations were revoked on the proposal of the marketing authorisation holder.
The electronic records shall contain detailed information on the receipt, own consumption and sale or transfer of mineral oil, including document numbers, the number of the notice of acquisition to the tax authorities, the place of storage and consumption, the purpose of consumption, the place of storage and consumption or the place of delivery and the customer registration number.
Notice of any acquisition of special mineral oil shall be made to the tax authorities between 24 and 72 hours before receipt.
The identification of the business partners, the name and nomenclature of the special mineral oil, quantity, purpose of consumption or information on sales or transfer shall be notified.
The notification of the expected quantity in the relevant year of mineral oil acquired, sold or consumed shall be submitted by the body together with the registration application or by the end of January of the calendar year concerned.
Notifications of the purpose of use and marking, place of storage or consumption, the identification data of the person to whom the special mineral oil is ressuscitated or transferred shall be transmitted before any change.
Notifications shall be made electronically via smart forms or by a data box in PDFa format.
In 2015, people handling special mineral oils filed 630 notices.
The tax administrator must give a statement in cases where he finds the handling of special mineral oils without registration or when the registered person fails to comply with his notification obligation.
As in the case of non-compliance with obligations in the transport of products subject to excise duties, these deficiencies cannot be remedied retrospectively.
The registration of a fuel distributor is mandatory for persons who sell or are authorised to sell fuel.
Registered fuel distributors may only be persons meeting the following criteria:
Compulsory concession of the Trade Licensing Office (specific form of trade licence).
The opinion of the customs office examining whether the applicant for the concession, the statutory body or the members of the applicant's statutory body – legal persons and the appointed responsible representative – fulfil the condition of reliability shall give an opinion on the application for a concession or, where appropriate, on the provision of a responsible representative.
If these persons fulfil the condition of reliability, the customs office shall issue a consent opinion.
A reliable person means a person of integrity, in terms of criminal property nature, customs and tax law.
Professional competence is a condition for the issue of a concession.
Debt-freeness of the same circle of persons as in the case of reliability.
The debt-free person is a person who provides sufficient guarantees that he will properly and timely fulfil his payment obligations vis-à-vis the State, i.e. the member of the Commission. has no arrears to the state budget and general health insurance.
A fuel distributor shall not be prohibited by a court or administrative authority from carrying out his activity.
The fuel distributor must not be in liquidation or bankruptcy.
Deposit (or bank guarantee) of CZK 20,000,000 (i.e. about €740,000), which can be reduced to CZK 10,000,000 (i.e. about €370,000) after three years of registration of the fuel distributor and other conditions.
The distributor shall notify the customs office within 20 days after the end of the calendar month.
The electronic notification shall contain information on the individual purchase and sale of fuel.
The reported data are data on business partners, document numbers, selected product, quantity, price, carrier and transport, place of loading and unloading.
The right to a refund of the tax on mineral oils consumed in agricultural primary production was reintroduced at the end of 2014.
The application of excise duty on mineral oils may only be claimed for an activity which is manifestly related to the activity carried out on the land.
In 2015, it was about 64,000. refund claims totalling CZK 1,172,844,680 (i.e. €43,401,720).
Since 2017, the Government of the Czech Republic has also introduced the refund of excise duty on fuel to livestock farmers.
Farmers or breeders who, for example, are involved in the rearing of bovine animals, pigs, poultry, sheep and goats, will be able to make this claim.
Tobacco products
Restrictions on the sale of tobacco products with the old tax rate
In response to the long-term under-achieving of budgeted revenues from excise duty on tobacco products, the Czech Republic has introduced, with effect from 1 January 2005, a new regulation on the use of the product tax on tobacco products. 12. 2014 restrictions on the sale of tobacco products with the old tax rate in the event of a change in the tax rate.
Excise duty on tobacco products is paid by the use of tobacco stickers.
The use of a tobacco sticker means its placement on unit packaging (Section 116 of the Excise Duty Act).
For the application of the rate of excise duty, the decisive production of the tobacco product shall be in the condition intended for the final consumer, without the need for its collection, delivery, dispatch or sale, or sale to the final consumer.
The letter of the alphabet characterising the rate of excise duty is indicated on the tobacco sticker together with the price for the final consumer of cigarettes, the label shows the number of pieces in the package or the amount of tobacco to smoke in kilograms.
The tobacco label has no identifier.
The duration of the transitional period for the resale of unit packets of cigarettes intended for direct consumption and bearing a tobacco label with a previous (old) tax rate has been fixed until the end of the last day of the second calendar month following the effective of the new rate of excise duty.
The evolution of tobacco label removal in 2014 and the comparison with previous years shows that tobacco manufacturers have significantly out-of-stock tobacco products with an 'old' tax rate each year, thereby effectively shifting the effectiveness of the 'new' tax rate by about one year.
Tax on raw tobacco
Due to the misuse of raw tobacco for the manufacture of tobacco products without the authorisation of the tax authorities and the non-imposition of excise duty, a tax on raw tobacco and monitoring of the treatment of raw tobacco were introduced as a measure against tax fraud.
With effect from 1 January 2005, the 7. 2015, excise shall be subject to raw tobacco which has not been used or supplied for the manufacture of tobacco products, delivered to another Member State or third country or for which the origin, purpose of use or the person to whom the raw tobacco has been or is to be supplied has not been established.
Restrictions on the use of raw tobacco
Measures such as the supervision of the transport and manufacture of tobacco products, the labelling of unit packets with control tape and restrictions on sales at designated locations have been supplemented by restrictions on the loading of raw tobacco.
Production facilities for the processing of tobacco raw materials and the manufacture of tobacco products are not subject to supervision by the customs authorities.
Only a registered person may store raw tobacco for a purpose other than the manufacture of tobacco products, but such tobacco may not be further processed or modified.
Only a person meeting the personal conditions of the applicant, the statutory body and the responsible representative may be a registered person, which is valid throughout the registration period.
The conditions of registration are: (a) the right to operate a business allowing the activity of a person storing raw tobacco, b) reliability, c) debt-free, d) the fact that the person storing raw tobacco has not been granted a prohibition of activity preventing the pursuit of his activity, e) the fact that the person storing raw tobacco is not in liquidation or in bankruptcy, f) the provision of a security deposit of CZK 20,000,000 (i.e. approximately CZK 740,000).
Electronic records shall include the date of receipt or issue of raw tobacco, the number of the document, the identification of the business partner, the indication of the quantity and type of raw tobacco.
Notice of any acquisition of raw tobacco by a registered person storing raw tobacco shall be made to the tax authorities between 24 and 72 hours before receipt or dispatch.
The details of the business partner, the quantity of raw tobacco, the address of storage, the purpose of use and the particulars of the carrier shall be reported.
The notification of the expected quantity in the relevant year of raw tobacco received or dispatched shall be submitted by the body together with the registration application or by the end of January of the calendar year concerned.
Notifications are submitted electronically by a data box in PDFa format.
The transport of raw tobacco must be accompanied by a document with the prescribed requirements.
Legislation of excise duties in the Czech Technical Society
The legal framework regulating the field of excise duties in the SR is based on EU legislation, thereby co-creating its uniform tax system.
The various types of excise duties are exhaustively determined by the legislation of the Czech Technical Party, which is similar to the legislation of the surrounding countries.
Definition of legislation in the Czech Customs Code
Four laws are secured by the legislation on the individual subjects of the tax.
Harmonisation was achieved by the adoption of the following excise laws: Act No. 98/2004 Z. z., on excise duty on mineral oils, Act No. 106/2004 Z. z., on excise duty on tobacco products, Act No. 530/2011 Z. z., excise duty on alcoholic beverages, Act No. 609/2007 Z. z., on excise duties on electricity, coal and natural gas.
All excise laws are substantive law and deal with the taxation of the subject of excise duties in the tax territory.
Act No. 563/2009 Z. z., on tax administration (tax code), is a regulation of procedural law, regulates the administration of taxes, the law and obligations of tax entities and other persons.
This legal framework transposed the individual provisions of Council Directive 2008/118/EC of 16 December 2008 on the protection of individuals with a view to the placing on the market of certain agricultural products [3], as last amended by Directive 2008/118/EC [2], the commission has been granted a directive on the protection of the european communities. It is therefore for the purposes of implementing the provisions of Directive 92/12/EEC.
Structure of legislative changes for individual types of excise duties in relation to the subject of control in the SR
Since 2011, legislation on the administration of excise duties has undergone several major changes according to the structure of individual excise duties.
In the EMCS system, the monitoring of the transport of selected products subject to excise duty under the suspensive exemption regime has been changed from a paper accompanying administrative document to an exclusively electronic system where such services are monitored in real time.
Under the EMCS electronic system, a suspension of access to EMCS was introduced in 2015.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
The customs office shall have the possibility to suspend access precisely on the justified concern of the undepayable or undetermined tax on previous tax years and its unenforceability.
This concerns the maturity of the tax, since the transport of excise goods requires the composition of the collateral, which is released by the termination of transport.
Excise duty on mineral oils
A major change in the management of excise duty on mineral oils occurred in 2011, when the possibility of using the so-called 'mineral oil tax' was abolished. red diesel.
The labeled gas oil, commonly called red diesel, was one of the mineral oils.
In the past, red diesel has been used for specific legally defined purposes, e.g. for the use of the fuel. in agriculture, and its use was favoured by a lower rate of excise duty.
This change had a positive impact on the revenue portion of the state budget.
The abolition of red diesel was aimed at reducing the public deficit, simplifying the system of taxing mineral oils and reducing the administrative burden on the business entities concerned.
In 2012, a new type of tax entity was created, namely a fuel dealer.
The purpose of this statutory amendment was to introduce a record-keeping obligation for all petrol stations.
The errification of the movement of taxed petrol and diesel is linked to the obligation to purchase petrol and diesel from a fuel distributor.
In 2014, new institutes of tax entities were introduced, namely the fuel distributor and the fuel consumer.
This change has contributed to the elimination of tax evasion in petrol and diesel and has made the movement of these fuels more clear (see Annex 4, Scheme A).
As part of the fight against tax evasion, the statutory provisions on the registration of tax entities trading in lubricating and base oils have been extended.
However, in the SR, these mineral oils are not subject to the obligation to label with an indication substance.
Excise duty on tobacco products
In the fight against tax evasion and monitoring of tobacco raw materials, the scope of the Tobacco Raw Material Act has been extended and a new tax entity – a tobacco trader – has been introduced.
Tobacco raw material is not a harmonised tobacco product and its movement is not monitored within the EU.
Furthermore, the obligation to register technological equipment for the production of tobacco products was introduced.
The legislation introduced a new system of ordering, assessing, printing, distributing and using control marks for the labelling of consumer packaging of tobacco products.
The check mark is cigarettes, cigars, cigarillos and tobacco.
Under the new system, the customer of the control marks must apply to the customs office for the issue of the inspection marks electronically, by means of an information system for the collection of the inspection marks.
This step introduced electronic communication between the tax entity and the tax administrator.
One state stamp printer was set up – in the Kremnica Mint.
The exercise of tax supervision over the printing of stamps was also introduced.
The changes have contributed significantly to the elimination of tax evasion.
The new system for printing control marks strengthens the system of checking goods, because a unique identification number is generated on the control mark, which can be used to easily verify whether the goods come from legal sources.
A unique 12-digit identification number (1-2nd place shall be the checksum; 3. the place determines whether the code belongs to a control mark or a group of packages; 4. the place is the identifier of the series; 5.–8. space is the alphanumeric part of the sequence; 9.–12. instead of the decimal part of the sequence) can also be applied in the form of a two-dimensional barcode.
The control mark for the labelling of cigarettes shall also indicate the price of cigarettes, the stamp for the validity of the excise duty rate, the number of cigarettes in the consumer pack and the length of the cigarettes.
Excise duty on alcoholic beverages
The biggest legislative change affected alcohol, wine and beer, because the original three substantive law regulations were repealed and a common law on excise duty on alcoholic beverages was created.
The law was drawn up mainly because of the need for a comprehensive solution to the issue of the taxation of alcoholic beverages, the solution of their production, the monitoring of movement, the security of tax, as well as the need to improve the business environment in the field, to streamline the performance of tax administration, to reduce the administrative burden for SMEs.
A new way of addressing the taxation of individual types of alcoholic beverages introduced the application of a uniform rate of excise duty to an alcoholic beverage and took into account the percentage of actual alcoholic strength.
For non-sparkling wine, sparkling wine and fermented beverages, the volume percentage of the actual alcoholic strength of the final product shall be taken into account.
The concentration of beer is also expressed as a percentage of the actual alcoholic strength in the finished product.
A category of small-scale fermented beverages has been introduced, the essence of which is the exemption from excise duty for a natural person who produces a fizzy fermented drink for his own consumption and for the consumption of his household not more than 1 000 litres per marketing year.
The legislation introduced a new system of ordering, assessing, printing, distribution and use of control marks intended for the labelling of consumer packaging of alcohol.
Under the new system, the customer of the control marks must apply to the customs office for the issue of the inspection marks electronically, by means of an information system for the collection of the inspection marks.
This step introduced electronic communication between the tax entity and the tax administrator.
One state stamp printer was set up – in the Kremnica Mint.
The exercise of tax supervision over the printing of stamps was also introduced.
The changes have contributed significantly to the elimination of tax evasion (see Annex 4, Scheme B) and the elimination of falsification of control marks.
The new system for printing control marks strengthens the system of checking goods, because a unique identification number is generated on the control mark, which can be used to easily verify whether the goods come from legal sources.
A unique 12-digit identification number (1-2nd place shall be the checksum; 3. the place determines whether the code belongs to a control mark or a group of packages; 4. the place is the identifier of the series; 5.–8. space is the alphanumeric part of the sequence; 9.–12. instead of the decimal part of the sequence) can also be applied in the form of a two-dimensional barcode.
Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
Excise duties on alcohol, mineral oils, tobacco products, beer, wine and intermediate products are regulated in the Czech Republic by one common law No. 353/2003 Coll.
The fixed fuel tax, the tax on natural gas and some other gases and the electricity tax are part of Act No. 261/2007 Coll.
In contrast, in the SR, each excise duty is regulated by a special law, except for the Excise Act on alcoholic beverages, which includes a tax on alcohol, beer, wine and intermediate products.
A special law regulates excise duty on electricity, coal and natural gas.
In the Czech Republic, from 1. 1. 2015, the issue of an authorisation for the handling of products subject to excise duty under the Excise Tax Act shall be subject to, inter alia, proof of the economic stability of applicants, which the customs authorities verify annually by carrying out a financial analysis.
In the SR, a similar form of analysis is carried out only when deciding to waive or reduce tax collateral.
FŘ SR carries out tax supervision in the form of the presence of an employee of the Financial Directorate over the handling of control marks for the marking of alcohol and tobacco products, their disposal in the printer and their sale to individual customers.
The law provides that the production of control marks is carried out by the state company Mint Kremnica.
The production of tobacco stickers and control tapes in the Czech Republic does not have the supervision of customs authorities in the printer.
Tobacco stickers and control tapes will be taken from the printer by the designated territorial office of the customs office in Kutná Hora.
Tobacco stickers are taken over by their customers at this territorial site, the alcohol marking tapes are further distributed to individual locally competent tax authorities according to the place of marking.
The legislation of the Czech Republic does not define the manufacturer of tobacco stickers and control tapes.
In The Czech Republic there is an obligation to register technological equipment for the production of tobacco products or part thereof, in the Czech Republic such an obligation is not introduced.
In the Czech Republic, the tobacco label bears an excise duty on tobacco products, which is paid at the time of collection of tobacco stickers at the authorized customs office.
On the other hand, the control mark does not contain excise duty on tobacco products.
In the Czech Republic, a refund of excise duty on mineral oils was introduced during the controlled period in case of their use for agricultural plant primary production, the so-called "mineral oil tax". green diesel.
Since 2017, this tax refund has also been extended to livestock production.
In the SR, such support for farmers is not in place (it existed until 31 December 2004). 12. 2010 as the so-called red diesel).
In order to strengthen the fight against tax fraud, a deposit of EUR 20 million was introduced for fuel distributors in the Czech Republic. czk (i.e. €740,000).
As a result of the introduction of this measure, the number of fuel distributors decreased from 1 891 entities in 2013 to 174 in 2014 (i.e. a decrease of 1 717 tax entities).
In The Czech Technical University, a similar fuel distributor institute is established, but without the deposit required to secure the excise duty on mineral oils.
In 2014, 303 distributors were registered in the Czech Germany and 407 distributors were registered in 2015.
In the SR, an institute of the seller of fuels and the consumer of fuels is established, to which the local customs office issues authorisations.
In the Czech Republic, such an institute is not established.
In the Czech Republic, the markings of selected mineral oils and also some other mineral oils are subject to the abolition of the so-called mineral oils. red diesel, mineral oil labelling is not applied.
In the Czech Republic, the alcohol marking control tape contains an eight-digit individual code used to verify the origin of alcohol and a 12-digit registration code indicating the spiritity of the spirit drink, according to which the records of the control tapes are kept.
The destruction, loss, and return of the control tape are entered in the registry on the following working day.
The holder of the tape is obliged to notify their use within the same period.
In the SR, a control mark intended for the marking of alcohol in consumer packaging contains a unique 12-digit identification number which, if used once a month, is communicated to the tax authorities and is used to verify the authenticity of the inspection mark.
The register contains the number of stamps collected, used and claimed.
Both the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic have established a mandatory registration institute or the registration of a spirit distributor.
In the SR, the registration is subject to the fulfilment of conditions relating, inter alia, to a storage area exceeding 200 m2; annual turnover from the sale of consumer packaging of alcohol of at least €100 000 or paid-up capital of at least €100 000; minimum number of 10 employees.
In the Czech Republic, obtaining registration is conditional, inter alia, on the deposit of CZK 5,000,000 (i.e. €185,000) in favour of the tax administrator for the entire period of validity of the registration.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
In the SR, the production of alcohol not only in consumer packaging requires the permanent presence of the tax administrator.
In the Czech Republic, a special form of registration of a person obliged to mark alcohol is required for the production of alcohol in the Czech Republic, subject to the condition of depositing a deposit in favour of the tax administrator in the amount of CZK 100,000 (i.e. 3,700 €) up to CZK 5,000,000 (i.e. 185,000 €) according to the amount of control tapes taken and the tracking device with continuous access by the tax administrator.
Evaluation
The legislation of the Czech Republic and The Czech Republic and the Czech Republic goes well beyond the EU minimum requirements for the subject and administration of excise duties and responds to identified risks from other Member States as well as to risks identified in tax territories.
Legislative changes adopted during the audited period allow tax authorities to prevent possible tax evasion to a greater extent.
In the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic, an excise duty on raw tobacco or tobacco raw materials has been introduced in addition to EU legislation in the fight against tax evasion in the form of misuse of tobacco raw materials (e.g. leaves).
Although raw tobacco and tobacco raw material are not a harmonised tobacco product, both the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic monitor their movement.
The SAO CR and the SAO SR may recommend that this measure be applied in other EU Member States.
In the Czech Republic, good practice has shown that the examination of economic stability for applicants for authorisation under the Excise Tax Act has proven itself because it reduces the risk of tax arrears.
For this reason, both audit institutions recommend applying such screening also under the conditions of the SR.
The distribution of control marks is more efficient in the Czech Republic than in the Czech Republic because it does not burden the customs authorities with the costs of transport between the printer and the customer of the control tapes and tobacco stickers.
The Financial Administration of the Czech Technical System has a better overview of the existence and location of technological equipment for the production of tobacco products.
In the Czech Republic, however, the collection of the tax on tobacco products is more effective, because the tobacco label order itself is a tax return followed by payment of the tax.
Thanks to the introduction of the institutes "fuel dealer" and "fuel consumer", the financial administration in the Czech Customs has a better overview of the places of sale of fuels.
The introduction of mandatory labelling of mineral oils in the Czech Republic makes it easier to control the misuse of mineral oils with a reduced tax rate or tax-exempt.
In the Czech Republic (2013) and in SR (2014) a new control tape was introduced, respectively, a mark containing an identification code.
The control tape in the Czech Republic also contains a registration code, while in the Czech Republic the new legislation has dropped its introduction.
The impacts cannot yet be assessed due to the short effectiveness of legislative changes.
The introduction of effective labelling of consumer packaging of alcohol by a check mark or tape is an effective measure in the fight against tax evasion.
The SAO SR and the SAO CR may recommend the introduction of this control measure also in other Member States.
The SR's position on the conditions for the distribution of alcohol is characterised by a pro-client approach that does not block the funds of tax entities.
On the other hand, the Czech Republic's approach is rather restrictive because it introduces bail-burdening cash flow of tax entities, but it reduces the risk of tax arrears.
Evolution of excise tax revenues
Excise duty is an indirect tax introduced by the State in order to increase the revenue of the state budget and also to regulate the quantity of goods sold, the consumption of which is considered harmful to individuals and/or to society (regulatory function of the tax).
According to the Commission Communication: EUROPE 2020 – A strategy for smart, sustainable and inclusive growth of 3.12.2008, the European Commission has adopted a proposal for a directive on smart, sustainable and inclusive growth. 3. 2010 under the resource-intensive Europe flagship initiative, the European Commission intends to improve the framework for the use of market-based instruments, inter alia, in the context of the European Commission's decision to improve the use of instruments on the basis of market, inter alia, the european commission' energy taxation revision, with a focus on reducing energy and resource consumption.
In order to fulfil the EC's intention, Member States should seek to shift the tax burden from the workforce to, inter alia, energy and environmental taxation as part of the greater "greenness" of tax systems.
The collection of tax revenues from excise duties in the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic includes collection of excise duties on mineral oils, tobacco products, alcohol, beer, wine and intermediate products, as well as natural gas, solid fuels and electricity.
The share of excise duties in total tax revenues and the share of GDP is tracked, inter alia, by the percentage of excise duties in the total tax revenues. (i) the Organisation for Economic Cooperation and Development (OECD).
Both Supreme Audit Institutions used the following selection criteria to query the OECD website.
Collection of excise duties in relation to macroeconomic indicators in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, the share of excise duties in total tax revenues and the share of GDP decreased slightly according to OECD data.
For the conversion of amounts in CZK to € as at 31 December 2004, the amount of the amount in czk is to be converted into 12. the ecb's exchange rate was used in the relevant year.
The nominal exchange rate of CZK against € in 2013 decreased by 9.1% year-on-year (from 25,140 to 27,425) in 2012.
This was mainly due to the monetary policy decision of the CNB Bank Board of 7 December 2004. 20136.
The resulting values of excise collection, excise duty rates and per capita income in € decreased significantly due to the exchange rate difference.
The significant reduction in the share of excise duties in 2014 was due to a one-off drop in excise tax revenues on tobacco products due to the impact of new legislation restricting the sale of old-priced tobacco products.
The share of excise duties is also influenced by the increase in income tax collection, which has increased significantly as a result of the improved overall economic situation of the Czech Republic.
The total collection of excise duties has the largest share of the excise duty on mineral oils (about 55.7% in 2015), but this has fallen despite the significant growth of the economy since 2012.
The collection of excise duties on mineral oils in 2013 and 2014 was significantly lower than in 2012 and 2015, although the registration of fuel distributors was introduced as anti-tax fraud measures in 2013.
The trend of eco-efficient vehicles and the promotion of biofuels are negatively reflected in the tax revenue.
A negligible share is the gas tax, the fixed fuel tax and the electricity tax, which is due to the low tax rate, which is close to the minimum rates set by the EU, compared to the surrounding states.
In the absence of a rate increase, their share will fall in the future in view of the ever-decreasing energy performance of buildings and production processes.
The collection of excise duty on alcohol in 2013 and 2014 was negatively affected by the reverberations of a large-scale case of tax fraud consisting in the placing in circulation of un taxed alcohol, 100 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 0000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000 000
In 2015, following the adoption of a series of measures against such action and the recovery of the spirits market, the recovery of excise duty on alcohol exceeded 4 million in 2012. €.
The share of the tobacco tax has increased as a result of rising rates.
The basic rates of excise duty changed between 2012 and 2015 for tobacco tax, where the rate was increased mainly due to compliance with Council Directive 2011/64/EU, on the structure and rates of excise duty on tobacco products.
As a result of the CNB's monetary intervention, the real rate of excise duties in €, excluding the tobacco tax, decreased significantly. For tobacco products, it rose only slightly.
In relation to price growth, GDP or living standards, the indexation of the excise rate is not set, so the functions of excise duties consisting in regulating socially problematic activities may not be fulfilled.
With the economic growth of the Czech Republic and the rise in living standards, real rates of excise duties are reduced.
7 Indexation – automatic adjustment of a certain economic quantity to inflation, this adjustment takes place on the basis of a law or contract (for pensions paid by the State is called valorisation).
Collection of excise duties in relation to macroeconomic indicators in the SR
The current legislative regulation of excise duties in the SR does not address the indexation of excise duty rates on the evolution of consumer prices because they are fixed.

Of all the excise duties introduced in Slovakia, the excise duty on mineral oils has the largest share of the state budget's tax revenues, with its share not falling below 52% throughout the audited period.
Excise duty on tobacco products accounts for the second largest share.
This tax accounts for an average of approximately 32% of the total collection of excise duties.
Between 2012 and 2015, the collection of excise duty per capita of the SR increased.
This development is due to an increase in excise duty rates on tobacco products, higher purchasing capacity and higher consumption of the population in a given year.
The increase in collection of excise duties per capita of the SR is constant and corresponds to the development of excise duty rates on tobacco products, higher purchasing capacity and higher consumption of the population in a given year.
In the Czech Republic, the decrease in income in € per capita is influenced by the CNB's intervention in relation to the exchange rate of the crown against the euro.
The difference between the Czech Republic and The Czech Republic in the total collection from the SPD is mainly due to the collection of excise duty on mineral oils and tobacco products, which is approximately 2.7 times or 2.8 times higher in the Czech Republic, but per inhabitant of the Czech Republic the collection for these selected products is only about 1/3.
This is due to the lower price of these selected products in the Czech Republic due to lower rates of excise duties in the Czech Republic and the exchange rate of CZK against € for foreign consumers.
The mineral oil tax also causes greater transit through the Czech Republic and cross-border purchases.
In the case of a tax on tobacco products, increasing foreign tourism to the Czech Republic and cross-border purchases has a significant impact.
The evaluation of the real rate of excise duties in the Czech Republic decreased as a result of cnb interventions.
The share of energy taxes in the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic in total tax revenues does not increase and there is no shift away from labour taxation to the taxation of consumption of selected products subject to excise duties, which is not in line with EU strategies.
However, the value achieved by the share of excise duties is consistently above average compared to the OECD average.
The overall collection of excise duties is mainly influenced by the change in excise duty rates, the development of economic condition and the behaviour of the population.
Future blackouts in the collection of excise duties due to environmental measures subsidised by the State in various forms will need to be replaced by other revenue or by reducing state expenditure.
The absence of indexation of excise duty rates in the Czech Republic and the SR reduces their regulatory functions and is insufficiently supported by eu objectives based on a Europe less dependent on environmentally-friendly sources and in reducing dependence on alcohol and tobacco.
Higher collection of excise duty per capita in the Czech Republic shows higher consumption of selected products by foreign consumers, which is influenced by the lower total price of selected products in €.
Administrative expenditure of excise duties
The effectiveness of administrative costs reflects the correlation between expenditure and revenue related to the management of excise duties, i.e. the cost of the project. 100 units of revenue (CZK, €).
The higher the resulting value, the worse the efficiency of administrative costs.
The effectiveness of the tax administrator in tax administration affects the scope and organization of the tax administrator, the management of the organization, the legal environment and the level of electronization of individual activities.
The determination of the efficiency of administrative costs of tax administration by the conversion factor is based on the number of employees involved in the management of excise duties in a line-driven structure.
In the Czech Republic, the administration of excise duties is carried out in addition to other activities by the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, which is a separate organizational unit of the state and the entity.
In the Slovak Republic, the tax administration of the Slovak Republic is provided by the Financial Administration of the Slovak Republic, whereby the customs authorities are the internal organizational unit, the costs and revenues are included in aggregate for the whole organizational unit.
Therefore, with regard to the possibility of comparing the efficiency of the administration of excise duties in the calculation of the efficiency of administrative costs, the expenditure and revenue of the Financial Administration of the Czech Republic were also included.
Administrative costs of excise tax administration in the Czech Republic
The administration of excise duties is a complex of administrative acts, which is carried out mainly by the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic.
Some partial control tasks are carried out by other public authorities, but their significance is negligible.
In particular, the following departments carry out the administration of excise duties:
Directorate-General for Customs

Unit 233 – Tax controls methodically manage and coordinate the execution of the tax control agenda at customs offices;

Department 302 – Administrative activities carry out decision-making activities where the legislation provides for the competence of DGC, e.g. decision on the delegation of the entity's territorial jurisdiction to another tax administrator in substance, decision-making on the attraction, i.e. the taxable person concerned; taking the matter over to the superior tax administrator, appealing against decisions of the customs authorities and examining complaints of inaction in tax and administrative proceedings;
Unit 303 – Revenue and Enforcement Management methodically manages, coordinates and performs tasks in the framework of international cooperation in the recovery of tax arrears and the performance of insolvency tasks;
