EMCS system
Pursuant to the preamble to Decision No 1152/2003/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16 December 2003 on the protection of the european communities's products[2', the Commission has decided to initiate the procedure laid down in Article 88(2) of the EC In order to ensure that the transport of goods is carried out in the context of the use of the goods in the community, the aim of the introduction of an electronic system for monitoring the transport of selected products was to enable real-time information on the transport of the products to be obtained and the prescribed checks carried out, to simplify the movement of goods within the Community under the excise duty suspension procedure.
When implementing the system, Member States should have allowed economic operators, in particular SMEs active in the sector, to use these national elements at the lowest possible cost.
Article 3 of that Decision allows the inclusion of national specifications, national databases forming part of the system and such technical or software equipment as the Member State deems necessary to ensure the full use of the system within its administration.
EMCS in the Czech Republic
EMCS Development and Functionality
In the Czech Republic, the EMCS system was preceded by the System of Registering Selected Products (EVV), which was operated from May 2004 to the end of March 2010.
EMCS is fully operational in the Czech Republic from 1. 4. 2010 and is continuously supplemented by European and national functionalities (see Annex 5).
In the Czech Republic, the so-called customs module and declarant module.
The customs module contains a number of national functionalities.
In addition to the Community system, shipments under the conditional exemption regime initiated and terminated in the Czech Republic are monitored in the EMCS system.
The system shall ensure, after approval of the notification of receipt of the consignment intended for the authorised consignee for the one-time acceptance of the automatic sending of the information to the register of tax entities, followed by the invalidation of the authorisation.
The system fully ensures the administration of received and submitted requests for international cooperation and spontaneous information from ELO, including the sending of responses with an attachment in any format and ensuring translations.
It is also possible to receive a report on manual cessation of exports in the ECS (only the referral of an automatically created message is implemented in the EU).
Risk profiles for outgoing or incoming shipments are set according to the currently required criteria.
The EMCS system will not allow the approval of e-AD or notification of receipt without the reaction of the competent customs authority to the risk profile (the risk profile cannot be ignored).
The declarant module is available to tax entities free of charge, it takes the form of a web application into which the user logs in with a username and password (coordinates) assigned to him after registration with CS CR.
Any action against the EMCS customs module shall bear a valid electronic signature in the declarant module of the EMCS.
The declarant module allows tax entities to directly record data on commenced and completed services under the suspensive exemption scheme, so that tax entities do not have to spend funds to acquire the system.
The national functionalities of the declarant module allow you to retrieve and store data offline (saves time on frequently used data), fill in recipient data based on seed ID checks and require mandatory filling of data that is optional at EU level (maximum data for risk analysis).
The system also allows for the payment of each shipment sent from the Czech Republic in real time to block the provision of excise duty in the appropriate amount of taxable supplies until the end of transport.
The amount of collateral is calculated automatically by the EMCS system.
Without sufficient collateral, the EMCS declarant module is not allowed to submit the e-AD proposal for approval to the CA.
Each warranty has a unique number and includes arc transport (including the above blocked lock) for which it was used.
The tax entity can manage its guarantees directly in the EMCS declarant module, where it sees the current amount of blocked and unblocked excise guarantees.
Expenditure on the introduction and use of EMCS
The development of EMCS was carried out on the basis of eight contracts with performance from 2006 to 2017 totalling CZK 46,791,924.60 (i.e. €1,761,412.56) excluding VAT.
In accordance with the concluded contracts, the contractor issued invoices for a total amount of CZK 43,577,255.19 (i.e. €1,640,401.10) excluding VAT from 2006 to the end of 2015.
In the audited period, expenses of CZK 14,545,454 excluding VAT (i.e. €547,438.99) were spent on the EMCS upgrade.
The amount spent on the upgrade of the EMCS in the audited period and converted into one transport entered into the EMCS is on average CZK 16.49 (i.e. €0.62), excluding national transport, the expenditure in the amount of one transport between the Czech Republic and the EU Member States is CZK 24.40 (i.e. €0.92).
EMCS technical support was implemented on the basis of four contracts with performance from 2011 to 2017.
By the end of 2015, the total amount of technical support of CZK 7,499,675 (i.e. €281,389.77) was invoiced, including value added tax.
The average amount of technical support spent since 2011 on one transport entered into the EMCS since 2010 is CZK 6.18 (i.e. €0.23).
The development invoices and technical support related to the national solution and the development of the EVV application, which was already operated by DGC prior to the EMCS system itself.
Invoices were paid under programme funding from national sources.
Technical support is invoiced as part of the supply of services to other applications provided by the supplier for the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic.
EMCS in SR
The EMCS is an electronic system operated by EU Member States to monitor the movement of excise goods between Member States under the suspensive procedure.
It replaced the accompanying administrative document – SAD, which was used before the effectiveness of this system, thus ensuring better control and management of transport.
In SR is introduced from 1. 4. 2010 and is continuously supplemented with requirements under EU legislation.
A unique reference code is generated for each transport, called a reference code.
ARC code under which it is possible to monitor the traffic online, i.e. in real time.
EMCS Development and Functionality
The EMCS system ensures the receipt and dispatch of excise goods only by tax entities authorised to use the EMCS system, thus greatly reducing the risk of tax evasion.
The greatest development of functionalities occurred in 2011, when the EMCS system was fully operational (see Annex 6).
Expenditure on the introduction and use of EMCS
The introduction of the EMCS system was implemented as an additional module of sysned application equipment and therefore it is not possible to determine precisely on the Slovak side the amount of the cost of its initial application.
Comparison and evaluation
Comparison
The aim of the EMCS was to replace the system based on the administration of transport in paper form.
The benefits of the EMCS system are a comprehensive overview of transport between Member States within the EU from notification of the start of transport to its completion – a reduction in administrative costs for tax authorities and tax entities for the processing, transmission and archiving of documents is important.
In the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic, a national functionality was introduced into the EMCS system allowing monitoring of traffic in a conditional system between two points in the Czech Republic or in the Slovak Republic.
In addition, automatic functionality of online monitoring and provision of a guarantee for excise duty is applied in the Czech Republic.
A national functionality is also established, which monitors the riskiness of the tax entity or transport, followed by a mandatory response from the tax administrator.
The Slovak Republic and the Czech Republic register a comparable number of transports within the EU in the EMCS system.
However, the expenditure incurred in the SR to upgrade this system was €744,310.01 higher between 2012 and 2015 than in the Czech Republic.
The SAO SR obtained data on the emcs upgrade from the FŘ only for the period from 2011, although this system was introduced and operated earlier.
Nevertheless, the expenses incurred to upgrade the EMCS system in the SR were €188,134.44 higher than the cost of introducing and upgrading the EMCS system in about ten years of operation in the Czech Republic.
Evaluation
For the controlled period, the amount of expenses related to the upgrade of the EMCS system in the SR in the amount of one transport exceeds 2.3 times the expenditure of the same type in the Czech Republic.
Conclusion
The cooperation of the SAO CR and the SAO SR met the objectives.
Both control institutions gained a deeper knowledge of the excise tax management system in the Czech Republic and The Czech Republic.
It was found that, despite the common basic legal framework, there are significant differences in both tax systems that affect the efficiency of the management of excise duties.
During parallel checks, examples of good practice have been identified that could contribute to reducing tax fraud, and their importance will increase with rising tax rates.
Procedures to reduce the cost of excise duty management have also been identified.
Mutual cooperation has revealed differences that significantly affect the efficiency of tax administration and limit international comparisons unless coordinated due diligence is carried out with the tax administrator.
In this, the role of supreme audit institutions is irreplaceable.
Report on the results of the parallel control of value added tax administration carried out in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany
Introductory word
The 1977 Lima Declaration stresses that the Supreme Audit Institutions (SAI) have the power to audit all public financial operations.
The declaration calls for tax receipts to be checked to the fullest extent possible.
The European Organisation of Supreme Audit Institutions (EUROSAI) considers tax to be one of the most important components of public revenue.
The EUROSAI VI Congress held in Bonn in 2005 dealt with the audit of public revenues carried out by the SAI.
A specific strategy for the audit of public revenues is an important step towards optimising the control activities of the SAI.
This concerns, in particular, taxes as the most large source of public revenue, which is most prone to large losses.
As national economies are increasingly interconnected and dependent, SAIs may, to some extent, be unable to carry out control activities without cooperation with another State's SAI.
An example is the audit of internationally organised fraud, which causes substantial losses in the income of many countries.
In order to combat this crime, responsible authorities need to cooperate with each other.
SAIs carrying out checks in this area must be willing to establish closer cooperation with each other.
Just on VI. The eurosai congress in Bonn was the idea of carrying out a review of the administration of value added tax (hereinafter referred to as "VAT") and the VIES system in the framework of cooperation between the Supreme Audit Office and the Federal Court of Auditors, the Bundesrechnungshof.
Careful preparation followed, with both parties first having to familiarize themselves with the legal environment and procedures for vat management in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany.
On the basis of an analysis of this information, a selection of control topics was carried out which was included in the control programme.
Achieving effective and efficient VAT governance is a long-term problem, and individual states (in particular the Member States of the European Union) are looking for solutions to improve, simplify and make the collection of vat more transparent.
We believe that the results of our inspection can serve not only to improve the work of tax administrators, but also as a basis for the proposal to improve the system of international information exchange.
Report on the results of parallel value added tax management checks carried out in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany
Introduction
Check number: (CZ) 06/27 (D) VIII 2 – 2005 – 1215
Subject of inspection:
(CZ) Administration of value added tax after the Czech Republic's accession to the European Union
(D) Verification of administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 and Commission Regulation (EC) No 1925/2004
Objective of the inspection:
(CZ) The aim of the control action in the Czech Republic was to examine the procedure of financial authorities in the administration of value added tax following the integration of the Czech Republic into the single internal market of the European Union (hereinafter referred to as "the EU") linked to the free movement of goods and services and to examine the use of the VIES system, in particular when checking the application of the right to value added tax exemption for intra-Community supplies.
(D) The aim of the inspection was to examine the system of control of intra-Community value added tax, with a particular focus on administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax under the abovementioned Regulations.
The result should be a report on weaknesses and recommendations for their elimination.
The System for the Exchange of Information on Value Added Tax Control Actions was carried out by the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic ('the SAO') and the German Bundesrechnungshof ('BRH') in cooperation on the basis of a contract concluded between the two supervisory institutions on 8 December 2004. They shall forthwith inform the
The cooperation focused mainly on the examination of selected commercial transactions carried out between payers from the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the "Czech Republic") and the Federal Republic of Germany (hereinafter referred to as "Germany"), the use of information obtained in the form of international cooperation between tax administrations and the comparison of vat management systems between the two countries.
The joint final report on the results of the control actions was prepared within the meaning of European Directive No 31 for the implementation of INTOSAI audit standards.
The period audited was from 1 January 2004 to 31 December 2005. 5. 2004 to 31 December 2004 12. 2005.
Summary of results and evaluation of parallel control actions
The parallel control in the field of VAT administration in the Czech Republic and Germany was carried out on the basis of a contract between the two SAI.
Outside the main point – the exchange of information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 and Commission Regulation (EC) No 1925/2004 – the control covered other topics, such as the registration of payers, VAT returns and summary reports, which are closely linked to the main point.
In addition, the control included the legal situation in the field of international bus passenger transport and the comparison of some statistical data.
By comparing the VAT management systems of the two countries, there were differences in the following areas:
1) VAT registration.
While in Germany entrepreneurs are registered regardless of the amount of their turnover, in the Czech Republic the primary criterion (among others) for registration is the exceeding of the limit set out in the VAT Act.
In the Czech Republic, only one tax identification number is assigned to the payers, which they also use in intra-Community transactions.
In Germany, the payers are assigned a tax number when registering for VAT, serving only for commercial transactions in the territory of Germany.
If the German payer intends to carry out intra-Community transactions, he must request the allocation of a special identification number, the so-called 'intra-Community transaction'. VAT ID.
As different registration methods cause problems, conditions should be levelled across the EU (see 4.1).
2) International bus passenger transport.
In the Czech Republic, international bus passenger transport is exempt from VAT with the right to deduct VAT.
In Germany, the part of the transport which takes place on German territory is subject to VAT.
Efforts should be made at EU level to harmonise the situation within the meaning of Article 393 of Council Directive 2006/112/EC on the common system of VAT (see 4.2)
3) VAT returns.
While in the Czech Republic payers only submit VAT returns for a single tax year (month or quarter), in Germany, the payers are obliged to submit so-called vat returns. provisional VAT returns (monthly or quarterly) and after the end of the calendar year they must file an annual VAT return.
Unlike czech payers, payers in Germany are obliged to submit preliminary tax returns electronically.
The introduction of the obligation to file VAT returns electronically in the Czech Republic would increase the efficiency of the Czech tax administration (see 4.3).
4) Summary reports.
While in the Czech Republic, payers report to the tax offices, in Germany, the payers submit summary reports to CLO.
Therefore, the tax authorities in the Czech Republic have data from summary reports available immediately after their submission.
German tax authorities have information from summary reports available only after their processing at CLO.
Combating VAT fraud requires that updated information on intra-Community transactions be available as soon as possible.
Monthly recapitulative reports would reduce the time shift between the date of the transaction and the update of data in VIES.
This would subsequently allow for a timely examination of taxation in the Member State of the acquirer (see 4.4).
Which would, however, require all Member States to adopt the same deadline for submitting a recapitulative statement.
5) International exchange of VAT information.
The Czech CUSTOMS monitors compliance with the three-month period for requests for information received.
German CLO does not track the elapsed time.
As a result, the German tax authorities dealt with a significantly lower percentage of the applications received within the deadline.
Because of these problems, BRH recommended that the German CLO carry out a permanent alert (see 4.6).
(6) Risk management system.
Each of the two Member States develops its own risk management system, hereinafter referred to as "RMS", which has its strengths and weaknesses.
The SAO and BRH point out that an effective RMS cannot be developed by only one Member State.
Successful RMS criteria, components and approaches must be exchanged and implemented in each EU Member State, otherwise fraudsters will choose the Member State with the weakest RMS (see 5.).
As part of the cooperation, both SAI examined selected cases of intra-community transactions carried out between tax entities from the Czech Republic and Germany.
Together, thirty-one cases of commercial transactions in which there were doubts as to their implementation or suspected VAT evasion were examined using the clo legislation.
It was found that:
In some cases, the tax authorities used information obtained in the form of international cooperation and gave the payers vat liability.
In such cases, the payers either wrongly claimed the exemption of supplies from VAT or did not admit the acquisition of the goods in the VAT return.
In some cases, the tax authorities could not use the information obtained because the information was either incomplete or incomprehensible.
In other cases, the information could not be used because of the different legal provisions in both Member States.
In some cases, the tax authorities of another Member State refused to reply to the request for information.
Cases have been identified where payers have misreported business transactions in summary reports.
As a result, the data in VIES were incorrect and the tax authorities had to investigate these cases (see 6.).

4. Administration of value added tax in the Czech Republic and Germany
Registration of payers in the Czech Republic
A) Payers who have their registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic
Under Act No. 337/1992 Coll., on the administration of taxes and fees (hereinafter referred to as "Act No. 337/1992 Coll.") means the taxpayer, the tax payer and the legal successor of a natural or legal person, which is defined as a tax entity by law.
As at 31 December 2004, the 12. 2004 a total of 421,865 tax entities were registered for VAT in the Czech Republic.
As of 1 January 2004, the As of 12 December 2005, the number of tax entities registered for VAT increased to 457 590.
A taxable person who has a registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic whose turnover exceeds CZK 1,000,000 (EUR 33,575) for the next 12 consecutive calendar months becomes a payer. on the third month following the month in which it exceeded the registration limit (Section 94(1) of Act No. 235/2004 Coll., on Value Added Tax; hereinafter referred to as "Act No 235/2004 Coll.").
The application for registration is obliged by this person to file within 15 days after the end of the month in which he exceeded the registration limit.
The current legislation does not allow the registration of a taxable person in cases where the reason for registration is to exceed the legal limit for registration.
A taxable person with a registered office, place of business or an establishment in the Czech Republic who carries out taxable transactions or transactions exempt from VAT with a right to deduct may become a tax payer even if he does not exceed a turnover of CZK 1,000,000 (EUR 33,575) if he fulfils any of the other conditions set out in Act No. 235/2004 Coll.
A taxable person with a registered office, place of business or an establishment in the Czech Republic who does not comply with any of the conditions laid down by law may apply for vat registration on a voluntary basis.
The registration procedure under Act No. 337/1992 Coll. is initiated by the delivery of the application for registration to the locally competent tax administrator.
The voluntary VAT payer on the VAT registration application shall also indicate the date on which he applies for registration as a VAT payer.
The tax administrator shall provide the data communicated by the tax entity, i.e. the tax able entity, the tax authorities, the tax authorities, the tax authorities, the tax authorities the completed registration application with all attachments, shall be checked.
If it has doubts about the data, it shall invite the tax entity to explain, supplement or substantiate the data.
After the tax administrator has verified that the tax entity fulfils the conditions for registration, it shall issue a decision in the form of a certificate that the tax entity is registered and has been assigned a tax identification number (hereinafter referred to as "VAT Registration").
The tax administrator shall indicate on the certificate the effective date of the VAT registration and the periodicity of the VAT tax period.
The tax year is a calendar quarter if the payer's turnover for the preceding calendar year did not reach CZK 10,000,000 (EUR 335 750).
If the payer's turnover for the preceding calendar year has reached CZK 10,000,000 (EUR 335,750), the tax period is a calendar month.
A payer whose turnover for the preceding calendar year has reached CZK 2,000,000 (EUR 67,150) is entitled to choose a calendar month for the tax year and shall notify the tax authorities of this change.
THISsegmentISintentionallyLEFTblank
The allocation of the VAT number in the registration certificate is always constitutional and the tax entity is obliged to indicate in all cases of communication (including payments) with the tax administrator and in cases where a special law so provides (e.g. Act No. 235/2004 Coll. when issuing tax documents).
The VAT registration number contains the code "CZ" and the master part, which consists of a generic identifier.
The general identifier for a natural person is the birth number or, where is the name of the individual. another general identifier, if provided for by a special law, and for a legal person an identification number (section 33(12) of Act No. 337/1992 Coll.).
If the tax entity has not fulfilled its registration obligation or at the request of the tax administrator, it shall be registered by the local tax administrator without delay.
The result of the registration procedure is the issue of an ex officio registration certificate, which is delivered to the tax entity.
In the Czech Republic, a tax entity that has acquired a business authorisation is assigned a VAT number at the time of its first registration for any tax.
The same VAT number is used by the tax entity even if it is registered as a VAT payer.
According to the wording of Act No. 235/2004 Coll., which is in force from 1 January 2004, the commission is required to provide for the following: 1. 2005, in the event of failure to comply with the VAT registration obligation, the taxable person may impose a refund of up to 10% of the total revenue or income for taxable transactions, which this person carried out unduly tax-free, for the period from the date to which he was to be a registered payer by law, to the date on which the tax administrator became a registered payer (section 98(1) of Act No. 235/2004 Coll.).
The payment of the amount thus determined is considered to be a tax payment (Section 98(3) of Act No. 235/2004 Coll.), i.e. it's not a penalty.
It is possible to revoke the registration of a VAT payer if the statutory conditions are fulfilled for two reasons:
1)
Cancellation of registration at the request of the payer, mainly due to the amount of turnover which does not exceed the registration limit (Section 106(1) of Act No. 235/2004 Coll.).
The payer is entitled to withdraw the registration no later than 1 year after the effective date indicated on the registration certificate.
2) Deregistration of registration "ex officio" (Section 106(7) of Act No. 235/2004 Coll.), if: a) the payer did not perform without notice of reason to the tax authorities for 12 consecutive months of performance, b) the payer does not fulfil his obligations under Act No. 235/2004 Coll., c) the payer ceases to be a taxable person.
B) Payers who do not have a registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic A person registered to tax in another Member State who does not have a registered office, place of business or establishment in the Czech Republic, or a foreign taxable person who performs a transaction with the place of supply in the territory of the country and is liable to admit and pay tax on such transactions pursuant to Section 108 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. "unsettled payer") becomes the payer on the date of the performance of the transaction.
This person is obliged to submit an application for registration to the Tax Office for Prague 1 at the latest on the date of the performance.
The registration application shall indicate all VAT registrations assigned to it in other Member States or in a third country.
If the "unsettled" payer submits an application for registration later than the date of the first taxable transaction in the Czech Republic, the Tax Office for Prague 1 registers it retroactively, because according to Act No. 235/2004 Coll., the tax entity became a VAT payer on the date of the first taxable transaction in the Czech Republic.
During retroactive registration, the Tax Office for Prague 1 requires proof from tax entities that the performance has been carried out (invoices or explanatory letters).
If the "unsettled" tax entity applies for registration in the Czech Republic before the first taxable transaction is carried out, then the Tax Office for Prague 1 asks for the submission of contracts for the performance to take place.
At the Tax Office for Prague 1, as of 31 December 2004, there was a total of 100 000 000 000 000 12. 2004 registered 473 "unsettled" payers, of which 124 payers from Germany, and as of 31 December 2004, the number of outstanding payers registered. As of 12 December 2005, 951 "unsettled" payers were registered, of which 233 payers from Germany were registered.
In accordance with the provisions of Article 106(1) of the Basic Regulation, the commission is required to 9 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. the tax administrator is entitled to cancel the registration of the "unsauly paid" payer on 31 December 2004. 1 January of the following calendar year, unless the payer has been obliged to admit and pay tax during the current calendar year.
By checking the SAO, it was found that if the "unsettled" payer submits a tax return abroad for postal transport on 25 April 2009, the tax return will be granted to the tax authorities. From 1 January 2005, the commission shall inform in accordance with the legal regulation in the deadline for filing the tax return, it is often not yet 31. Available from 1 January.
In cases where the facts applicable to the possibility of deregistration to the tax authority are known at a later date than 31 December 2006, the commission shall, in the event of a decision on the application of this Regulation, decide to withdraw the registration from the tax authorities. In the Czech Republic, it is no longer possible for the "unsauched" payer to cancel the VAT registration in a given calendar year.
Registration of payers in Germany
Due to the legal provisions of the German Tax Code (§ § 137, 138 Abgabenordnung, hereinafter referred to as "AO"), anyone who carries out business activities is obliged to inform the municipal/municipal authority or the competent tax authority.
The deadline for submitting information is one month after the start of the business.
This information is processed by the municipal/municipal tax office.
If the tax authority finds an undertaking which has commenced but has not registered, the competent tax authority may register the payer ex officio – even retroactively.
Taxpayers who are both tax residents and non-residents in Germany are required by law to register for VAT if they meet the criteria set out in Section 2 of the German VAT Act (hereinafter referred to as "UStG").
This obligation does not depend on the amount of turnover they make.
There is no voluntary VAT registration in Germany.
There are special tax offices for entrepreneurs permanently living abroad.
For example, for those based in the Czech Republic, the relevant Chemnitz-Süd Tax Office is the competent.
As at 30 June 2004, the On 15 April 2004, a total of 295 Czech entrepreneurs were registered at the Chemnitz-Süd Tax Office; as at 1 January 2004, the A total of 1050 Czech entrepreneurs were registered on March 1, 2006.
THE BRH found that these special tax authorities often refused to register the so-called "tax authorities". independent workers based in the new eastern EU Member States.
As work permits from 10 new EU Member States are limited after they have joined the EU, these independent workers have tried to avoid these restrictions by starting a business.
These undertakings do not meet the criteria for entrepreneurs set out in Paragraph 2 of the UStG, as they are usually dependent on a single employer, which determines their working hours and the way in which they perform their work.
In order to register, the entrepreneur must complete a questionnaire from the competent tax authority in which he must provide information on the company and the activities it carries out.
The questionnaire is a standard form that is binding on all tax authorities in Germany.
It is processed either by special departments of the tax authorities or by general focus departments responsible for assessing taxpayers.
This form shall assess the risk of individual taxpayers before the tax office issues a tax number.
The structure of the tax number for domestic transactions is governed by certain rules:
The first three digits provide information about the relevant tax authority, the next three (or four) provide information about the relevant department at the tax office, the other five (or four) are to distinguish the payers, the last being always the check digit.
If an entrepreneur intends to participate in intra-Community trade, he or she needs a VAT identification number (VAT ID) in order to receive an intra-Community tax-exempt delivery.
THE CLO assigns a VAT ID at the request of the entrepreneur if the entrepreneur is registered in Germany and has a vat number.
THE CLO assigns vat ids to entrepreneurs automatically when they indicate an intra-Community delivery in their VAT return.
The VAT ID structure is the country code (DE) followed by a series of nine digits.
Registration of the entrepreneur may be cancelled: 1. at his request (for example, if he has ceased his business), after carrying out all administrative work (assessment for all marketing years) and 2. if the tax administration becomes aware that it no longer engages in business activities.
The validity of the VAT identification number is usually linked to the validity of the VAT number.
In such cases, the tax authorities are obliged to inform the CUSTOMS of the abolition of the tax number in order to allow the CUSTOMS to terminate the VAT identification number.
Under the German VAT Act (Section 19 (1) UStG), tax residents in Germany are not obliged to pay VAT in the case of 1. whereas turnover plus the relevant VAT of the previous calendar year does not exceed EUR 17 500 and 2 July 1999; not be more likely to exceed EUR 50 000 in the following year.
So-called small entrepreneurs ("Kleinunternehmer") are not entitled to invoice other entrepreneurs vat and are not entitled to an input tax deduction.
Although they are not obliged to pay VAT, small entrepreneurs must be registered with the tax office and have to file an annual VAT return.
A small entrepreneur may declare that the provisions of § 19 para. 1 UStG apply.
This declaration shall be binding on him for the next five years.
The entrepreneur can then invoice VAT and deduct input tax.
For tax non-residents, there is the possibility to appoint tax representatives (Section 22a of the UStG).
It is necessary to ensure that they carry out exclusively exempt commercial operations and are not entitled to an input tax deduction.
The function of the tax representative is to fulfil the tax obligations of a foreign entrepreneur who does not have to register for VAT.
Invoices must show information about representation for tax purposes.
Comparison and evaluation
The situation is different in both countries.
While in Germany entrepreneurs are registered regardless of the amount of their turnover, in the Czech Republic the primary criterion (among others) for registration is the exceeding of the limit set out in the VAT Act.
If the tax entity in the Czech Republic does not exceed the set limit, it has the possibility to apply for VAT registration voluntarily.
The registration process is standardized in Germany, but there may be differences due to different organizational models in federal states.
In the Czech Republic, the payer is assigned a VAT number at the time of his first registration for any tax.
If the payer registers for VAT, he also uses the same VAT registration number for intra-Community transactions.
In Germany, the payer is assigned a tax number when registering for VAT, serving only for business transactions in the territory of Germany.
If the German payer intends to carry out intra-Community transactions, he must request the allocation of a special identification number, the so-called 'intra-Community transaction'. VAT ID.
As the SAO and BRH have discovered, germany's two-step registration system can cause many misunderstandings in other Member States, such as the Czech Republic, which allocates a single identification number for national VAT registration and registration for intra-Community transactions.
On the other hand, a two-stage system allows retroactive (national) registration in cases where payers refuse to inform the municipality or the relevant tax authority about their business.
This retroactive registration allows the correct assessment of VAT for the previous tax year, in particular an accurate estimate of the VAT obligation.
Because different registration methods cause problems, conditions should be levelled across the EU.
The German Parliament recently decided to introduce a tax identification number (hereinafter referred to as a VAT number).
The Federal Tax Office will allocate vat registration number at the birth of a natural person.
This VAT number will be valid for the life of a natural person who is a German resident.
If a natural person starts a business, the competent tax authority shall request an economic VAT number, which will be used as a VAT ID.
In the future, there should be no delay between the national registration of the payer and the allocation of the VAT ID.
Work on the introduction of an IT resource to manage the VAT registration number has not yet been completed.
International bus passenger transport
Legislation in the Czech Republic
According to the provisions of Section 70 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll., it is valid from 1. 5. 2004 the transport of persons between individual Member States and also between Member States and third countries in the Czech Republic is exempt from VAT with the right to deduct.
Such transport shall be exempt from VAT, even if it is carried out by entrepreneurs who are registered for tax in other Member States or by a foreign taxable person.
Return transport is considered to be a separate transport.
If "unsettled" tax entities in the Czech Republic do not carry out any other economic activity in addition to international bus transport of persons, they are not obliged to register as VAT payers in the Czech Republic.
International transport of persons in the Czech Republic was exempt from VAT under the Act of Accession of the Czech Republic, Annex V to Chapter 10. Article 5(1) of Regulation (EC) No Article 1(1)(b) (b) which states:
'For the purposes of Article 3(1) of Regulation (EC) No 28(2) And regulation (EC) No 125 Article 3(b) of The Basic Regulation, the commission shall Directive 77/388/EEC, the Czech Republic may continue to exempt value added tax on international passenger transport referred to in point 17 of Annex F to the Directive until the condition laid down in Article 10 of Directive 2001/12/EC has been fulfilled. 28(2) And regulation (EC) No 125 Article 4 of the Directive or for as long as the same exemption is applied by an existing Member State, whichever is the earlier.'
Description of legislation in Germany
Pursuant to Article 46 of Council Directive 2006/112/EC of 28 June 2006 on the approximation of the community for the purposes of the european union's free movement of such data [2], it is appropriate to take into 2006, implemented under Section 3b(1)(a) of the Treaty on European Union. 1 of the German VAT Act is the place of provision of passenger transport (i.e. transport services) route (i.e. the place where the transport takes place).
The German tax system therefore does not distinguish between national and international cross-border passenger transport.
Only that part of the route that takes place in Germany constitutes a taxable provision of transport in Germany.
The German tax system also does not distinguish between tax residents and non-residents.
If a non-resident tax resident transports passengers via Germany, then that part of the route that takes place in Germany is also a taxable provision of transport.
The non-resident tax resident must notify the competent tax authority before carrying out his services in Germany.
The tax authority shall register this non-resident taxable person (cf. 4.1.2) and issue a special certificate for any bus or coach specified in the taxpayer's notification.
The taxpayer is obliged to declare his taxable transport in the German VAT return.
As of 1 January 2004, the As of March 31, 2006, the Chemnitz-Süd Tax Office registered 741 Czech payers who carried out passenger transport.
If the carriage of passengers is provided to a tax resident who is a taxable person for VAT, the tax non-resident does not have to pay VAT to the tax authority himself.
Instead, the entity which is obliged to pay VAT to the tax authority and the invoiced net amount to the non-resident tax resident is the tax resident who is the recipient of the services; this process is known as 'reverse charge' and complies with Article 196 of Council Directive 2006/112/EC.
In addition to the notification of the non-resident tax return and its VAT return, the German tax administration has several means of assessing the correctness of the taxable provision of passenger transport granted.
The mobile control groups of the customs office carry out an audit of the certificates of buses authorised (licensed) for foreign transport, which are used for the carriage of passengers through Germany.
After each audit, the mobile control groups shall send a control report to the relevant tax authority.
If the bus driver does not have a valid certificate, the mobile control group is entitled to request VAT from the bus driver before continuing to transport further.
A non-resident tax resident may deduct the VAT thus paid on the tax calculated in his VAT return.
If the tax office has doubts as to the accuracy of the VAT return, it may notify the intention to carry out an audit, which must take place at the tax authority's office, or it may use the means of administrative cooperation referred to in Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 (see 4.6).
Even if a non-resident tax resident refuses to pay the amount of VAT assessed in accordance with its statutory rate, the tax office may request administrative cooperation in accordance with Council Directive 76/308/EEC.
If a review of the VAT return or the fulfilment of the obligations of a non-resident tax return is to be carried out, BRH considers all such means of administrative cooperation to be too labour intensive compared to the small amounts of VAT to be paid for the taxable provision of passenger transport.
In particular, the audit of the accounts of a non-resident tax resident raises disproportionate costs for both the taxpayer and the tax administration.
Tax administration must audit foreign accounting, which does not only mean the need to know a foreign language, but also familiarity with foreign accounting standards.
An audit of this type is also likely to require more time than an audit of a tax resident, but this audit is limited to the provision of passenger transport in Germany.
On the other hand, a non-resident tax member may not only accept the right to carry out an inspection which is due to his national tax administration, but also the right to carry out an audit by other Member States in which he carries passengers.
In addition, in each Member State in which only one provision of passenger transport takes place, the taxpayer is obliged to fulfil all the tax obligations applicable to it in those Member States, in all languages and on all the tax forms of those Member States.
The actual taxation of cross-border passenger transport therefore raises disproportionate bureaucratic costs.
Comparison and evaluation
The legal situation in both countries is different.
In the Czech Republic, the transport of persons between individual EU Member States or between Member States and third countries is exempt from VAT on the basis of the Act of Accession of the Czech Republic, entitled to deduction.
In Germany, the part of the transport which takes place on German territory constitutes a taxable transaction.
If this transport is provided in Germany by an unsettled payer for the first time, he is obliged to notify the competent tax authority in advance of the provision of the transport.
The tax office registers this payer and the payer is obliged to grant in Germany the taxable provision of part of the transport in the tax return.
The implementation of the law is very time-consuming in Germany.
At least three of the four Czech payers registered with the Chemnitz-Süd Tax Office carry out passenger transport.
Compared to the effort, the tax revenue, if implemented, is rather low.
Member States which collect VAT in accordance with Article 46 of Council Directive 2006/112/EC of 28 June 2006 on the approximation of the following directive of 2006/112/EC of 28 June 2006 on the approximation of the following directive On 15 November 2006, on the common system of VAT, they are burdened with time consuming obligations without a financially sensitive result.
In order to avoid disproportionate costs to assess VAT, the provision of cross-border passenger transport should only be taxed in one Member State.
This could be the state where the transport begins or where the provider resides.
Such taxation would require the adaptation of Council Directive 2006/112/EC.
VAT returns
Submission and processing of VAT returns in the Czech Republic
The payer is obliged to file a VAT return within 25 days after the end of the tax year on the form prescribed by the MF, even if he has not incurred any tax liability, unless the law provides otherwise.
The actual tax liability is payable within the time limit for filing the VAT return, with the exception of the tax charged in connection with the import of goods pursuant to Section 20 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll., for which the tax maturity is determined by customs legislation.
If a refundable overpayment arises as a result of the assessment of the excessive deduction, the payer shall be returned to the payer without request within 30 days of the assessment of the excess deduction.
The time limit is not applied in cases where the tax administrator initiates tax proceedings relating to the payer's tax liability.
In accordance with article 73(1)(a) of the Basic Regulation, the Commission shall, in accordance with the procedure laid down in Article 10 11 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. may be exercised in the ordinary VAT return no later than for the last tax year in which the right to deduct could be exercised.
After the expiry of that period, the right to deduct may be further exercised within 3 years of the end of the tax year in which the right to deduct could be exercised first.
However, this is only possible by submitting an additional VAT return.
Amendment to Act No. 235/2004 Coll. effective from 1 January 2004 1. 2005 allows the submission of an additional VAT return only for the period when the right to deduct could be applied for the first time.
The payer is obliged to submit an additional VAT return if a) the summary of corrections increases the tax liability, b) performs a correction at which the last known tax liability is not changed, but only the data previously claimed by the tax entity, c) performs the correction of the rate and amount of the tax pursuant to Section 49 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll.
The payer may submit an additional VAT return if the summary of corrections reduces the tax liability.
The payer is obliged to submit an additional VAT return by the end of the month following the discovery of these facts.
The filing of a VAT return in electronic form can be done both via the Internet or on a technical data medium.
Submission via the Internet may be made as a submission with a data message bearing a guaranteed electronic signature or as a submission with a data message not provided by a guaranteed electronic signature.
In the case of submission with a data report not provided by a guaranteed electronic signature, submission in writing is still required, i.e. the delivery of the computer report to the tax authorities (e-form).
The VAT return contains separate lines related to intra-Community delivery/acquisition values.
The values of the acquisition of services are reported on special lines of the VAT return.
Some lines are used for the purpose of the initial automated scan within the ADIS system.
The values of the supply of goods to other Member States to tax-registered persons in other Member States shall be compared with the information given in the summary reports submitted by the Czech payers.
The values of the acquisition of goods from other Member States from tax-registered persons in other Member States shall be compared with those obtained through VIES from recapitulative reports of payers from other EU Member States.
The Tax Office is taking a test of the credibility of VAT returns within the ADIS system.
This test is carried out automatically, as vat returns cannot be measured without the test.
The trust test involves calculating trust criteria and evaluating risky types of VAT returns.
In accordance with the provisions of Article 37(1) of the Basic Regulation, the commission is required to In accordance with Article 1 of Act No. 337/1992 Coll., the Tax Office may repeatedly impose a fine of up to CZK 2,000,000 (EUR 67,150) on a person who fails to comply with the obligation of a non-monetary nature under this or a special tax law, or imposed by a decision under that Act.
Automated tax information system used by the FA to technically support tax administration.
By checking the SAO, it was found that the tax authorities mostly did not use the possibility to impose a fine on the payers for not submitting a VAT return.
Submission and processing of VAT returns in Germany
In Germany, we distinguish between a preliminary monthly or quarterly VAT return and an annual VAT return.
Those taxpayers who are required to submit advance VAT returns must still submit an annual VAT return.
Even small entrepreneurs who are not obliged to pay VAT must file an annual tax return.
In general, taxpayers are required to submit a quarterly VAT return by 10 April 2018. the day following the quarter in which VAT occurs (Section 18(2) UStG).
However, if the VAT liability exceeds EUR 6 136 in the previous calendar year or if it is a newly created undertaking, the relevant entrepreneur is obliged to submit a monthly VAT return by 10 June 2009. the following month.
The taxpayer may also decide to file a monthly VAT return if a refund has been made in the past year which exceeded EUR 6 136 (Section 18(2a) of the UStG).
VAT returns do not have to be filed unless the amount of the annual VAT exceeds EUR 512.
The relevant amount of VAT tax shall be paid by 10 April 2006. the day following the tax period in which vat was incurred.
The refund may lead to an even more detailed investigation by the FA.
There are no deadlines (by law) for processing tax returns and refunding excess VAT deductions.
In order to return the tax in a timely way, it is possible to offer collateral for the amount to be refunded.
The basic principle is to process vat returns and return the tax quickly.
The German VAT Act provides for the possibility to extend this period (Section 18(6) of the UStG).
Such an extension should be requested separately.
It allows you to submit a VAT return and pay the relevant VAT liability a month later, provided that in the case of a monthly return a special deposit is paid.
This advance payment will be settled against the December VAT tax liability.
Whenever an error is detected, the entrepreneur must file a VAT tax return.
There is no additional VAT return.
Once the annual VAT return, which must be filed by 31 December 2006, is granted by 31 December 2005, the vat return is granted in accordance with the From 1 May of the following calendar year, registered with the tax office, the entrepreneur can not correct the erroneous preliminary tax return, but only the annual VAT return.
Correction of the annual VAT return to the benefit or disadvantage of the payer is possible within the next 4 years after the year in which the first annual VAT return was filed.
After these four years, the annual VAT return can normally be corrected only in cases of tax fraud or evasion.
Payers are required to file their vat pre-tax returns electronically.
Tax authorities may apply exceptions to this rule in order to avoid excessive hardness.
The filing of an annual VAT return is possible in paper form or via the Internet, either certified or without it.
If it is carried out without certification, the payer must submit the declaration once more on paper with personal signatures.
In the event that the payer does not submit vat returns, the tax administration is entitled to make a rough estimate of the taxpayer's turnover.
In the case of late filing, the payer may be fined (up to 10% of the tax to be paid or EUR 25 000).
During a previous inspection, the BRH found that the tax authorities often did not charge this standard fine.
In other cases where the tax authorities imposed a fine, the amount was assessed inconsistently and arbitrarily.
The standard fine therefore fails to meet its objective of shortening the average delay, especially when submitting an annual VAT return.
The VAT return contains separate lines related to intra-Community delivery/acquisition values.
The values of the acquisition of services are reported on special lines of the VAT return.
Non-taxable transactions must be reported on a separate tax return/VAT line.
In the case of VAT returns which are submitted in paper form, a copy must be made either through the scanner or by the staff specially entrusted with it.
Data from vat returns submitted electronically is immediately available to the tax authority staffer.
Once all the data has been entered into the system, RMS personnel will pass them and select cases that meet certain criteria.
The selected VAT returns must be checked by the tax authority employee on the basis of a control report drawn up by the system.
section 5.2).
Although the tax administration must roughly estimate the amount of VAT that the taxpayer must pay, the estimated tax must be as precise as possible.
Comparison and evaluation
In the Czech Republic, the payers submit a VAT return within 25 days after the end of the tax year.
Depending on the amount of the payer's turnover, the tax period is either a calendar quarter or a calendar month.
In Germany, the payers submit advance VAT returns, depending on the tax liability in the previous year, either within 10 days of the end of the calendar quarter or the month.
Until 31 December 2005, the Import From 1 May of the following year, the payers are obliged to file an annual tax return.
The obligation to submit an annual VAT return has its pros and cons:
+ at the end of the calendar year, the payer is able to correct errors in (monthly preliminary) tax returns by submitting a single annual VAT return;
– if the payer corrects the intra-Community transactions awarded, the correction cannot be related to the period for which the recapitulative statement is filed;
– the Federal States do not normally compare VIES data on intra-Community acquisitions of German payers before the annual VAT return is processed.
In accordance with registration (see 4.1.3), German payers are obliged to file an annual VAT return regardless of their turnover.
This obligation allows the German financial authority to check the maximum turnover limit for small entrepreneurs.
In addition, the responsible tax authority is able to compare the annual VAT return with the returns for direct taxes and with the final accounts.
In the Czech Republic, tax authorities are able to determine the amount of the payer's turnover only from the submitted income tax returns.
Unlike the Czech Republic, payers in Germany are obliged to submit VAT returns in electronic form.
The introduction of the obligation to file tax returns electronically in the Czech Republic would contribute to increasing the efficiency of the Czech tax administration.
Summary reports
Submission and processing of summary reports in the Czech Republic
The recapitulative statement ('SH') is submitted in accordance with the provisions of Section 102 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. of the payer who made the supply of goods to another Member State to a taxable person in another Member State.
Data on the value of the delivered goods are always given in Czech currency broken down by individual tax entities, indicating their VAT ID under which they are registered in their country.
Data on the services provided shall not be included in the SH.
Sh shall be submitted to the locally competent tax authority for each calendar quarter for each calendar quarter.
The correction of the erroneous data is carried out in the subsequent SH within 15 days from the date of detection of errors.
The erroneous data given in sh are always replaced by the data given in the subsequent SH.
As well as tax returns, both the payer and the SH can file in electronic form.
In the event that the payer does not submit sh or subsequent SH and had them pursuant to Act No. 235/2004 Coll. submitted, asked by the tax administrator to file it and at the same time instructs him on the consequences in the event of non-submission of sh or subsequent SH, i.e. that the tax administrator is entitled to repeatedly impose a fine of up to CZK 2,000,000 (EUR 67,150) for non-compliance with non-pecuniary obligations.
By checking the SAO, it was found that the tax authorities mostly did not use the possibility of imposing a fine on payers for non-compliance with their legal obligations.
In particular, in the case of sh submissions, tax entities are not sufficiently motivated to fulfil their obligations, since the failure to submit a SH does not affect the vat liability.
The tax administrator is obliged according to § 102 para. 5 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. data in sh, or in the subsequent SH, to examine, remove any confusion and use the data for the determination of tax liability.
In the event of a mismatch of the data in the SH and the data in the relevant (payer with the monthly tax period) or the relevant (payer with a quarterly tax period) vat return, the tax administrator should verify the correctness of the tax liability granted as specified in the VAT return.
Erroneous data in sh the tax entity removes by filing a subsequent SH itself, or may be invited to do so.
The tax administrator shall correct the information on the supply of goods to other Member States in the ADIS system if:
– the payer does not demonstrate the data specified in the SH (or subsequent SH) and corrects them by filing a subsequent SH,
– the tax administrator has demonstrated that the information given by the payer in the SH or the subsequent SH is not true.
The tax administrator does not replace the submission of the tax entity by inserting a correction without filing a subsequent SH, it merely modifies the data in the VIES database so that it is up to date, complete and accurate.
Data from sh shall be sent to the Member States concerned.
They may be sent and received only by a national financial authority intended to cooperate with other Member States in the field of VAT; this is CLO (in the Czech Republic it performs this function of MF, department of international cooperation in the administration of VAT (CLO).
O_MCTL is an automatic message that clo receives from other Member States.
Contains any bad VAT IDs listed in the sent SH lines.
If the bad VAT ID is used in one of the migrated regular SH or subsequent SH rows, a record is made to the wrong VAT ID table.
The table contains the so-called "Notice of doubt on VAT ID".
The tax administrator checks the data and records the result of the verification in the system.
When acquiring goods from another Member State, the payer is obliged to declare VAT and indicate the acquisition values on separate lines of the VAT return.
Selected cases of irregularities in the value of the acquired goods declared by the Czech payer in his VAT return and in the value of the delivered goods, as stated by payers from other Member States in their SH, are sent from CLO to the tax office for examination.
Tax authorities are obliged to investigate irregularities.
There are three situations:
a) The value declared by the Czech payer in the relevant vat return lines is lower than the value of the delivery declared by eu payers.
In this case, the tax administrator shall verify the accuracy of the data.
(b) The difference amount is 0.
This situation can occur either by changing the data in the EU (the foreign supplier corrects his SH) or by changing the data in the VAT return (the Czech tax entity itself will file an additional VAT return in the meantime).
In this case, it is at the discretion of the tax administrator whether, despite this fact, he will verify the accuracy of the data in the VAT return.
c) The value of the acquisition of goods from other Member States, which the Czech tax payer has indicated in the relevant vat return lines, is higher than the value of the delivered goods declared by eu payers.
Here, too, it is at the discretion of the controller whether to verify the accuracy of the data.
After examining the difference and clarifying the causes of its occurrence, the tax administrator shall indicate to ADIS the result of the verification.
The scan results are transmitted back to CLO.
Graph 1 (n/ GRAPH) shows the number of cases sent from CLO to the tax authorities for examination for each quarter of 2005.
Chart 1 above shows that the number of cases transmitted from CLO to the tax authorities decreased for each quarter of 2005.
There was a significant decrease in the number in the 4th year of the year. quarter 2005. THE DUTY has increased the minimum financial limit, inter alia, by increasing the amount of the aid. with regard to the possibility of sending requests for information to other EU Member States.
The discrepancy between the vat return data and the EU data may not always be caused by an error on the part of the domestic payer.
It may also be an error on the part of EU payers or a mistake resulting from the fact that certain types of transactions may be entered into sh in different ways in each EU Member State.
Table 1 is the most common reasons for irregularities in the values of reported transactions detected in the audited tax authorities.
Submission and processing of summary reports in Germany
Entrepreneurs who make intra-Community deliveries from Germany to other EU Member States or participate in tripartite transactions are required to submit a quarterly SH in which intra-Community deliveries are reported by beneficiaries (Section 18a(1) of the UStG).
Sh must be administered by 10 April 2009. the month following the relevant calendar quarter.
If the extension of this period is allowed in the case of preliminary VAT returns, this also applies to SH.
CLO must be supplied.
From 1 January 2005, the They must be submitted electronically from 1 January 2007.
Exemptions may be allowed by the competent tax authorities to certain taxpayers in order to avoid undue hardness.
In cases where taxpayers become aware that incorrect information is provided in the SH, it is necessary to submit a corrective report within one month.
In the event that taxpayers do not submit sh, CLO will initiate proceedings in order to enforce the submission of this report.
Part of this procedure is: – first reminder – the second reminder associated with the threat of a fine/penalty payment and – the assessment of the penalty payment.
Although the German Tax Code allows fines of up to EUR 25 000 (Section 329 AO), CLO levies fines in three steps, in amounts of EUR 125, 250 and EUR 500.
In addition, § 26a para. 1 No 5 UStG provides that payers act unlawfully if they do not intentionally or negligently submit a SH, submit them incomplete, do not submit them on time or if they do not correct or repair a late SH at all.
This offence can be punishable by a fine of up to EUR 5 000.
Information on intra-Community deliveries cannot be entered into VIES by the Tax Office because sh processing is the exclusive task of CLO.
SH data is stored only in the CLO system.
Therefore, data from SH are only visually available to the Tax Office after their processing to CLO.
The time limits for sh processing are laid down in Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
Sh data must be stored within three months following the relevant calendar quarter.
In the event of incorrect VAT IDs being mentioned in the SH of German payers, CLO receives O_MCTL codes from another Member State.
CLO contacts a specific entrepreneur and asks him for the correct information.
If the CLO fails to obtain the correct information, the case is referred to the relevant tax authorities.
It is then up to these tax authorities to request the correct information.
During the inspection, BRH found that most entrepreneurs had corrected the VAT ID at clo's request.
However, the challenge, threat and assessment of the three additional fines take up too much time in cases where the payer may be involved in cross-border carousel fraud.
These cases, which were eventually reported to the relevant tax authorities, were usually completed within one or two months.
The Tax Office rejected the exemption of declared intra-Community supplies in 73 % of these cases.
When the payer provided the correct VAT ID, the tax office asked him to file a corrected SH on CLO, as the tax authorities cannot repair the data in VIES themselves.
THE BRH found that neither the tax authorities nor CLO checked the submission of the corrected SH, so the payers often failed to comply with the requests.
In view of the fact that CLO does not have access to the VAT return data, a comparison of the data on the supply of goods granted in the VAT return and in sh shall not take place before the submission of such data to the CLO of the other Member States.
This check can only be carried out by the tax authorities and is usually applied when preparing a VAT check.
Data obtained from other Member States are processed at CLO.
Incorrect VAT IDs are selected and are subsequently submitted to the Member States concerned.
This data is used for the purpose of the acquisition control carried out by the tax authorities.
Once they are entered into the system, CLO checks them on the basis of a comparison with data from previous calendar quarters.
If they meet certain criteria (see 5.2), control information is created and sent to the relevant tax authorities.
This procedure is applied on a permanent basis, while the compilation of data on the acquisition of goods or services for all VAT payers is created at a later date and submitted to the tax authorities.
Rms installed for the purpose of the assessment procedure shall subsequently check these data with data on intra-Community acquisitions.
This system completely covers those entrepreneurs who do not have full right to deduct VAT.
Comparison and evaluation
In the Czech Republic, payers who have made the delivery of goods to another Member State to a taxable person in another Member State shall submit sh to the locally competent tax authority within 25 days after the end of the calendar quarter.
The tax authorities shall process the SH and transmit the data to CLO.
The values of the supply of goods to another Member State, indicated by the payer in the SH, are compared at the tax authorities with the values of the supply of goods to another Member State indicated by those payers in the VAT returns.
The results of the comparison are used in the assessment procedure.
In Germany, payers who have made intra-Community delivery are obliged to submit a QUARTERLY SH until 10 January 2010. the day of the following calendar quarter.
SH payers are administered to CLO, from 1 January to 31 December 2005. 1. 2007 in electronic form.
The tax authorities have information from sh available only after their processing to CLO.
Payers from the Czech Republic and Germany list only the supply of goods in SH, the provision of services is not mentioned in sh.
Unlike the Czech tax authorities, the German tax authorities are not able to correct the erroneous lines filed by sh.
As a result of this limited access to the german VIES data, the incorrect VAT ID was not corrected even if the payer provided the correct VAT ID to the FU.
The German tax authorities do not compare the information on intra-Community supplies that are included in the Vat return of the German payer and his SH.
The differences between the data of these two statements are not usually established before the German CLO provides data from VIES to other Member States.
In view of the BRH findings, it is clear that the comparison would increase the reliability of the data transmitted in VIES.
Data on the supply of goods to Czech payers, delivered from other Member States, are compared in the Czech Republic with data on the acquisition of goods from other Member States declared by Czech payers in their VAT returns.
The comparison shall be carried out separately by clo for each calendar quarter.
The most significant cases of irregularities are passed on to the tax authorities as a warning of possible errors in the tax returns of the payers.
Unlike the Czech tax administration, the German tax administration does not usually control the taxation of intra-community acquisitions.
Such a general check is processed only for payers who are not fully entitled to the deduction of VAT.
In addition, the German tax administration checks the taxation of intra-Community acquisitions of other payers only if RMS produces a control notice or if the payer is designated for inspection anyway.
This procedure relieves the tax authorities from the need to clarify the reasons for each difference.
On the other hand, the detection of VAT fraud depends on the quality of rms.
Combating carousel fraud requires continuously updated information on intra-Community acquisitions as soon as possible.
The current SH system, specifically VIES, provides financial authorities with information that may be up to six months old.
This delay can be reduced by up to four months if the payers are given SH monthly.
Monthly filing would not be a significant increase in bureaucratic costs, since most payers in the Czech Republic and Germany are obliged to file tax returns for VAT on a monthly basis – and SH does not require any additional information compared to the tax return.
In order to avoid bureaucratic costs, the filing of sh may be linked to the filing of a VAT return.
However, the obligation to submit a SH monthly would cause more time differences between the reporting of intra-Community delivery and intra-Community acquisition and could increase the flow of data between the customs.
In 2006, the German Federal Government considered the general provisions of monthly SH.
Its implementation failed because of the doubts of the federal states.
They feared that the monthly submission of data from VIES to CLO of other Member States could lead to confusion and confusion.
In fact, if the obligation to monthly SH and monthly data transmission were to be effective, a monthly update of VIES would require a European monthly SH standard.
