International Level 3 Information Exchange
Implementation of the international exchange of information in the Czech Republic
The international exchange of information enables tax authorities to obtain information from other Member States concerning intra-Community business transactions and the payers who have carried out such transactions.
Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 on administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax and repealing Regulation (EEC) No 218/92 distinguishes between the two basic categories of exchange of information, namely the exchange of information on request and the exchange of information without prior request.
The international exchange of information on request is carried out in the form of a so-called "data exchange". requests for information ('The ZOI'), using standardised SCAC forms.
Tax authorities from the Czech Republic send their ŽOI or replies to the ŽOI delivered through the financial directorates to CLO, which ensures the translation of the information provided on standardised SCAC forms into a foreign language and their dispatch to other Member States.
CLO also secures the income of the YOI from other Member States and the responses to the submitted ŽOI, their translation into Czech and distribution to locally competent tax authorities for processing.
In Article 3(1) of Regulation ( 8 Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 provides for a maximum period for the processing of the ZOI to be 3 months after receipt of the application.
All ŽOI, transmitted during the audited period between the Czech Republic and Germany, were subjected to inspections of the SAO.
Out of the total of 94 ŽOI received in the Czech Republic from Germany, 70 were cases (i.e. 74.5 %) within the three-month period, a further 23 cases (i.e. 24.5%) has been settled after that period and the remaining 1 case has not been sent to the Germany until the SAO is checked.
Graph 2 provides more detailed information on the deadlines within which replies to ŽOI received from Germany were sent from the Czech Republic.
Of the 335 ŽOI shipped from the Czech Republic to Germany, 136 were in 136 cases (i.e. 40.6%) received within the three-month period, another 179 (i.e. 53.4%) requests were answered after this deadline and 19 cases (i.e. 5.7%) the reply from Germany was not received until the SAO was checked (in the remaining 1 case it was not possible to determine from the data transmitted when the reply from The Germany was received).
Graph 3 provides more detailed information on the deadlines within which replies to ŽOI sent to Germany were sent to the Czech Republic.
The percentage of intra-Community transaction values presented in the ŽOI transmitted between the Czech Republic and Germany is graph 4.
As can be seen from the chart above, the value of commercial transactions examined through the ŽOI was most often in the band above EUR 60 000.
The international exchange of information without prior request takes place either in the form of automatic or structured automatic exchange of information or in the form of spontaneous exchange of information.
Tax authorities from other Member States are often passed on to tax authorities from other Member States without prior request information which may be relevant to them in the management of VAT.
In the Czech Republic, all information is collected at CLO.
Information shall be transmitted electronically between Member States.
'Automatic exchange' means, pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, the systematic communication of predetermined information to other Member States, without prior request and at pre-determined regular intervals.
'Structured automatic exchange' means the systematic communication of predetermined information to other Member States, without prior request and as soon as the information is available.
The Czech Republic provides other Member States with information on the delivery of new means of transport in the form of automatic exchange.
This information is available to the tax authorities from the Form Of The Report on the Delivery of a New Means of Transport pursuant to Section 19 of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. and from a copy of the issued tax document.
The tax administrator shall complete the necessary data in a specially crafted template and transmit it to the contact officer at the Financial Directorate, where the data are collected and within the specified deadline, i.e. by a deadline. no later than two months after the end of the quarter in which this information was available, the CLO shall be transmitted to the CUSTOMS for subsequent processing and transmission to other Member States.
Furthermore, the Czech Republic provides other Member States with information on vat-exempt mail sales in the Member State of origin, information on intra-EU operations that appear to be unjustified and information on potential "missing traders".
This information is sent to other Member States by spontaneous exchange using the SCAC form.
Implementation of the international exchange of information in Germany
In Germany, both requests for information and the processing of spontaneous information are initiated by the locally competent tax authority.
The tax authorities send the completed SCAC 2004 form directly to the German CLO, which transmits scac forms to foreign CLO.
The tax authorities were instructed to write their requests for information or their own spontaneous information only in German; even the SCAC form you use is not multilingual.
Half of the German requests for information audited by brh were sent in order to ensure taxation of intra-Community acquisitions in another Member State, or to demonstrate the exemption of intra-Community supplies from Germany to another Member State.
If the German CLO receives a request for information from another Member State, it shall check the value of the supplies of goods or services referred to in the application for a minimum limit of EUR 15 000.
In the absence of a reasonable reason for this request, the German CLO shall reject any application containing an amount below that fixed limit.
In addition, the German CLO translates the free texts of the SCAC form [(B1-17) or (E)] if these texts are not in German or English.
To respond to a request for information, CLO shall send the request to the relevant tax authority, asking for a three-month period.
There are no additional deadlines for processing applications at specific organisational levels of tax administration.
Although the German CLO has technical conditions for monitoring past time limits, it lacks sufficient staffing capacity to alert the tax authorities to the answer to unfilled requests for information.
The tax authorities shall obtain the necessary information by sending a letter to the taxpayer or by carrying out an audit.
Auditors usually choose between two different types of audits: a special VAT audit covering any taxable process over a period of several months, or a so-called VAT inspection, which can only relate to one commercial operation that has been carried out recently.
This short and flexible type of audit does not require any notification to the taxpayer and has demonstrated its usefulness in investigating individual taxable business operations.
In the context of automatic exchange without prior request, germany provides other Member States with information – on THE VAT IDs allocated to payers resident in other Member States – on the refund of input tax to payers resident in other Member States.
In addition, the Germany has undertaken to provide other Member States with the following information through a structured automatic exchange:
a. The supply of new means of transport to entrepreneurs without the use of their VAT ID, b. sending or catalogue sale in other Member States which is not taxable in Germany, c. significant differences between intra-community acquisitions declared by the payer and data from VIES, provided by other Member States, d. intra-community delivery of goods not declared by the German payer in SH because the deliveries were treated as domestic transactions, e. potential "trade missingr" , which carried out intra-Community transactions independently of the validity of their VAT ID, f. entrepreneurs who supplied the goods to potential "missing traders" or to those recipients who misused their VAT ID.
Comparison and evaluation
The sending of ŽOI or spontaneous information is initiated in both the Czech Republic and germany by locally competent tax authorities, which send the completed SCAC form to CLO.
While the Czech CLO uses the bilingual SCAC form (English) and translates the information sent into English or German, the German tax authorities follow the order that they write ŽOI or spontaneous information only in German on a monolingual form.
German CLO does not provide translation of German texts.
By examining the ŽOI transmitted between 1 January 2004 and 31 December 2004, the 5. 2004 to 31 December 2004 On 12. 2005 between the Czech Republic and Germany, the SAO found that the Czech tax administration handled 74.5% of the applications received within the specified three-month period, while žOI shipped to Germany were settled by the German tax administration within the specified time limit in only 40.6% of cases.
Although the German CLO warns the tax authorities of a three-month period, it does not track the elapsed time limits.
The result of missing warnings is a large number of delayed responses to the ZOI.
Due to these problems, BRH recommended that you carry out regular warnings on CLO.
The situation has already improved.
According to the latest information, the German CLO is now drawing the attention of the tax authorities to the answer to the unfinished answers to the ZOI.
VAT risk management
Risk management in the Czech Republic
In the Czech Republic, several departments at various organisational levels of tax administration are engaged in the management of vat risks.
Within the MF, the following services deal with the issues of risk management and the fight against VAT fraud:
The Department of Methodology and Performance of VAT and within it the report Risk Management in the field of VAT, which, inter alia, manages the selection of risks of possible tax evasion and evaluates trends of these risks at domestic and Community level.
It coordinates nationally the operation of the Trust of VAT Tax Returns and the use of VIES data in terms of the risks of tax evasion in intra-Community transactions.
Based on data from the trade balance of the Czech Republic, it evaluates risk commodities, processes conceptually the management of VAT risks and cooperates in this area with the relevant EU institutions and other Member States.
Department of International Cooperation in VAT Management, which, among other things, has been used for the development of the vat system. it ensures the exchange of VAT information, participates in the creation and maintenance of information databases, analyses data from other Member States contained in the VIES system, ensures public awareness and ensures other forms of international cooperation within the meaning of Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
Both SAI requested data on the number of erroneous VAT registration numbers or VAT IDs contained in reports O_MCTL transmitted between the Czech Republic and Germany for each quarter of the period audited.
This information is contained in the following tables.
The data show significant differences.
This may be due to different basis for determining the number of messages O_MCTL.
While the Czech CLO refers their numbers to the calendar quarter for which sh was filed, the German CLO refers to their numbers to the calendar quarter in which the report was O_MCTL received.
Department of Tax Control and Search Methodology, which, among other things, has been used for the construction of tax control and search methodologies. conducts risk analysis in the framework of the methodological management of tax controls and, in line with the risk analysis, sets priorities for the targeting of tax controls in the plans of the financial directorates, processes risk analyses in the context of the reduction of tax evasion, including the collection of knowledge gained from tax administration and from other sources, and proposes measures to reduce tax evasion.
In the financial directorates, search departments are set up, which carry out, inter alia, the financial research departments. the search for tax entities and areas that are at risk from the point of view of the occurrence of tax fraud (e.g. online shops, gold, the pharmaceutical industry), the search for unregistered tax entities for the risks of tax evasion (e.g. in the field of internet services, mediation, radio and press services, etc.), analysis of chain fraud links and transmission of information to territorial financial authorities.
A specialised control unit is set up at selected 12 tax offices.
They have regional competence, tax checks outside the territorial jurisdiction of the tax authorities are carried out on the basis of a mandate.
The need to set up a separation of specialised tax controls has emerged on the basis of the increasing findings of new and improved forms of tax evasion, which occur mainly among chain-connected entities.
These departments focus on the control of tax entities according to the requirements of search departments, tax entities with specific activities and multinational companies and tax entities of a large scale of activity in terms of turnover size.
The following mechanisms have been integrated into ADIS to reduce VAT risks: – the role of Credibility of VAT Returns, used to assess the risk iness of tax returns, – the role of selecting tax entities for inspection, allowing the choice of payer criteria to be selected for control, – the role of VIES, through which tax authorities have access to data provided from other EU Member States.
The role of VIES enables: – to verify the validity of VAT IDs of payers from other Member States, – to obtain from other Member States the values of goods delivered to the Czech payer, declared in sh by all its suppliers from other Member States, – to generate a report of payers who have not submitted sh, – to carry out a formal check of the data that the payers from the Czech Republic have provided in the Sh, before sending this data to other Member States, – to generate a report of payers for which the information on the supply of goods to other Member States, as indicated in the VAT returns, does not match the data in the SH, – to generate a report of payers for which the value of the acquisition of goods from other Member States indicated in the VAT returns does not match the data declared in the SH by all its suppliers from other Member States.
In the context of activities to reduce the risks of tax evasion, tax authorities have access to registers of government bodies such as the tax authorities. commercial register, land register, motor vehicle register, trade register, etc.
More detailed information can be found in chapter 4.4.1 Submission and processing of summary reports in the Czech Republic.
Risk management in Germany
Due to the federal structure of Germany, the federal tax administration (in particular CLO) and the tax administration of 16 federal states are involved in the development and operation of RMS.
Although there are joint development working groups, neither CLO nor federal tax administrations share a completely consistent database.
At CLO level, ST I 2 ('KUSS' – Coordination Unit for Special VAT Audits and Tax Investigations) collects the findings of a control on tax fraud in a specific database called the OPUS.
KUSS has established, in cooperation with the tax authorities, a new database called ZAUBER designed to transfer the names of companies of tax cheats "missing traders".
KUSS coordinates related cases of national and cross-border tax fraud.
Kuss experience is reflected in rms development in working groups.
In addition, several other CLO and MF specialists are entrusted with rms duties and powers.
At CLO level, a formal control of the composition of the VAT IDs of other Member States in sh submitted by German payers is in place.
This formal check is carried out before the provision of SH data to other Member States, to improve the clarity and use of the VIES data provided (see 4.4.2).
Verification of the validity of the VAT IDs specified in the SH is based on the codes O_MCTL provided by other Member States (for the procedure for correcting an invalid VAT ID, see also 4.4.2).
In addition, RMS on CLO is based on VIES data transmitted by other Member States and produces several types of control reports based on several characteristics, which usually feature in the so-called "control system". carousel business operations, in order to identify potential "missing traders".
The tax authorities of the Länder are instructed to process these control reports and, in some cases, report on the results of their CLO findings.
The findings of the BRH audit confirmed that it is necessary to take into account all available characteristics if the existence of a tax fraud case (instead of an exclusive focus on the company's turnover) is to be envisaged with sufficient probability.
The BRH therefore proposed to the MF that different characteristics be taken into account when processing reports.
RMS should also penalise other factors, such as the taxpayer's payment behaviour (morale), the field (of economic activity) or the structure of the shareholders.
The second level of RMS is processed in the tax administrations of the Federal States and focused on the processing of VAT returns.
For example, RMS generates a list of those payers who have reported intra-community delivery in their tax returns.
This list is posted to CLO to monitor the full administration of SH.
In addition, this type of RMS compares intra-Community acquisitions reported in the payer's annual VAT return with data from the VIES system.
The Tax Administration of the Federal States seeks to avoid comparing quarterly data because such comparisons would reveal too much dissenting data, which is attributed to reasons other than tax evasion or tax fraud; Such as:
– different execution time of the intra-Community transaction, in the supplier's view, on the one hand, and the beneficiary on the other;
– different accounting of sales discounts and sales actions (incentives) and their different reporting in the tax return.
In addition to comparing data from VAT returns and VIES, many Federal States have introduced RMS elements based on VAT return data and some other facts (such as the structure of the company name, the age of the shareholders, the number of employees and the taxpayer's payment behaviour/ morality).
Bavaria has introduced rules-based RMS that allow a team of tax fraud specialists (risk managers) to program their own rules for earmarking potential tax fraud perpetrators.
This RMS is applied when the tax authorities process a monthly VAT return.
The competent tax authority will therefore receive a recommendation made by RMS before VAT is determined.
Because this RMS is unable to reflect current findings into its activities, risk managers must adjust the relevant rules based on the feedback from the tax authorities.
The Administrative District of Mecklenburg-Western Pomerania programmed an adaptive artificial neural network with data from tax files in which the inspection detected tax evasion.
On the basis of this data, RMS is able to identify the characteristics of tax evasion.
RMS creates a list of tax files that are suspected of tax evasion once a month.
The competent tax authorities use this list as a basis for auditing decisions of proposed taxpayers.
After the audit, the auditors must report their findings in order to reflect the results of the list into RMS.
The North Rhine-Westphalia administrative region uses an adaptive artificial neural network that is combined with a rules-based fuzzy system.
Based on the large number of data assessed tax returns for VAT and some other facts, this neural-fuzzy system or system of collection of potentially useful information (so-called data-mining system) calculates the likelihood that a particular taxpayer has committed a tax fraud.
It then compiles a monthly list of potential fraud perpetrators.
Local tax authorities use this list as a basis for selecting the relevant taxpayers for inspection and notify the findings of the control to the Data Processing Centre.
The introduction of any of these three RMS in the other Länder is also ongoing.
Given that none of these three RMS are based on the same approach, a combination of all systems seems useful for tackling tax fraud.
The question remains whether this system will lead to the expected results.
Comparison and evaluation
Although the specific RMS criteria in the Czech Republic and Germany cannot be discussed in this report, the SAO and BRH found that each Member State developed its own RMS.
As well as different approaches in the three Federal States of Germany, the RMS of each EU country has its strengths and weaknesses.
Eu Member States' tax authorities are currently discussing new trends and new models of cross-border VAT fraud.
VAT fraud – especially carousel fraud – does not prove to be a national problem, but rather a European problem.
Payers in fraudulent activities act simultaneously not only in one Member State, but in several states.
An effective RMS cannot be developed by only one Member State.
Successful RMS criteria, components and approaches must be exchanged and implemented in each EU Member State, otherwise fraudsters will choose the Member State with the weakest RMS.
The LOSS of VAT caused by fraud in the EU does not have to hit the Member State of the initiator of the fraud.
Any Member State involved in fraudulent activities may be affected.
Therefore, there should be a European exchange and a debate on RMS.
Selected check findings when validating business transactions
In the framework of cooperation on the implementation of parallel control actions, the SAO and BRH examined the quality and use of information on selected business transactions, which were the subject of an international exchange of information between the tax administrations of the Czech Republic and Germany.
Furthermore, the two audit institutions jointly examined the execution of several commercial transactions in which there were doubts as to their implementation or irregularities in the way in which the payers from both countries reported those commercial transactions in their VAT and SH tax returns.
At brh's request, the SAO examined a total of 8 cases involving commercial transactions carried out between 8 Czech and 8 German tax entities.
Furthermore, in 43 cases, the SAO examined the values of intra-Community transactions with Germany reported by Czech payers in their tax returns and SH on the basis of brh notices.
BRH examined a total of 23 cases at the request of the SAO concerning commercial transactions carried out between 23 German and 21 Czech tax entities.
Important information was exchanged on the basis of Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 through official communication with CLO.
By examining selected cases, it was also a case of the use of the product. different way of registering in EU Member States leads to the problems referred to in Chapter 4.1:
1.
According to the data in VIES, the Czech payer was to be acquired in iii. 2004 from the German payer of goods worth EUR 60 500.
Since the Czech payer reported the acquisition of goods only worth EUR 29 869, the Czech tax administrator sent a request to Germany to check the value of the delivered goods.
In response to the ŽOI delivered from germany, the German party stated that in The II. In 2004, the German payer delivered goods worth EUR 27 381 to the Czech payer, in III. eur 31 997 and in IV. 2004, worth EUR 10 276.
Furthermore, the reply showed that the VAT ID of the German payer was valid only from 28 April 2004. 9. 2004, but in 2006, following an additional request from the German payer for the vat ID, the German CLO retroactively issued a certificate of validity of the VAT ID from 1 January 2006. 5. 2004.
The German payer carried out the SH correction.
For the Czech payer, on the basis of this information, it was the acquisition of goods.
The SAO found that the Czech taxpayer, following an investigation by the tax administrator, submitted additional VAT returns for each tax year 2004, in which he increased the value of goods acquired from other Member States and at the same time claimed the right to deduct VAT on the acquisition of goods from other Member States.
However, from these additional VAT returns, the Czech tax administrator could not clearly determine whether the values of deliveries from the above-mentioned German supplier were included.
Brh found, at the request of the SAO, that the German supplier had been registered for VAT in September 2003.
However, since he did not ask for a VAT ID when registering, he was assigned only an identification number for transactions within germany.
Although it is usually not possible to assign a VAT ID retroactively to a payer in Germany, in this case the German tax officer in 2006 retroactively assigned the VAT ID to the aforementioned German payer VAT as of 1.5.2004.
The German CLO allocates the VAT ID retroactively, unless the German entrepreneur caused a delay in the allocation; for example, if the delay was caused by CLO after the payer's request for a VAT ID.
In this case, CLO allocates the VAT ID retroactively because the entrepreneur does not need his own valid VAT ID for intra-Community delivery under Section 6 of the German VAT Act.
On the other hand, the German consignee does not need a valid VAT ID of his supplier in order to report intra-Community acquisitions.
Because of these different procedures between Member States, the German DUTY in this particular case allocated the VAT ID retroactively.
2.
The Czech tax administrator requested, as part of the international exchange of information on the verification of the registration of the German payer for VAT.
VIES listed the date of registration 5. 3. 2005, the date 1 January 2005 of the German payer's registration certificate issued by the german tax authority at the locally competent tax office indicated the date of 1 January 2005. 10. 2004.
In a reply received from Germany, the German party stated that the German tax entity had been registered from 1 January 2004. 10. 2004, but the VAT ID was granted to him in Germany for organisational reasons until 16 December 2004. 2. 2005.

For the tax year III. In the quarter of 2004, the tax office paid VAT of CZK 1,880 (EUR 60) to the tax entity.
BRH found, at the request of the SAO, the German payer's VAT ID had been assigned up to 16. 2. 2005, when he informed the Tax Office of his business, which he started in 2004.
In addition, the tax office registered it for VAT retrospectively on 1 January 2004. In order to monitor the submission of the annual VAT return for 2004, it is necessary to monitor the submission of the annual VAT return for 2004.

3. The Czech payer declared in the VAT return for September 2004 and sh for III. In 2004, the delivery of goods worth CZK 114,615 (EUR 3,642) to the German payer.
When verifying the registration of the German payer in VIES, the Czech tax administrator found that his registration was valid from 11 January 2004. 11. 2004, i.e. after the delivery of the goods by the Czech payer to Germany.
The Czech payer submitted an additional DAP for VAT, in which he declared a taxable amount on the transactions carried out in the country of CZK 114,615 (EUR 3,642) and VAT of CZK 21,777 (EUR 692) paid.
By asking the local tax authority in the Czech Republic, the SAO found that the Czech payer subsequently submitted a request for a retrial in respect of an additional VAT return and as an evidence he submitted a confirmation to the German tax administration that the German payer had been tax-led since 1 January 2004. 1. 2000.
Therefore, the Czech tax administrator verified the validity of the registration of the German payer in the framework of the international exchange of information.
The reply received from Germany showed that the Vat ID had not been assigned to the German payer until 11 December 2004. 11. 2004, i.e. after the date of delivery of the goods.
For this reason, the tax administrator in the Czech Republic rejected the request for a retrial.
BRH found that the case was not an intra-Community acquisition of goods because the German payer received the VAT ID up to 11.11.2004.
However, the German beneficiary declared the acquisition as an intra-Community acquisition and declared VAT on that acquisition when it requested an input tax refund in the same amount.
However, in the absence of changes in the value of VAT which the German payer was obliged to pay, the tax administrator in Germany did not correct the information in his VAT return.
Furthermore, BRH found that the name of the German payer referred to in ŽOI was changed during the processing of the reply in Germany, resulting in a confusion between two German tax entities.
This change in the name of the German payer also confused the Czech tax administrator.
4.
As part of the international exchange of information, the German tax administrator verified the acquisition of goods by the Czech payer in the first quarter of 2005, worth EUR 22 686 from the German payer.
By asking the local tax administrator in the Czech Republic, the SAO found that the administrator carried out a local investigation with the Czech payer, in which he verified that the delivery of the goods had taken place and that the Czech payer had posted and paid the invoice for the goods in question.
The Czech payer did not admit the acquisition of the goods in the VAT return because the German supplier did not indicate his VAT ID on the tax document, but only the tax number intended for national transactions in Germany.
In the VIES application, the Czech tax administrator found that the German payer had been registered for VAT for intra-Community transactions only from 21 January 2004. 4. 2005, i.e. after the delivery to the Czech payer has been carried out.
At the same time, the Czech tax administrator asked the German tax administration to send a copy of the German payer's registration certificate so that he could take steps to assess the tax if necessary.
The Czech Tax Office assessed the transaction as the acquisition of goods from a non-payer from Germany and therefore did not subsequently assess the tax on the Czech payer from that business transaction.
BRH found that, under German legislation, a payer who supplies goods to other Member States does not have to have a VAT ID assigned in order for intra-Community supplies of goods to be exempt from VAT.
The supplier must only have at his disposal the VAT ID of the pro-customer from another Member State and must be able to prove the transport of the goods in question to another Member State.
According to the German VAT Act, this was therefore an intra-Community transaction and VAT should be levied in the Czech Republic.
In any event, it is important that the Czech tax administrator noticed this transaction because the delivery of the machine at that value was not the basic business of the German supplier.
As described in Chapter 4.6.2, the German CLO refuses to reply to the ZOI concerning intra-Community transactions of less than EUR 15 000: 5.

Since the Czech tax administrator did not obtain the means of proof for the assessment of the tax on the goods acquired, he terminated the tax audit without finding it and the tax liability remained measured in the original amount.
Brh found, at the request of the SAO, that the German payer had acted as a so-called "payer". "fiscal representative" (§ 22 a – e UStG).
The German payer reported those deliveries in his annual VAT return and in SH.
He was granted the right to receive the exemption.

12.
In the context of the international exchange of information, the German tax administrator requested, by means of the SCAC form, to verify the supply of goods and services carried out in III. quarter 2005.

In response to ŽOI, the Czech tax administrator stated that the Czech payer had supplied the German payer with a production line, including assembly.
The individual parts of the production line were delivered by the Czech payer before the Czech Republic's accession to the EU and after 1 January 2004. 5. 2004 the line was assembled on the basis of an order.
The German payer did not take over the assembled line because he claimed to have defects.

In this particular case, the place of the so-called where the production line has been installed.
Under the German VAT Act, the German recipient of the service is obliged to pay VAT.
At the same time, the beneficiary may claim the deduction of VAT on the same amount.
In the absence of changes in the value of VAT that the German payer was obliged to pay, the corrections in the VAT return were neglected by the German tax authority.
13. Czech payer A was to purchase a machine worth EUR 58 000 from the German payer C in February 2005, according to data from VIES.
The Czech tax administrator sent a request to Germany for the examination of this supply.
In response to the ŽOI, the German side stated that the machine had already been delivered by German payer C to the Czech payer B in 2004, but was to return the machine to German payer C in October 2004.
According to the information of the German tax administration, the machine was not transported back to Germany, but transported to the organizational unit of the German payer C in the Czech Republic.
Furthermore, it emerged from the response to a request for information that the German payer C sold the machine to Czech payer A in February 2005.
This payer took over the machine at the headquarters of the organizational unit of the German payer C in the Czech Republic.
Since the delivery took place only within the Czech Republic, it was not an intra-community delivery of goods.
The SAO, by asking the tax administrator of the locally competent payer B, found that, according to VIES data, the German payer C supplied in III. in the quarter of 2004 to the Czech payer B goods (another machine) worth EUR 88 027.
The payer B denied this acquisition of the goods, therefore the local tax administrator from the Czech Republic sent the ŽOI to Germany.
According to the response to this request, the delivery of the machine took place.
By further investigation with payer B, the Czech tax administrator found that the machine worth EUR 88 027 was not in the accounts of payer B and that it could be a machine of the same type as the german payer C's organisational unit to the Czech payer A in February 2005.
Furthermore, the SAO found that the Czech tax administrator had carried out a local investigation on the local payer A.
The tax administrator had at his disposal an invoice from the German payer C of 7 December 2004. 2. 2005, to which payer A was listed as a customer of the machine.
The Czech tax administrator found that payer A does not have this invoice included in the accounting.
The payer A had a leasing contract with another Czech company, where the subject of the lease was a machine of the same type.
The handover of the machine from the leasing company took place on 9. 2. 2005, the transport of the machine was provided by a leasing company.
The information contained in the response to the request for information was not used by the Czech tax office to determine the tax liability of payer A.
BRH found that the German payer C did not deliver the machine to the Czech Republic, but to another German payer D.
It was therefore not an intra-Community supply of goods, but a taxable supply in Germany.
For these reasons, the German tax administrator did not recognise the German payer C's VAT exemption and corrected the data in his tax return.
German payer D supplied the machine to the Czech payer B.
According to German legislation, this supply was not taxable in Germany, but was subject to VAT in the Czech Republic.
Furthermore, BRH found that german payer C reported in its SH for the first quarter of 2005 the delivery of the machine worth EUR 58 000 to the Czech payer A.
This supply was not examined during the tax audit carried out by the German tax authority.

Vat on the sale of goods in Germany was not included in the Czech VAT return.
The Czech tax administrator assessed the additional VAT return unchanged after the local investigation.
According to Czech legislation, the above case did not take the goods from other Member States because the goods were not shipped or transported from another Member State to the Czech Republic.
The Czech tax administrator therefore made an incorrect conclusion of the local investigation.
BRH found that, immediately after receiving the reply to the ŽOI, which stated that the goods had not left Germany, the German tax return had been corrected and claimed VAT of EUR 1 600.
In addition, the competent tax authority has sent a notification to the tax authority of the actual recipient of the goods to ensure that the resale of those goods is properly taxed.

BRH found that the German tax administrator responsible, on the basis of the Czech reply to the ŽOI, would not recognise the German payer's right to exempt that supply from VAT.
19. During the inspection, the German tax authority was unable to clarify the difference of EUR 3000 between the value of the goods acquired and the value granted from another Member State.
It was communicated that the Czech payer should have delivered during IV. quarter 2004 to 2005 to the German payer of goods worth EUR 89 424.
Since the acquisition declared by the German payer did not correspond to the data in VIES, the German tax administrator requested the verification of supplies and their payment in the context of the international exchange of information.
In response to the ŽOI, the Czech tax administrator stated that the sole managing director of the Czech company had been deleted from the Commercial Register on 8 December 2004. 7. 2005 and the new managing director was not registered.
The German recipient of the goods was apparently related to a companion of the Czech company.
The Czech payer filed both VAT and SH tax returns, which, after the deletion of the executive from the Commercial Register, was signed by an unauthorised person – the said partner of the company.
The accounting officer of the Czech tax payer confirmed to the tax administrator that the company's shareholder had deposited the cash paid for the invoiced goods in EUR into the company's account.
Cash documents were not issued.
The SAO in the Czech Republic found that the tax administrator had recognized the Czech payer as IV. In the quarter of 2004, the right to exemption from VAT on the supply of goods to another Member State of CZK 1,326,307 (EUR 42 145) and CZK 1,416,180 (EUR 47 548) for qi 1.
BRH found that the tax administrator in Germany had not corrected the Vat return of the German acquirer because the German judge had in the meantime confirmed the insolventness of the German payer.
Since the previous check did not reveal any signs of tax fraud, it will not be possible to recover the assessed tax liability.
20. According to the data in VIES, in 2005, the German payer purchased goods worth EUR 4 251 196 from the Czech Republic after acquiring goods worth EUR 43 274 in the previous year.
In the 2004 tax return or in the 2005 tax return, the German payer did not report an intra-community acquisition.
Furthermore, it did not report reasonable supplies.
Because of these differences, the German tax authority, ŽOI, sent a copy of the report to the Commission on 4 April 2004. 2005 and 1 December 2005. quarter 2006.
The Czech supplier reported intra-Community delivery of goods to the German payer for the two quarters in the two quarters, with a total value of CZK 167,246,083 (EUR 5,615,299).
On 6 June 2005, the Council adopted Decision 9. 2006 was delivered to the ŽOI, in which the German party requested to check whether the Czech payer of reported intra-community supplies had been made.
In response to this ŽOI, the Czech tax administration stated that the german side's request could not be met because the Czech payer had no managing director.
As is apparent from the materials provided by the SAO to the competent tax administrator, on 30 June 2005, the commission decided to initiate the procedure laid down in Article 88(2) of the EC On 3. 2006, a protocol on the opening of the VAT control for IV was drawn up with the managing director of the Czech payer. 2004 and January to December 2005.
At the same time, the payer was invited by the tax administrator to submit all accounting and tax documents for the above periods, but he did not submit any documents.
According to the Commercial Register, the sole managing officer of the Czech payer ceased to be a member of the Office of the Czech Payer. 5. 2006, a new managing director was not appointed.
Since April 2006, the Czech payer has stopped submitting VAT returns.
As part of the SAO's control in cooperation with BRH, he examined, among other things, several cases of intra-Community supplies made between the Czech Republic and Germany that were not the subject of a previous exchange of information between the tax administrations of the two countries.
Information on the cases examined was transmitted by the two SAIs through the CLO of both countries.
21. The Czech company (eCR) which is not resident in Germany has informed the competent tax authority (Chemnitz-Süd) that it intends to carry out a taxable transaction in Germany.
Because of this information, the company has been registered since June 2005 but has not received a German VAT ID.
(ECR) has received an order from a Danish entrepreneur (eDK) for the production of several wind farms and for the supply of these wind farms on behalf, at risk and on behalf of a Danish customer to Austria.
Due to the lack of own capacity, the Czech company handed over part of the order to the German payer (eD), which is based in Germany.
The following diagram shows the contractual relations and the method of transport of wind farms:
According to the German legal situation, the place of execution of these transactions must be determined according to the following:
– The Danish entrepreneur (eDK) sent wind farms to be installed under his name, at his risk and his account to Austria.
Since the installation of this supply took place in Austria, the supply of wind farms is taxable in Austria.
– Since the carrier was instructed by a Danish entrepreneur (eDK) and the transport took place under his name, at his risk and on his own account, the delivery of the German subcontractor (eD) took place where the transport began – in Germany.
Although wind farms were dispatched to another Member State and the beneficiary is a registered payer from another Member State, the supply of a German subcontractor (eD) could not receive an exemption because another Member State of destination differs from another Member State of the registered office of the Czech company.
This supply is therefore correctly taxed in Germany and the Czech company (eCZ) deducted the input tax in its tax returns.
The place of delivery of the Czech company (eCR) is also determined by the beginning of transport.
Transport of some wind farms started in the Czech Republic and others in Germany.
– The delivery of those wind farms that are produced in the Czech Republic took place in the Czech Republic.
– The supply of other wind farms produced in Germany took place in Germany.
Thus, the Czech company (eCR) carried out both intra-Community delivery from the Czech Republic to Austria and intra-Community delivery from Germany to Austria.
BRH found that the Czech company (eCR) did not report any intra-Community acquisitions in its VAT return in Germany or to sh to the German CLO.
So it is possible that the Czech company reported all intra-Community delivery uniformly as intra-Community delivery from the Czech Republic.
The SAO found that (eCR) reported no intra-Community delivery to Austria, but intra-Community delivery to Denmark.
A verification of the taxation of intra-Community acquisitions in Austria would require the cooperation of at least four tax administrations (Austrian, Czech, Danish and German), although this case shows no evidence of tax fraud or evasion.
Furthermore, the SAO and BRH examined the transactions in order to highlight the differences between the declaration in the tax return and the VIES data, which were caused by different VAT rules in 2004.
The cases audited also demonstrate that changes in legislation need time to put new legislation into practice by both payers and tax authorities:
22. In SH for II. to IV. In the quarter of 2004, the Czech payer reported intra-Community delivery to the German payer with a total value of CZK 792,977,452 (EUR 25,197,885).
Over the same period, another Czech payer in SH reported intra-Community delivery to another German payer with a total value of CZK 18,157,265 (EUR 576 970).
According to the information provided by the SAO from BRH, in both cases it was a supply of electricity.
Both Czech payers reported the above deliveries in SH in accordance with the wording of Act No. 235/2004 Coll., in force in 2004.
By further examining the above transactions, the SAO control group found that in 2004 there were differences in the legal arrangements for the supply or acquisition of electricity between the Czech Republic and Germany.
While in the Czech Republic the payers reported the supply of electricity in accordance with the valid version of Act No. 235/2004 Coll. as intra-Community delivery of goods, from the point of view of the German legal regulation in force in 2004 it was not an intra-Community acquisition, but a taxable transaction with the place of performance in the territory of germany.
The difference in legal regulations in the Czech Republic was eliminated by the adoption of Act No. 635/2004 Coll., which amends certain laws in connection with the adoption of the Act on Administrative Fees, effective from 1. 1. 2005.
23. In the examination of selected intra-Community transactions in cooperation with BRH, it was further found that the Czech payer reported in SH for 1 January 2004 that the czech payer had reported in THE SH for 1 January 2004, the commission had not been granted the right to pay. to 4 May 2005. In the quarter of 2005, intra-Community delivery to a German payer with a total value of CZK 240,411,163 (EUR 8,071,823) and another Czech payer reported intra-community delivery to the German payer for the same period, totalling EUR 263,470,776 (EUR 8,846,050).
According to the information provided by the SAO from BRH, in both cases it was a supply of electricity.
According to the wording of Act No. 235/2004 Coll., effective from 1 January 2004, the commission has been in force since 1 January 2004. 1. 2005, in the case of supply of electricity, the place of supply of electricity shall be the place of supply of electricity, the place where the purchaser has its registered office, the place of business or the establishment for which the goods are supplied.
Therefore, Czech payers should not have entered into the supply of electricity to SH in 2005.
The fact that the two payers mentioned above reported intra-community supply of electricity in SH distorted the data in VIES by a total of CZK 503,881,939 (EUR 16,917 873).
Conclusion
The cooperation met the objectives of BRH and the SAO.
Both SAI gained a deeper knowledge of the VAT management systems in the Czech Republic and Germany.
The cooperation revealed the differences between the two systems and showed that the legislation in the field of VAT management differed.
Suspicious cases of intra-Community transactions were detected during parallel checks.
Some of them make sense to examine them afterwards.
On the basis of the control findings, the two SAI made recommendations on VAT management.
Monitoring these recommendations should also be part of a follow-up.
The new experience and knowledge gained through the cooperation of the two control institutions are the basis for the successful implementation of the following VAT management checks.

The report was prepared in Czech, English and German and signed by the President of the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the President of the Bundesrechnungshof, The Federal Republic of Germany.
Report on the outcome of international cooperation in the controls of excise duty management between the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic in 2006
Introductory word
The present joint report shall inform about the progress and outcome of international cooperation in parallel checks carried out by the Supreme Audit Office, the Czech Republic and the Najvyšší control office of the Slovak Republic, focused on the management of excise duties in the period after the entry of the two countries into the European Union.
The cooperation was carried out on the basis of a cooperation agreement in control activities concluded in February 2006.
The topic of parallel controls was selected in view of the fundamental change in the system of collection of excise duties, which took place in connection with the integration of the Czech Republic and the Slovak Republic into the internal market of the European Union from 1 January 2004. They shall forthed 2004.
The functioning of the European Union's internal market requires the free movement of goods, including excise goods.
The basic principle is to allow the circulation of uninterdened goods until the date of delivery for final consumption.
In accordance with that principle, the new legislation adopted in both countries allows the movement of goods under tax supervision under the conditional exemption regime.
The system places great demands on tax authorities and foresees close synergies between the competent administrations of the Member States in the fight against tax fraud in this area.

The subject of the contract was cooperation in parallel checks "Administration of excise duties", included in the plan of control activities of the SAO-CR for 2005 under No. 05/34, and "Control of the procedure of colny authorities in the management of consumption taxes", included in the plan of control activities of the SAO SR for 2006 under No. 48/11.

2. Administration of excise duties
The administration of excise duties in the Czech Republic was carried out by 31 December 2004. The financial authorities shall for the purposes of this Regulation.
From 1 January 2005, the This was taken over by the customs authorities, which had so far collected excise duty only on importation.
Mineral oils, alcohol, beer, wine and intermediate products and tobacco products are subject to excise duty in the Czech Republic.
In 2004, the state budget income from excise duties in the Czech Republic totalled EUR 82.8 billion. czk and on the revenue of the state budget from taxes and fees of CZK 424.7 billion. 19.5% of excise duties.
In 2005, the state budget income from excise duties amounted to EUR 103.6 billion. czk and share of the state budget revenues from taxes and charges in the amount of CZK 460.4 billion. CZK was 22.5%.
In 2004, the excise duty on mineral oils to the state budget amounted to 80 % of the total revenue from that tax and in 2005 it was 90,9 %.
The difference to 100 % of EUR 13 billion is not the same as the eur 13 billion difference. in 2004 and CZK 6.9 billion in 2004. Czk in 2005 was the income of the State Transport Infrastructure Fund.
The administration of all excise duties in the Czech Republic shall be carried out by the customs authorities from 1 January 2005. In the 10th ly administered the provisions of This Regulation, the competent authorities of the Council of 15 May 2004 on the use of mineral oil excise duties shall be exempted from the provisions of This Regulation. 1, 2002.
Until then, the administration of excise duties was carried out by the tax authorities.
Excise duty in SR is subject to mineral oil, alcohol, beer, wine and tobacco products.
In 2004, the state budget income from excise duties in the Czech Technical Union was EUR 43.4 billion. and total tax revenues of EUR 209.5 billion. Sk accounted for 20.7% of excise duty.

The legislation in both countries is based on European Union rules on this area, in particular: - Council Directive 92/12/EEC on the general arrangements for the holding, movement and monitoring of products subject to excise duty (hereinafter referred to as "Directive 92/12/EEC"), - Commission Regulation (EC) No 2073/2004 on administrative cooperation in the field of excise duties (hereinafter referred to as "Regulation No 2073/2004"), - Commission Regulation (EEC) No 2073/2004 2719/92 on the accompanying official document for the transport of products subject to excise duty under the excise duty suspension scheme (hereinafter referred to as 'Regulation No 2719/92'), - Commission Regulation (EEC) No No 3649/92 on a simplified accompanying document for the movement within the Community of products subject to excise duty which have been released for domestic consumption in the Member State of dispatch (hereinafter referred to as 'Regulation No 3649/92').
The basic legislation regulating the issue of excise duties in the Czech Republic is Act No. 353/2003 Coll., on Excise Duties, as amended, (hereinafter referred to as "Act No. 353/2003 Coll.") effective from 1. They shall forthwith inform the Commission of the 15 January 2004
In the management of excise duties in the Czech Republic, the customs authorities are, inter alia, the competent authorities of the European Union. bound by the following generally binding legislation: - Act No. 98/2004 Z. z. o consumer tax on mineral oil and in the pollution of non-corrupt prescriptions (hereinafter referred to as "Act No. 98/2004 Z. z."), - Act No. 104/2004 Z. z. o consumer tax on wine in the invalidity of non-glassy prescriptions (hereinafter referred to as "Act No. 104/2004 Z. z.), - Act No. 105/2004 Z. z. on the consumer tax on lieh in the non-corrupt regulations (hereinafter referred to as "Act No. 105/2004 Z. z." - Act No. 106/2004 Z. z. on the consumer tax on tabak products (hereinafter referred to as "Act No. 106/2004 Z. z." - Act No. 107/2004 Z. z. on the consumer tax on beer in the pollution of non-skorších predpisov (hereinafter referred to as "Act No. 107/2004 Z. z.").
2.1. Movement of excise goods under the conditional exemption procedure between Member States of the European Union
The conditions for the movement of excise goods under the suspensive exemption procedure are laid down in Directive 92/12/EEC in Title III — Movement of goods 15 to 20.
Under those provisions, only an authorised storekeeper who means a natural or legal person authorised by the competent authorities of a Member State to manufacture, process, store, receive and dispatch products subject to excise duty may carry out such goods.
The consignee in another Member State may be an authorised warehousekeeper or an economic operator without the status of authorised warehousekeeper, who may not, however, store or continue to resussign those products under the suspensive exemption procedure.
An authorised warehouse provider in the Czech Republic and in the Czech Republic means the operator of the tax warehouse, the economic operator is the authorized recipient for the repeated or one-time reception of products subject to excise duty.
The movement of products subject to excise duty under the suspensive procedure is only possible with an accompanying document under Directive 92/12/EEC.
The accompanying document shall be issued by the consignor in four copies before the start of the service, unless the competent authorities of the Member State of dispatch require a further copy.
2.2 Procedure for the commencement and termination of the transport of goods under the conditional exemption procedure between the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic
Transport from the Czech Republic
The procedure for the start of transport is governed by the provisions of § 25 para. 3 of Act No. 353/2003 Coll., where, inter alia, the Shown:
'The tax warehouse operator shall inform the customs office which is located at the relevant tax warehouse from which the transport is to commence before the transport of the selected products commences;
the transport of selected products may be commenced only with the agreement of that customs office.
The customs office shall give its consent to the transport of the products selected without delay after the condition of securing the tax has been fulfilled..."'
The consignor in the Czech Republic can start transporting all types of products subject to excise duty only with the consent of the local customs office.
The customs office shall give its consent to the commencement of transport only if a security of the tax at the rate of the tax attributable to the products transported is provided.
The consignor is obliged to draw up an accompanying document in five copies before the start of transport.
On the accompanying document, the customs office shall indicate the consent to the commencement of the transport.
Copy No 1 shall be kept by the consignor, copy 2, 3, and 4 shall be kept by the consignor to the carrier and copy No 5 shall be kept by the customs office authorising the transport.
According to Slovak legislation, the consignee in slovakia retains copy No 2 of the accompanying document. At copies Nos 3 and 4, they shall confirm receipt of the products and shall submit both copies to the customs office competent locally.
Copy No 3 certified by the customs office shall send to the consignor not later than 15 September 2005 at the latest. the day of the month following the calendar month in which it accepted the products.
Copy No 4 shall be kept by the customs office of the consignee.
Transport is terminated by acceptance of products by the consignee.
The customs office in the Czech Republic, which authorised the commencement of the transport, shall decide on the release of the tax security within 5 working days of the presentation of copy No 3 of the accompanying document, which is confirmed by the consignee and the Slovak customs office.

For the transport of other products subject to excise duty (mineral oil, wine and beer) during the period from 1 January 2005 to 31 December 2006, the total supply of goods and services shall be subject to the prices of mineral oil, wine and beer. They shall forth with the time before 31 May 2004 the The tax body was not obliged to notify the Customs Office of Poprad or the competent customs office of the commencement of transport under the conditional exemption procedure.
The tax administrator only became aware of the transport of these products during the local investigation or during the tax check from the accompanying documents and from the accounting documents of the tax entity.
The consignor in SR is obliged to draw up an accompanying document in four copies before the start of transport.
Copy No 1 shall be kept by the consignor (when transporting alcohol and tobacco products, he shall send a copy of copy No 1 electronically or by fax to the Customs Office of Poprad and the competent customs office).
Copies Nos 2, 3 and 4 shall accompany the goods transported.
According to Czech legislation, the recipient in the Czech Republic will keep copy No. 2 of the accompanying document issued by the consignor in The Czech Republic and on copies Nos. 3 and 4 the receipt of the products.
Certified copies Nos. 3 and 4 shall be sent no later than the first working day after the end of the transport to the local customs office in the Czech Republic.
The customs office shall keep copy No 4 and copy No 3, at which it shall verify the accuracy and validity, be returned to the consignee.
The consignee shall send the certified copy No 3 no later than the following working day after its receipt to the consignor to the SR.
Transport in the SR shall be deemed to have been completed on the date of receipt of the products by the consignee.
The termination of the transport is demonstrated by the consignor by submitting copy No. 3 of the accompanying document certified by the recipient and the tax administrator in the Czech Republic.
