In 2006, amendments to all excise laws were progressively adopted in the Czech Republic, according to which the consignor of goods under the conditional exemption procedure is obliged to send a copy of copy No 1 of the accompanying document electronically or by fax to the customs office of the local consignor before the start of transport.
The document proving the cessation of the transport of pouring alcohol and tobacco products shall be copy No 3 of the accompanying document certified by the consignee and his competent tax administrator.
The document proving the completion of the transport of mineral oils, wine and beer is copy No 3 certified by the consignee.
Confirmation by the tax administrator of another Member State of receipt of those goods by the consignee shall be required if the consignee is obliged, under the legislation of the Member State concerned, to certify copy No 3 of the accompanying document.
2.3 Records of commenced and completed transports carried out by customs authorities in the Czech Republic and In The Slovak Republic
There is no single electronic system in place to monitor the transport of goods under the conditional exemption procedure between The Member States of the European Union.
Decision 1152/2003/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16 December 2003 amending Decision 1152/2003/EC on the application of the system of certain products of food It requires the Member States and the European Commission to introduce, from 1 January 2003, an electronic system for the transport and monitoring of products subject to excise duty. The electronic system (Excise Movement and Control System) which would allow excise tax authorities in each Member State to obtain real-time information on the transport of goods in each Member State.
The system will allow the electronic transmission of accompanying documents, which are currently only used in paper form, and will contribute to the simplified movement of goods under the suspensive exemption procedure and to ensure more effective control of the movement of unsu taxpayers' products across all Member States.
This system will include national databases for national transports.
The Customs Administration of the Czech Republic records all transports initiated and terminated in the Territory of the Czech Republic in the Module Registration of Selected Products (hereinafter referred to as "EVV").
All customs authorities in the Czech Republic have access to the system online.
In the case of transports carried out only in the Territory of the Czech Republic, the tax authorities can obtain information about the commencement or termination of transport immediately after the registration of the accompanying document by the customs office to the EVV.
The customs office shall release the security of the tax on the goods transported by the consignor at the time of registration of the termination of transport by the customs office of the local consignee.
The customs authorities in the SR use a database based on the SysNed application software, which ensures the automation of their activities in the management of excise duties and communication with the systems of the European Union.
By registering the tax warehouse, tax warehouse operator or authorized recipient in the SysNed application software, this information is automatically transferred to the "System for Exchange of Excise Data" database (hereinafter referred to as "SEED").
3. Preparation and cooperation
The first coordination meeting between representatives of the SAO-CR and representatives of the SAO SR, at which a specific procedure for cooperation in the implementation of parallel controls in the field of excise duties was discussed, took place in January 2006.
The two sides became familiar with excise legislation and the organisation of excise tax management in both states.
Particular attention was paid to the procedure of the customs authorities of the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic in the authorisation or in the initiation and cessation of transport of products subject to excise duty under the conditional exemption procedure and the exchange of information between the excise tax authorities of both countries.
At the meeting it was agreed that the Czech and Slovak parties: - will process the total data on the quantity of excise goods transported from the Czech Republic to slovakia and vice versa, whose transport was started during the controlled period - compare data on transports of mineral oils - combined nomenclature code 2710 and 2711 and alcohol - combined nomenclature code 2207 and 2208 under the conditional exemption scheme initiated in the Czech Republic and terminated in the Slovak Republic and vice versa in the months of November 2004 and September 2005.
During the checks, the periods examined were extended to October and November 2005 and the transport of tobacco products under the conditional exemption scheme was also subject to control in those months.
Tables 1 and No 2 show the total quantity of products subject to excise duty which have been transported under the conditional exemption scheme between Czech and Slovak tax entities during the period audited.
4. Comparison of records of the transport of goods under the suspensive exemption procedure
The SAO-CR handed over to the Slovak side a database of transports completed in the Czech Republic, which contained a total of 5,876 items listed on the accompanying documents, of which 5,738 items related to mineral oils, 134 items of alcohol and 4 items of tobacco products.
The SAO SR forwarded to the Czech side a database of transports completed in the Slovak Republic containing a total of 3,319 items on the accompanying documents, of which 696 were covered mineral oil, 2 066 items of alcohol and 557 items of tobacco products.
The SAO-ČR compared the data on the transports mentioned in the records of the commenced transports in the Czech Republic with the data on completed transports registered in the Slovak Republic.
The results of the comparison are given in Table 3.
Data on transports in the months of November 2004 and September 2005 compared the SAO-CR with the database of the Slovak customs administration, which was transmitted to him by the SAO SR at the beginning of the inspection.
The database did not contain data to reliably reconcile individual transports, and therefore only 63% of the traffic started was assigned.
Individual transports were assigned according to multiple data, e.g. consignor, consignee, date of transport, quantity of products transported.
Data on transports started in the Czech Republic and completed in slovakia in the months of October and November 2005 were compared by the SAO-CR with the Slovak Customs Administration database, which contained all the data according to the accompanying documents, on the basis of which 93% of the commenced transports were clearly assigned.
In the database of the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic, data on the amount of mineral oils were given in litres or tonnes depending on the type of mineral oil.
In most cases, the amount of alcohol was indicated in litres, but it was possible to convert it into litres of absolute alcohol on the basis of the database of the percentage of alcohol.
The quantity of tobacco products was indicated in pieces, in thousands of pieces and kilograms by type of tobacco products.
For shipments initiated in the Czech Republic, the termination of which was not reliably verified in the Slovak database or for which the indication of the quantity of products transported was not matched, an inspection of the accompanying documents was carried out.
The accompanying documents for 487 transports of alcohol, mineral oils and tobacco products were subjected to the inspection.
Checks of these documents were carried out at the customs offices at which the SAO-CR carried out the inspection.
For transports authorised by other customs offices, accompanying documents were requested through DGC.
The Czech side asked the Slovak side to verify the implementation of 141 transports, for which the customs authorities in the Czech Republic have not documented the certified copy No. 3 of the accompanying document, or the quantity of products indicated on the accompanying document did not agree with the quantity of products listed in the database.
Furthermore, data on transports registered in the Slovak database were transmitted to the Slovak side, but the database did not contain the transport database of the Czech customs administration.
The SU SR found 95 transports in the Slovak Customs Administration database.
The remaining 46 transports were verified by the local customs authorities, which have been provided with copies of the accompanying documents.
The Slovak side forwarded copies of the accompanying documents to the Czech side, on the basis of which the transport was also identified in the Czech database, with the exception of transports carried out by two Czech tax entities, which were not found in the Czech database of commenced transports.
By checking these cases, the following were found to be:
- 11 shipments of alcohol were recorded in the Slovak transport database in total quantities of 276.7 litres of alcohol carried out by the Czech tax entity in 2004 and 20 liters of alcohol transport in total in 2005.
The SAO-CR found that it was the transport of taxed products, for which the sender does not need the consent of the tax administrator.
The consignor informed the tax administrator in writing of the commencement of the transport. He carried out the transport on the basis of accompanying documents used for the transport of products under the suspensive exemption scheme;
- a total of 94 transports of mineral oils were registered in the Slovak transport database, combined nomenclature code 2710 11 21, totalling 173,000. litres carried out by the Czech tax entity between September 2004 and December 2005.
The SAO-CR found that between May 2004 and June 2005, the tax entity carried out transport of 102,000. litres of un taxed mineral oils without proper authorisation.
The tax entity held a special authorisation for the reception and use of exempt products, on the basis of which the un taxed products could only be supplied to the holder of the same authorisation.
The commencement of transport to the customs office in the Czech Republic was not notified and he did not provide a tax security of CZK 1,207,680 for the products transported.
Between July 2005 and December 2005, the tax entity shipped 71,000 in the territory of the SR. litres of taxed mineral oils. Even in these cases, he did not fulfil his legal obligation by not notifying the customs office of the commencement of the transport.
The consignor may start transport of products placed for free tax circulation in the tax territory of the Czech Republic to another Member State without the consent of the customs office, but he is obliged to inform the customs office in writing before the start of transport.
A tax entity collecting products put into free circulation in another Member State is obliged to report the quantity and ensure vat before removing them.
Products may be transported only with a simplified accompanying document, the essentials of which are regulated by Regulation No 3649/92.
This Regulation also permits the use of the accompanying document for transport under the suspensive exemption procedure, on which it must be clearly indicated that it is a 'simplified accompanying document for the purposes of tax control (excise products)'.
The same legislation on transport and the admission of products put into free circulation in another Member State also applies in the SR.
In those cases, the tax operators transported the products put into free circulation with an accompanying document for transport under a suspensive exemption procedure, the 3rd ed amount of which was granted on 3 December 1998. and 4. the beneficiary has been submitted to the tax authorities in the SR for verification.
The customs authorities in the Slovak Customs Have registered these services in the database under the conditional exemption procedure, since the accompanying documents did not indicate that it was a simplified accompanying document.
The SAO SR compared the database of transport of the Czech customs administration with the database of transport of the Slovak customs administration and found:
- the quantity of products transported has been reported inconsistently in the databases, e.g. in the case of the quantities of products transported; mineral oil is indicated in litres, in hectolitres or in kilograms; the alcohol was indicated in litres or litres of alcohol, making it more difficult to compare the quantity of goods transported,
- the quantity of alcohol transported in the invoices did not match the quantity recorded in the databases,
- not all related invoices were included in the databases,
- in the database of the Slovak customs administration, two transports of alcohol from the Czech Republic to Slovakia were registered in November 2004 in the total volume of 47 237 liters of alcohol, which were not in the database of the Czech customs administration.
The Slovak party handed over copies of the accompanying documents to the Czech party.
5. International exchange of information between the customs authorities of the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic
The conditions for cooperation between the administrative authorities of the Member States responsible for the management of excise duties were governed by 30 June 2005. It is necessary to provide for the assistance of the member states' competent authorities in the field of direct taxation, certain excise duties and insurance premium taxes.
On 1 January 2005, the Council adopted Decision Regulation No 2073/2004 lays down rules and procedures allowing the competent authorities of the Member States of the European Union to cooperate and exchange the information necessary for the correct assessment of excise duties.
Each Member State shall designate a central liaison office which shall ensure contacts with other Member States in the field of excise management and shall be responsible for the exchange of information on the movement of excise goods.
In the Czech Republic, the report "Excise Liaison Office" (hereinafter referred to as "ELO ČR") was set up at DGC to ensure the exchange of information in the field of excise duties between Member States of the European Union.
The security of tasks related to the management of systems for the control of the movement of excise goods (SEED, MVS, EWSE) and the exchange of information in the framework of mutual administrative assistance between the Member States of the European Union and the SR shall be carried out with effect from 1 January 2007. The office of ELO at the Customs Office of Poprad was asked to do so by 15 May 2004.
With effect from 1 January 2005, the On 1 July 2005, the tasks of elo are carried out by the ELO Department (with its registered office in Poprad) of the Department of Excise Duties of the Customs Directorate of the Czech Customs (ELO SR).
In accordance with the provisions of Article 3(1) of Regulation (EC) No 126 In particular, the central liaison office is responsible for the exchange of data contained in the electronic REGISTER of SEED, - the Early Warning System Excise ('EWSE'), - requests for verification of the movement of excise goods sent to or received from other Member States by the 'Early Warning System Excise' ('MVS').
The content, scope and functionality of SEED, EWSE and MVS are regulated in Articles 22, 23 and 24 of Regulation No 2073/2004.
SEED - a system for the exchange of information on tax entities trading in excise goods.
The system consists of national registers of excise payers and enables tax authorities in the Territory of the European Union to ascertain whether products subject to excise duty are traded by a person entitled to do so.
Each national register shall be made available to the competent authorities of the other Member States only for the purposes of excise duties.
The central liaison office of each Member State shall ensure that persons involved in the movement of excise goods within the territory of the European Union can obtain confirmation of the information stored in that database.
In accordance with Section 41 of Act No. 98/2004 Z. z., with Section 39 of Act No. 104/2004 Z. z., with Section 46 of Act No. 105/2004 Z. z., s § 40 of Act No. 106/2004 Z. z. z. and with § 39 of Act No. 107/2004 Z. z. z. ELO SR maintains an electronic database containing a register of operators of tax warehouses, authorized recipients and tax warehouses - database SEED.
The customs authorities in the SR contribute to the SEED database by registering the tax warehouse, the tax warehouse operator or the authorized consignee in the SysNed application software, which is automatically linked to ELO SR.
For example, if a new tax warehouse operator, authorized recipient, or tax warehouse is registered in the SysNed database, the related data is automatically transferred to the SEED database.
The SAO SR found that the exchange of SEED databases between the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic and the Customs Administration of the Czech Republic took place in the audited period, usually once a month, exceptionally multiple times a month.
The SR Customs received 22 SEED files and sent 25 SEED files.
Data to the SEED database in the Czech Republic are transferred from the national register, in which all persons authorised to dispose of products subject to excise duty and issued authorisations for handling these products are registered.
Individual customs offices in the Czech Republic do not have access to the international SEED database.
Requests from customs authorities to provide information from the SEED database of other Member States are obtained only through ELO ČR.
EWSE - an early warning system aimed at controlling the transport of excise goods through which the transport of risky consignments is announced.
The transport of certain products subject to excise duty in quantities exceeding the limits laid down by the European Commission regulation and, on the other hand, transport which is assessed as a risk by the tax authorities is considered to be a risky consignment.
The exchange of information is carried out in two forms:
- information - sent when the limits are exceeded,
- warning message - sent if the transport of goods is assessed as risky.
When assessing the risk level of a consignment, ELO SR uses the SEED database to send the warning message, on the basis of which it checks the data contained in the accompanying document.
In the event that the SEED database does not match the data in the accompanying document (for example, the registration number of the consignee or the registered office of the consignee does not match), ELO SR draws up a warning message to be sent to the ELO office of the Member State of the recipient of the goods.
The ELO shall, when drawing up the reports, be governed by the regulations of the Tax and Customs Commission CED 317 and CED 457, which determine, inter alia, the type and quantity of goods in the relevant units of measure for the preparation of information and warning reports.
In the audited period ELO SR sent ELO CR one warning message.
In the Czech Republic, information about started deliveries of products in quantities exceeding the specified limits is generated automatically when entering data from the accompanying document into the database when approving transport.
If the tax administrator in the Czech Republic evaluates the consignment as a risk on the basis of its own analysis, it will process the so-called a warning message sent by ELO CR to the member state concerned.
In 2005 ELO ČR sent two warning messages to ELO SR.
MVS - the system of control of the movement of goods - allows, through requests from the MVS, to control the individual transport of products subject to excise duty as well as to check the specified route of transport between the operators indicated in the accompanying document.
The exchange of information shall take place on the basis of a request in which the ELO of the sending country specifies its requirements.
The system shall be used in particular in cases where the consignor takes over the certified copy No 3 of the accompanying document and requires, for example, the use of a copy of the accompanying document. refund of excise duty and in cases where the particulars on the accompanying document cannot be verified in the international SEED database.
In the audited period ELO SR, ELO ČR sent 33 requests to the MVS.
ELO ČR sent ELO SR 25 requests to the MVS.
The customs authorities in the Czech Republic most often checked the data given in the accompanying documents, in particular the quantity of products received or dispatched or whether the consignor of the products specified in the accompanying document is entitled to dispose of products subject to excise duty, if this fact could not be verified in the international SEED database.
The received REQUESTS for THE EMV were forwarded in both countries to the customs authorities locally responsible for the consignor or consignor of excise products.
The customs authorities checked the requested data and notified the result of the investigation through ELO to the other Member State.
6. Summary
The cooperation of the SAO-CR and the SAO SR made it possible to compare the basic legislation governing excise duties in both states, the procedure of the customs authorities of the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic in the initiation and termination of the transport of products under the conditional exemption procedure between the two states, the registration of such transports and the comparison of information between customs authorities in the framework of international cooperation.
6.1 By comparing the legislation governing excise duties in the Czech Republic and the Czech Republic, differences were found:
(a) in the procedure of tax entities and tax authorities when initiating the transport of products under the suspensive exemption scheme.
The transport of products under the conditional exemption regime can be started by a tax entity in the Czech Republic only with the agreement of the tax administrator, who will allow the start of transport, provided that the transported products have been provided with a tax security amount of the tax attributable to them.
The commencement of the transport of products under the suspensive exemption scheme in the SR shall not be subject to the authorisation of the tax authorities.
During the period audited, the tax entity was obliged to notify the tax authorities of the start of the transport of alcohol and tobacco products.
The transport of mineral oils, beer and wine could have started without informing the tax administrator of this fact.
In 2006, amendments to all excise laws were progressively adopted in the Czech Republic, according to which the consignor of goods under the conditional exemption procedure is obliged to send a copy of copy No 1 of the accompanying document electronically or by fax to the customs office which is locally competent to the consignor before the start of transport;
(b) within the time limits for dispatch of copy No 3 of the accompanying document.
The recipient in the Czech Republic is obliged to send copy No. 3 and 4 of the accompanying document to the tax administrator for verification no later than the next working day after the end of the transport.
Certified copy No. 3 is obliged to send to the consignor no later than the next working day after its receipt from the tax administrator.
The consignee in the SR is obliged to send to the consignor of the products copy No. 3 certified by the tax administrator and the recipient of the products no later than 15. the day of the month following the month in which he received the goods.
6.2. The customs authorities in the Czech Republic keep electronic records of the transport of products under the suspensive exemption procedure.
The content and method of keeping this register is not regulated by law in the Czech Republic or in the Czech Republic.
The customs authorities in both countries shall enter in the register all the data from the accompanying documents on the basis of which the transport is carried out.
There is currently no single electronic system for monitoring the transport of goods under the conditional exemption procedure between Member States of the European Union to allow excise managers in each Member State to obtain real-time information on the transport of goods.
Pursuant to Decision 1152/2003/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 16 December 2003 on the protection of the european communities's products,[ The information shall be asked to be asked by the Authorities of the It is envisaged that the electronic system for monitoring the movement of products subject to excise duty should be established.
On the basis of the contract for cooperation in control activities, the Czech party handed over to the Slovak side a database of transport of products under the conditional exemption procedure initiated in slovakia and completed in the Czech Republic.
The database contained 5 876 items relating to transported mineral oils, alcohol and tobacco products.
The Slovak party handed over to the Czech party a database of transport of products under the conditional exemption procedure initiated in the Czech Republic and terminated in slovakia.
The database contained 3 319 items relating to transported mineral oils, alcohol and tobacco products.
The Czech side compared the data on the transports mentioned in the records of commenced transports in the Czech Republic with the registration of transports completed in the Slovak Republic.
The Slovak side compared data on the transport of goods under the conditional exemption procedure initiated in Slovakia and terminated in the Czech Republic.
The comparison of data was hampered by the fact that the quantity of goods transported was not uniformly reported in the databases.
In cases where it was not possible to clearly assign data on individual transports in both records, an inspection of the accompanying documents was carried out and breaches of the suspensive exemption regime and cases of tax evasion were not detected.
On the basis of the findings of parallel controls, it can be concluded that Member States can obtain valuable information from the transport records to improve the management of excise duties.
The establishment of an electronic system for the transport and control of excise goods within the meaning of Decision No 1152/2003/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council will allow for the electronic transmission of the accompanying document and more effective control of movements under the conditional exemption procedure within the territory of the European Union.
Communiqué
This report was prepared in Czech, English and Slovak.
The report was signed by the President of the Najvyššie Control Office of the Slovak Republic and the President of the HighEst Audit Office, the Czech Republic.
Value added tax administration in the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany
Report on the results of the follow-up
Introductory word
Taxation is generally a key source of public revenue.
It goes without saying that the Supreme Audit Institutions (SAI) should focus their attention on this area.
Examples include value added tax fraud (hereinafter also 'VAT').
In their case, a loss of EUR 100 billion is estimated annually in the European Union (hereinafter referred to as the "EU").
As early as 2005, participants in the VI had become more interested in the use of the the euroai congress in Bonn agreed on the need for very close cooperation.
As part of this cooperation, SAIs can exchange control procedures, find the best solution, etc.
VAT is a very suitable area for control cooperation, as it is the only tax harmonised within the EU.
The Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the SAO) and the Federal Court of Auditors (Bundesrenungshof, hereinafter referred to as "BRH") carried out the first parallel control action in the field of VAT in 2006.
The relevant report was published in 2008.
As VAT fraud is not limited to a single country, but is widespread throughout the EU, close cooperation between the SAIs is needed to ensure a comprehensive evaluation of the steps taken to tackle this problem.
The two SAIs therefore decided to further develop cooperation in this area and carried out a subsequent parallel check.
1. Introduction
Check number: (CZ) 09/11 (D) VIII 2 - 2009 - 0892
Subject of inspection: (CZ) Value added tax administration (D) Bilateral audit with THE SAO (follow-up)
Objective of the inspection:
(CZ) The aim of the control action was to examine the procedure of the financial authorities in the management of VAT, in particular to verify the procedure for dealing with selected cases of commercial transactions between the Czech Republic and the Federal Republic of Germany (hereinafter referred to as "Germany"), and to examine the procedures of the tax administrations of both countries in the framework of international cooperation.
(D) The control action was designed to evaluate the measures taken by the tax administration to implement the recommendations issued by the SAO and BRH.
The intention was also to cover other VAT-related areas.
The resulting control findings were intended to be compared with the proven best practice (if any).
The period audited was the years 2006 to 2008, in the case of material contexts, the period preceding and following, until the completion of the inspection.
2. Summary of results and evaluation of parallel control actions
The follow-up control of VAT management in the Czech Republic and Germany was carried out on the basis of an agreement between the two SAIs.
Suspicious cases of intra-Community transactions were detected during previous parallel checks.
Some of them required further vetting.
On the basis of the control findings, the two SAIs made recommendations on VAT management.
The follow-up control action carried out was used to evaluate the measures taken in response to these recommendations and to examine selected suspicious cases.
The check was further targeted, e.g. by the commission. selected cases of high-risk intra-Community transactions, mutual assistance in debt collection and the implementation of VAT controls on large tax entities.
When checking vat management in selected areas in both countries, the inspectors reached the following control findings:
1. Recommendations from the previous inspection
• Recommendation 1: The conditions for registering payers should be harmonised within the EU
In previous parallel checks, comparisons of VAT registration systems in both countries found differences.
As different forms of registration cause problems, the two SAIs recommended harmonising the conditions for registration of payers within the EU.
This recommendation has been presented at EU level.
The proposal for an amendment to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 on administrative cooperation in the field of value added tax and repealing Regulation (EEC) No 218/92 (hereinafter referred to as "Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003") called for the extension of existing databases within the EU, including a database of VAT payers' vat identification numbers.
It also amended common standards for the registration and deregistration of tax payers.
THE SAI expected EU Member States to agree on appropriate standards to support their decision to exclude unreliable traders from the VAT system as quickly as possible.
However, the latest version of that document, agreed by the EU Member States under ECOFIN, no longer contains the issue.
Both SAIs regret that the idea of common minimum standards has been abandoned.
However, they continue to regard this intention as a relevant tool for prevention in the fight against VAT fraud.
• Recommendation 2: Monthly reporting of summary reports
In the framework of international cooperation, the previous control action recommended that all EU countries introduce a monthly deadline for reporting, allowing for a more timely examination of intra-community transaction values.
Council Directive 2008/117/EC amending Directive 2006/112/EC on the common system of value added tax to combat intra-Community tax evasion reduces the period for which summary reports on intra-EU transactions are reported to one month.
In the Czech Republic, this measure was implemented through the Value Added Tax Act with effect from 1 January 2007. It was implemented from 1 January 2010, and was implemented in Germany from 1 January 2010. They are very, on 17 July 2010.
In Germany, the obligation to submit monthly summaries was not introduced within the deadline in accordance with the applicable EU rules, whereas in the Czech Republic it did.
• Recommendation 3: Comparison of vat declaration data and summary reports in Germany in order to achieve greater reliability of data in VIES and consideration of the interconnection of the two VAT return systems and for summary reports
The German tax administration accepted the BRH's recommendations and set up a working group to explore possible solutions.
Work is still ongoing and BRH will closely monitor further developments.
• Recommendation 4: Sharing of successful criteria, components and approaches of the risk management system at EU level Based on the results of the previous control action, the two SAIs agreed that an effective risk management system cannot be developed by only one Member State.
Successful criteria, components and approaches of the risk management system need to be exchanged and implemented in each EU Member State.
If this is not the case, the perpetrators of fraudulent activity will choose the Member State with the weakest risk management system.
The inspection found that our two Member States use different risk management systems that have their advantages and weaknesses.
In this area, the SAO has carried out a eurocanet review, which allows for the exchange of information within the EU, while brh has focused on German participation in the so-called 'eurocalnet'. risk management platform.
2. Follow-up of selected intra-Community transactions cases
During the previous control action, commercial transactions were jointly examined for which there were doubts about their implementation or irregularities in the reporting of commercial transactions in tax returns or summary reports to tax payers from both countries.
Both SAIs selected nine cases for follow-up, which included intra-community movement of goods between the Czech Republic and Germany.
The checks carried out by the tax authorities of the countries concerned were not concluded at the date of completion of our previous joint control action.
The subsequent control action verified that most of the tax proceedings in relation to the selected cases of commercial transactions between the czech republic and Germany were closed and that adequate measures were taken by the tax administration of the Czech Republic or Germany (e.g. additional VAT assessment or avoidance of input tax refunds).
3. Control of selected cases of risky intra-Community transactions
High-risk cases of intra-Community transactions carried out by EU payers included in EUROCANET have been selected for inspection.
EUROCANET is a tool for detecting risky tax payers within the EU.
Member States' participation in this system is voluntary.
The Czech Republic is an active participant in EUROCANET, while Germany has passive status.
It is not satisfactory for an active participant in the system if some Member States refuse to participate.
In view of the fact that the German tax administration did not engage in the exchange of data in EUROCANET, it was not possible to obtain any information as to which suppliers with the German VAT ID were assessed as risky.
As part of the control action, the SAO identified both cases of normal commercial transactions and cases suspected of involvement in carousel transactions or VAT fraud.
Tax authorities have limited possibilities for controlling risky transactions, in particular with regard to so-called 'risk transactions'. missing traders, while the mere physical examination of documents can hardly prove to the tax entity any fraudulent conduct.
A similar situation arises for tax authorities when imports and exports to third countries are linked to intra-Community carousel transactions.
In such cases, it would be appropriate to ensure greater cooperation between customs and financial authorities in order to identify goods and irregularities in the transport documentation, as well as to monitor their physical movement within the EU towards the end consumer.
Germany, like some other countries, is hesitant to participate actively in EUROCANET due to the lack of a sufficient legal basis.
Other tools are used in Germany to detect risky tax payers, which have so far proven themselves to the German tax authorities.
In this area, experience needs to be communicated and exchanged between EU Member States.
The Council of the EU has reached political agreement on the proposal for a regulation amending Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
Its main innovation is to create a EUROFISC network.
The experience gained so far in using EUROCANET should be the basis for the creation of this new vat fraud network.
4. Mutual assistance in the recovery of claims
In the field of international debt recovery assistance, all EU Member States are governed by the same European legislation.
Therefore, the method of handling applications for international assistance in the recovery of claims in the Czech Republic and Germany is the same.
The SAO and BRH compared the statistics submitted by the two Member States to the European Commission for the years 2006-2008.
The data contained in these statistics did not match.
Both SAIs consider it useful to renegotiate statistics at EU level in order to find a way to avoid persistent mismatches.
Without this, statistics will not be reliable and comparable.
In addition, the SAI agrees that reliable statistics should contain more information on VAT.
It would probably be useful for the Commission to analyse, on the basis of more detailed statistics, an analysis to help Member States strengthen the effectiveness of the fight against VAT fraud.
In the opinion of both SAIs, this means assistance for Member States with low recovery rates, so that they can increase the recovery rate to at least the EU average.
If a Member State so wishes, the Commission should actively participate in this process.
5. Control of large tax entities
The SAI analysed the legal situation regarding VAT control for large tax entities (hereinafter referred to as 'VDS') in both countries.
In addition, in the form of a questionnaire, they gathered information from tax authorities on areas which the SAI considered essential to the management of this issue.
It is clear from the responses received that the situation in both countries is developing differently.
The Czech Republic has a system for regulating the selection of risk-prone cases, which is based on a large volume of relevant data (e.g. information from tax checks carried out, data from balance sheets and profit and loss accounts, etc.).
This ensures effective management and analysis of VAT control in general.
In 2012, a dedicated tax office for the administration of the VDS is planned.
There is no similar system in Germany yet, which makes it difficult to manage and analyse VAT control in general.
Germany has so far been more focused on selecting the individual cases in question, in particular on the basis of the VAT return data and the recapitulative statement.
The analysis of this data is based on various risk management components that will be strengthened.
3. Course of control action
3.1 Control action in the Czech Republic
The inspection was carried out between May 2009 and February 2010 by Division II. - the revenue department of the state budget and the territorial departments IX. Plzen, X. České Budějovice, XIII. Brno and XV. Ostrava.
The audited persons were: The Ministry of Finance of the Czech Republic (hereinafter referred to as the "Czech Ministry of Finance") and 25 financial authorities (hereinafter referred to as "FÚ"): FÚ Brno II, FÚ Brno III, FÚ Brno IV, FÚ in Břeclav, FÚ in Domažlice, FÚ in Hodonín, FÚ in Hradec Králové, FÚ in Cheb, FÚ in Jablonec nad Nisou, FÚ in Karlovy Vary, FÚ in Kralupy nad Vltavou, FÚ v Kraslice , FÚ Ostrava I, FÚ Ostrava III, FÚ in Písek, FÚ in Pilsen, FÚ for Prague 1, FÚ for Prague 4, FÚ for Prague 8, FÚ in Rakovník, FÚ in Sokolov, FÚ in Tábor, FÚ in Vysoké Mýto, FÚ in Zlín and FÚ in Žamberk.

Later, in December 2008, the leaders of both AIDs signed a cooperation agreement in the implementation of parallel controls.
At the Bonn meeting in June 2009, the control teams informed each other of the initial results achieved during the preparation of the inspection, discussed possible audit approaches and agreed on a further procedure.
The second meeting took place in Prague on 2 and 2 December 2005. - 4. They shall forthwith inform the Council of their information on the
