The report on the results of parallel control actions was prepared during a working meeting in June 2010.
4. Control of VAT management in selected areas
4.1 Evaluation of recommendations from the previous inspection
4.1.1 Evaluation of recommendations in the Czech Republic
Recommendation 1
The conditions for registering payers should be harmonised within the EU
On the basis of the results of the previous control action, the SAO recommended the modification of the conditions for registration for VAT and the introduction of a new rule for the deregistration of registration in the Czech Republic.
The revised conditions should make it possible to reduce more effectively the risk of possible tax evasion in the collection of VAT.
In this context, it was found that, in some cases, the tax authorities did not use the right to cancel the VAT registration of payers who did not fulfil the obligations under Act No. 235/2004 Coll., on Value Added Tax ('the VAT Act').
The Czech Ministry of Finance has not yet proposed an amendment to the provision of the obligation of tax authorities to cancel the VAT registration for payers in the event of repeated non-filing of a VAT return.
According to the VAT Act, the tax administrator may revoke the registration of the tax payer "ex offo" in cases where: a) the payer has not carried out without notice of the reason to the tax authorities for twelve consecutive months of performance, b) the payer does not fulfil his obligations under this Act, c) the payer ceases to be a taxable person.
In the previous control action, it was found that the legislation in force allowed the FA for Prague 1 to cancel the VAT registration as of 31 December 2004. 1. unsettled payers who have not been obliged to declare and pay tax during the current calendar year.
The FÚ did not often cancel the VAT registration for Prague 1, as the relevant provision provided for an insufficient deadline for the cancellation of registration.
This problem was eliminated by an amendment to the VAT Act with effect from 1 January 2008. They shall forthwith inform the Commission of their view that they shall
The tax administrator is entitled to cancel the registration of an unsaved tax payer if the tax payer has not delivered any goods or services subject to vat in the previous calendar year or exempt goods or services entitled to deduction of VAT.
Recommendation 2
Monthly reporting of summary reports
In the framework of international cooperation, the previous control action recommended that all EU countries introduce a monthly deadline for reporting.
The Council Directive reduces the periods for which summary reports on intra-EU performance are reported to one month. This measure was implemented in the Czech Republic through the VAT Act with effect from 1 January 2004. They shall forthwith inform the Commission of their
There is also a new obligation to submit summary reports in electronic form.
The recapitulative statement must be submitted to the payer even if the services for which the place of performance is determined in accordance with § 9 para. 1 of the VAT Act, granted to another Member State by a taxable person in another Member State and if he is obliged to award and pay the tax to the recipient from those services.
This obligation is based on Council Directive 2008/8/EC amending Directive 2006/112/EC as regards the place of supply of the service.
Recommendation 3
Comparison of vat declaration data and summary reports in order to achieve greater reliability of data in VIES This recommendation concerned the German tax administration.
The Czech administration compares data on intra-community transactions reported in VAT tax returns and summary reports of Czech payers automatically in the ADIS system.
Recommendation 4
Sharing successful criteria, components and approaches of the risk management system at EU level
Proper VAT collection is one of the prerequisites for the proper functioning of the EU internal market.
The fight against VAT fraud is therefore an area of priority interest and has received considerable attention in recent years.
The importance of this struggle is demonstrated, inter alia, by the fact that the the conclusions of a study published by the European Commission in October 2009 in which an external evaluator attempted to establish the difference between the eligible and actual VAT amounts collected in the 25 EU Member States ('EU-25') during the period 2000-2006.
On the basis of the analysis of the available data, the author of the analysis concluded that the estimated amount of loss on uncollected VAT for this period is BETWEEN EUR 90 and EUR 113 billion, with an average of 12 % of the eligible VAT not collected annually in the EU-25.
For the Czech Republic, the VAT loss for 2006 was estimated at 18%.
In the framework of international cooperation, it was stated in the previous control action that an effective risk management system could not be developed by only one Member State.
The successful criteria, components and approaches of this system must be shared and implemented in each EU Member State.
As regards the risk management system, the SAO carried out a eurocanet review for the exchange of information in the EU.
Cases of risky intra-Community transactions carried out by EU tax payers included in EUROCANET have been selected for inspection (see Chapter 4.3).
The objectives of improving administrative cooperation and increasing the effectiveness of combating VAT fraud should also be achieved by establishing a EUROFISC network to improve the cooperation of responsible authorities in a form that enables fraud to be detected already in their germs.
This network should later also become an important source of information in the assessment of risks to intra-Community transactions.
The ECOFIN Council approved the creation of the EUROFISC network on 7 December 2005. It shall, at the same time, set out the basic principles to be followed by the network.
The EUROFISC is already a functioning system for the rapid and selective exchange of eurocanet information developed by the Belgian tax administration in cooperation with other Member States and with the support of the European Commission and OLAF.
The aim of this system is to detect risky business transactions and entities involved in organised VAT fraud.
4.1.2 Evaluation of recommendations in Germany
The evaluation of the recommendations from the first report produced the following findings:
Recommendation 1
The conditions for registering payers should be harmonised within the EU
The German tax administration has established a well-functioning system for the registration of tax payers, which is based on a detailed questionnaire.
The Federal Ministry of Finance alerted the Commission to this system in October 2007.
The system is improved on an ongoing basis.
At present, the questionnaire data are processed electronically and will then be used for the survey as part of risk management during registration.
The Commission presented a proposal for an amendment to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, which included common standards for the registration and deregistration of tax payers.
Member States have requested further clarification and detailed development of this issue.
BRH has asked the Federal Ministry of Finance to secure the level of standards already achieved in this area in Germany.
Recommendation 2
Monthly reporting of summary reports
On 8 June 2005, the Council adopted Decision The law on the transposition of EU directives into national law was adopted on 15 April 2010.
This Act contains provisions concerning the monthly submission of summary reports on intra-Community deliveries.
Those provisions took effect on 1 January 2005. They are very, on 17 July 2010.
Recommendation 3
Comparison of vat declaration data and recapitulative reports in order to achieve greater reliability of data in VIES and consideration of the interconnection of the two VAT return systems and for summary reports
A joint working group composed of workers from the Länder and the Federal Ministry of Finance has been set up.
The group developed a strategy for automatically comparing data from VAT returns and summary reports.
This strategy is still being discussed in the Länder.
Furthermore, the Working Party looked at a tool designed to optimise the control procedure for transactions in the internal market.
Recommendation 4
The sharing of successful criteria, components and approaches of the risk management system at EU level The exchange of relevant information takes place at EU level.
Germany is a participant in this exchange in the context of the so-called risk management platform.
The European Commission supported the idea of this platform and, on the basis of a written consultation of 18 December 2005, the European Commission has adopted a proposal for a directive on the application of the european union's strategy for the 2 The establishment of the Risk Management Platform was added to the Fiscalis Action Plan 2006-2007.
Platform members are further divided into sub-groups dealing with individual topics such as: • risk management tools, • influencing negotiations, • evaluation, • updating the risk management guide.
At the beginning of 2010, reports on the results of the activities of these sub-groups were published.
4.1.3 Evaluation
Registration
The issue of conditions for VAT registration and the cancellation of VAT in different countries has been addressed at EU level.
The proposal for an amendment to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 included the extension of existing databases within the EU, including a database of VAT payer tax identification numbers.
It also regulated common minimum standards for the registration and deregistration of tax payers.
The issue of registration and registration has so far been left to the national legislation of the EU Member States.
Member States have requested further clarification and detailed development of this issue.
THE BRH has asked the Federal Ministry of Finance to ensure that the level of standards already achieved in Germany does not fall.
On 8 June 2005, the Council adopted Decision On 16 June 2010, the ECOFIN Council reached political consensus on that proposal for a regulation.
The intention of common minimum standards has been abandoned.
Member States must implement national procedures and are only obliged to inform the Administrative Cooperation Committee of these procedures.
Both SAIs regret that the Commission has failed to convince Member States of the need for common standards for the registration and deregistration of payers, since both SAIs consider this measure to be an important element of prevention in the fight against VAT fraud.
They would therefore welcome the Commission's further efforts in this direction.
Monthly reporting of summary reports
In the framework of international cooperation, the previous control action recommended that all EU countries introduce a monthly deadline for the submission of summaries, allowing for a more timely examination of intra-Community transaction values.
Council Directive 2008/117/EC amending Directive 2006/112/EC on the common system of value added tax to combat intra-Community tax evasion reduces the period for which summary reports on intra-EU transactions are reported to one month.
In the Czech Republic, this measure was implemented through the VAT Act with effect from 1 January 2004. It was published on 1 January 2010. They are very, on 17 July 2010.
Germany has not introduced an obligation to submit summary reports monthly according to the specified calendar, while the Czech Republic has (in accordance with EU directives).
Comparison of vat declaration data and recapitulative reports in Germany in order to achieve greater reliability of data in VIES and consideration of the interconnection of the two VAT return systems and for summary reports
The German tax administration accepted the BRH's recommendations and set up a working group to find possible solutions.
Work is still ongoing and BRH will closely monitor further developments.
Sharing successful criteria, components and approaches of the risk management system at EU level
Germany and the Czech Republic apply different approaches to the risk management system for the purpose of identifying risk-prone traders.
The SAO has carried out a eurocanet control for the exchange of information in the EU (see chap. 4.3).
In this area, BRH focused on German participation in the so-called "German" movement. risk management platform.
4.2 Follow-up of selected intra-Community transaction cases
In the previous control action, the execution of commercial transactions, for which there were doubts as to their implementation or irregularities in the way in which payers from both countries reported these business transactions in their VAT returns or summary reports, was examined.
Both control institutions selected for follow-up nine cases involving intra-Community movement of goods between the Czech Republic and Germany, the control of which was not completed during the previous joint control action.
1)
Czech payer acquired in 1. goods worth EUR 22 686 from the German payer in the quarter of 2005.
This acquisition of goods was not accepted by the Czech payer in his VAT return because the German payer was not assigned a VAT ID during that period, but only a tax number intended for national transactions in Germany.
On the basis of international administrative cooperation under Council Regulation (EC) No 798/2003, the Czech tax administrator received information that, under the German VAT Act, the payer who supplies goods to other Member States does not have to be assigned a VAT ID in order for intra-Community supplies of goods to be exempt from VAT.
A subsequent inspection by the SAO found that, on the basis of a check carried out by the Czech tax administrator, the Czech payer submitted an additional VAT return in which he admitted the acquisition of goods at that value and at the same time claimed the same amount in that tax return.
2)
In the 4th century, the Czech payer had a total of 100,000 people who to purchase goods worth EUR 12 561 from the German payer in the quarter of 2004.
The acquisition of these goods was denied by the Czech payer and did not mention in his VAT return.
The German tax authorities refused cooperation at the request of Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, since the turnover of transactions did not exceed EUR 15 000.
Since the Czech tax administrator did not obtain the evidence, he terminated the inspection without finding it and the tax liability remained at the original level.
The SAO subsequently found that the Czech tax administrator had received from Germany two spontaneous information pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, which showed that the German payer had invoiced the goods to Slovakia.
The Czech payer purchased the goods from the Slovak payer and stated this acquisition in the proper VAT return for the month of October 2004.
3)
In the 4th century, the Czech payer had a total of 100,000 people who in the quarter of 2004, a passenger car worth EUR 48 500 was purchased from the German payer.
The acquisition of the goods in question was not accepted by the Czech tax payer.
This payer has not submitted VAT returns since August 2004, so the tax administrator assessed VAT of CZK 0 for that quarter.
On the basis of the information obtained in the context of the international exchange of information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 from Germany, the tax authorities invited the payer to submit an additional VAT return in March 2007, which the payer did not submit.
A subsequent inspection revealed that the tax administrator carried out further tax proceedings in 2007, which showed that the czech payer had sold the passenger car in question to a car bazaar in the Czech Republic.
The Czech tax administrator issued a payment notice for the December 2004 tax year, which subsequently assessed VAT for the acquisition of goods from another Member State and its subsequent sale of CZK 295,379.
By order of the regional court, the Czech payer was dissolved with liquidation and a liquidator was appointed.
In the absence of enforcement of the taxable debtor's depreciable assets, this arrears appear to be impenetrable.
4)
The Czech payer was to carry out the delivery of new means of transport (passenger cars) to Germany during the 4th century. 2004 and 1 December 2004. total amount of EUR 198 167 in the first quarter of 2005.
The response to a request for information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 showed that an unsealed tax-criminal procedure is pending against a German entity in Germany.
In the subsequent inspection, BRH obtained information that, after the conclusion of the tax proceedings in Germany, it was established that the German tax payer had been involved in fraudulent activities.
Intra-Community acquisitions of goods were taxed at a value of EUR 182 424 (year 2004) and EUR 369 690 (year 2005).
The SAO subsequently found that the Czech payer was involved in carousel shops with new means of transport.
On the basis of the information of the German tax administration concerning the screening of supplies of goods, a VAT check was initiated with the Czech tax entity for the tax year April, May and June 2005.
On the basis of the control findings and information obtained in the framework of the international exchange of information, the tax administrator additionally assessed VAT for the period May 2005 of CZK 703,031 and czk 726,551 for the period June 2005.
5)
In February 2005, Czech payer A was to purchase a machine with a total value of EUR 58,000 from the German payer.
This German payer was to deliver in the 3rd quarter of 2009. In 2004, the Czech payer B was a machine worth EUR 88 027, but payer B denied this acquisition of the goods.
Subsequent inspection of the SAO found that payer B acquired the machine from a German company, which had an organizational unit established in the Czech Republic.
Czech payer A did not report the acquisition of goods from the German payer in his VAT return.
A reply from the German tax administrator to a request for information pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 showed that the German payer did not make an intra-Community delivery of the machine worth EUR 58 000, but the supply of goods within the Czech Republic.
The BRH subsequently found that, after the tax check, the intra-Community supply of the machine was reclassified for the supply of the machine in the country and the VAT exemption was abolished.
6)
In the 3rd year, the German tax payer had a tax refund. the Czech payer of goods worth EUR 11 600.
The goods were purchased and subsequently sold in Germany in 2005.
The SAO subsequently found that the Czech tax administrator had assessed the submitted additional VAT return, where the acquisition of goods from another EU Member State was unduly indicated, including the acquisition of goods at that value.
The BRH found that, after receiving a reply to a request for information pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003, the German tax authorities corrected the German payer's VAT return and subsequently assessed VAT of EUR 1 600.
The further movement of goods in Germany and the application of VAT in Germany are subject to tax control.
The recapitulative statement of the German payer has not yet been corrected because corrections to recapitulative reports in Germany can only be carried out by the payer who submitted the recapitulative statement.
7)
The Czech tax administrator received a request from the German tax administration for information pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003 whether the Czech tax payer had purchased a passenger car worth EUR 47,400 from the German payer in February 2005.
After the tax procedure for the tax year was carried out, the Czech tax administrator charged a tax liability of CZK 0 to the Czech taxpayer and told the German tax administrator that he could not confirm the purchase of the car by the Czech payer.
A subsequent inspection of the SAO found that the registration of the Czech VAT payer was cancelled in 2007 for non-compliance and the Czech tax administrator sent the documents to the Police of the Czech Republic.
By subsequent checks, BRH found that the German payer had changed his registered office and the new locally competent tax administrator had abolished the VAT exemption for the supply of the car in question to the Czech payer on the basis of the check carried out.
The German tax payer has not yet corrected the data in the recapitulative statement and has lodged an appeal against the tax administrator's decision.
8)
According to data from the VIES system, the German payer delivered to the Czech tax payer in the period from 3 January 2004 to 31 December 2006. quarter 2004 to 1 January 2004. total of EUR 33 205 in the first quarter of 2005.
A subsequent inspection by the SAO found that the Czech tax administrator tried to ascertain the causes of the differences arising from the Czech tax payer in the acquisition of goods in the period from 3 January 2004 to 31 December 2004. quarter 2004 to 1 January 2004 quarter 2005.
The Czech tax payer repeatedly submitted an additional VAT return for the first year in auat.... quarter 2005.
The Czech tax administrator did not clarify the difference in the value of the acquired goods in the amount of CZK 134,273 for the period 3. quarter 2004 to 1 January 2004. In the 2005 quarter of 2005, as according to the czech tax administrator it was not possible to accurately capture commercial transactions for each quarter, and therefore the tax administrator accepted the additional tax returns submitted.
9)
In the 3rd year of the year, the German tax payer delivered a tax refund. czech payer of EUR 46 854 in the first quarter of 2004.
Over the same period, the Czech payer admitted intra-Community acquisition of goods worth only EUR 14 856.
The Czech tax administrator verified the amount of supplies made in the framework of the international exchange of information pursuant to Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
The reply to the request for information received from Germany was accompanied by 3 invoices with a total stated value of delivery of goods of EUR 31 998, which is the value corresponding to the difference between the acquisition declared by the Czech payer in the VAT return and the data given in the VIES system.
Subsequent inspection of the SAO found that the Czech payer submitted an additional VAT return for the tax year of July 2004 to January 2007 after many urgencies by the tax administrator.
In that tax return, the tax payer also exercised his right to deduct VAT, thus leaving the tax liability unchanged for that tax year.
The follow-up check verified that for selected cases of commercial transactions between payers from the Czech Republic and Germany, most tax proceedings were completed and that tax authorities in both the Czech Republic and Germany took adequate measures (i.e. additional VAT or avoided input tax refunds).
4.3 Control of selected cases of risky intra-Community transactions
4.3.1 Results of the inspection in the Czech Republic
EUROCANET can be an important source of information for the detection of risk entities within the Member State in which the goods were acquired.
In the Czech Republic, the signal information obtained from EUROCANET was compared by the relevant local tax authorities with the data on the acquirers.
From 1 January 2005, the In the quarter of 2008, the Czech Republic sends data to EUROCANET on risky transactions and on tax entities acting as suppliers.
As part of international cooperation, nine Czech tax entities included in EUROCANET were selected for control.
These entities acted either as suppliers or as purchasers of goods.
Relevant data from tax authorities from other Member States were captured in EUROCANET.
Since the German tax authorities did not participate in the exchange of data in EUROCANET, it was not possible to obtain any information to help ascertain whether suppliers with a German VAT ID had been assessed by the German tax administration as risky entities.
The control action revealed cases of normal commercial transactions as well as cases suspected of involvement in carousel transactions or VAT fraud.
Where applicable, tax authorities have used the exchange of information under Council Regulation (EC) No 1798/2003.
Such as:
• Tax authorities have not detected any suspected involvement in risky transactions when verifying signal information.
The tax authorities shall continuously monitor such tax entities for their inclusion in EUROCANET.
• During the verification of risk transactions, the tax authorities did not demonstrate in the accounts submitted a derogation from the rules applicable to the calculation of the tax base and VAT, even though they found irregularities in the transport and storage of goods or revealed business relationships with suspicious or non-contact companies from other Member States.
• Verification of business transactions was complicated as some tax payers did not cooperate with tax authorities and could not be contacted.
The local tax authorities mostly examined the risky tax entities and risk transactions referred to in the EUROCANET signal information.
Tax authorities in the screening of risky transactions, in particular in connection with the screening of the so-called "tax authorities". missing traders have limited options and only from physical checking of documents makes it difficult to prove to the tax entity fraudulent conduct.
Stricter VAT registration requirements and more flexible registration cancellations would help reduce missing trader fraud.
In the case of tax entities involved in carousel fraud and other fraudulent activities, VAT is registered for the purpose of reporting fictitious deliveries of goods within the EU or for the issue of formally correct tax documents to payers who unduly draw input VAT deductions.
In cases where the involvement of tax entities in carousel transactions and other fraud is suspected and goods are imported and exported from third countries, it would be appropriate to ensure greater mutual cooperation between customs and financial authorities.
Closer cooperation between these authorities would assist in identifying goods and discrepancies in the transport documentation and in monitoring the physical movement of goods within the EU towards the end consumer.
The participation of EU Member States in EUROCANET is voluntary.
The fact that three large Member States (Germany, Italy and the United Kingdom) did not participate in eurocanet activities was assessed by the European Parliament at the end of 2008 as a weakness of the system, which should be eliminated by the establishment of a mandatory EUROFISC network.
4.3.2. Results of the inspection in Germany
The BRH analysed the information available from the Federal Central Tax Office containing data from EUROCANET.
These figures were a criterion for the selection of six files of German tax payers for inspection.
Germany, like some other countries, refused to actively participate in EUROCANET.
Germany thus has passive status, which means that it does not send data to Brussels, but is merely the recipient of eurocanet data.
The justification for this position is contained in the following statement:.in the government's view, it is not legally permissible for state (public) institutions to provide data to EUROCANET.
There is currently no legal basis to violate the applicable rules on the concealment of tax information.
In addition, the Government has no reliable information on how such data are used by other Member States under EUROCANET.' 17 Since October 2007, the Federal Central Tax Office has analysed eurocanet data and has been conducting it to the tax authorities of the Länder in accordance with the agreed procedure.
German tax authorities receive control information on the direct trade relations of payers (registered with specific tax authorities) with traders from other Member States who have been included in eurocanet.
However, the German tax authorities do not receive any information as to whether such a trader from another Member State has any risky business relationships with traders from other Member States who also maintain business relations with the German trader in question.
4.3.3 Evaluation
The Czech Republic is an active participant in EUROCANET, while Germany has passive status.
It is not satisfactory for an active participant if some Member States refuse to participate actively.
As a result, the control in the area had to be carried out in different ways.
However, the results did not reveal major differences with regard to the detection of VAT fraud cases, as EUROCANET is not the only systemic risk management tool.
The tax administrations of both countries have a number of other tools to detect fraudulent transactions, but it is necessary to establish a comprehensive risk management system within the EU.
The Council of the EU has reached political agreement on a proposal for a regulation whose main contribution lies in the establishment of the EUROFISC network.
The envisaged network to combat VAT fraud should also include the experience gained in the use of EUROCANET data.
Member States should therefore communicate their experience at European level.
On the other hand, cases brought to the courts at national and European level show that a debate between the Member States and the Commission on the conditions of tax exemptions for intra-Community transactions appears to be necessary.
4.4 Mutual assistance in debt recovery
4.4.1 International debt recovery assistance in the Czech Republic
In particular, the following directives are a fundamental adjustment of international cooperation in the recovery of certain financial claims within the EU:
• Council Directive 76/308/EEC on mutual assistance in the recovery of claims arising from operations which are part of the financing system of the European Agricultural Guidance and Guarantee Fund, as well as agricultural levies and customs duties;
• Council Directive 2001/44/EC amending Directive 76/308/EEC on mutual assistance in the recovery of claims arising from operations which are part of the system of financing of the European Agricultural Guidance and Guarantee Fund, agricultural levies and duties, value added tax and certain excise duties;
• Commission Directive 2002/94/EC implementing certain provisions of Council Directive No 76/308/EEC on mutual assistance in the recovery of claims arising from certain levies, duties, taxes and other measures.
In the Czech Republic, Council Directive No. 76/308/EEC was implemented by Act No. 252/2000 Coll., on international assistance in the recovery of certain financial claims.
Following the adoption of Council Directive 2001/44/EC, it was necessary to implement this Directive into the Czech legal system while amending the said Law No. 252/2000 Coll.
In this context, a new Act No. 191/2004 Coll., on international assistance in the recovery of certain financial claims was adopted.
Commission Regulation (EC) No 1179/2008 of 28 June 2008 laying down the general rules for the application of Council Regulation (EC) No 1250/1999 on the application of The European Union's financial claims to the European Union [2] is a new provision for the system of arrangements for international cooperation in the recovery of certain financial claims within the EU. 11. 2008.
New models of applications are set out in the Annex to the Regulation, which shall apply from 1 January 2005. 1. 2009, the obligation of electronic communication and the obligation of the requesting authority to confirm the conformity of the documents sent with the original document are newly established.
Main principles for the provision of international cooperation in the recovery of claims:
1. reciprocity;
2. assistance shall always be granted only on the basis of an application containing the prescribed formalities;
3. the assistance shall not apply to financial claims which are of a criminal legal penalty in the requested State;
4. the provision of international assistance in the recovery of claims shall be followed by the national law of the State which has been requested;
5. foreign claims shall not take precedence over recovery;
6. assistance shall be provided only in the recovery of uncontested claims;
7. the principle of exhaustion (the requesting State has, without success, used all applicable possibilities to recover a claim due to its legal system).
Act No. 191/2004 Coll. defines the three forms by which assistance takes place, namely the provision of information, the service of documents and the actual recovery of claims.
Procedure for sending claims recovery requests to other EU Member States
The local tax authority electronically sends a request for information, a request for service or a request for recovery of claims together with the relevant documents to the Czech Ministry of Finance through the Financial Directorates.
The Czech Ministry of Finance will arrange for the application to be translated into the appropriate language, scanned including annexes and sent to the competent tax authority of the designated state via the CCN/CSI network.
Two basic requirements apply to recovery: the claim must exceed EUR 1 500 and must not be older than 5 years.
If those requirements are not met, the requested office may refuse enforcement.
Procedure for receiving claims recovery requests from other EU Member States
Upon receipt of a request from another Member State, the Czech Ministry of Finance must confirm receipt of the request as soon as possible within seven days.
If the Czech Ministry of Finance decides not to comply with the application, it shall inform the requesting authority of the reasons for the rejection of the application and indicate the specific provisions of the Directive to which it relies.
This communication shall be sent no later than three months after the date of confirmation of receipt of the request.
Upon receipt of the request, the Czech Ministry of Finance will verify that the application has all the requirements according to the law and should immediately submit the request through the financial directorate to the local tax authority for processing.
If the request for a levy is accepted, the tax administrator shall, inter alia, decide to grant the aid. finds out the debtor's assets, e.g. the acquisition of land register statements, identification of accounts in banks, verification of registration of vehicles at the transport inspectorate, etc.
After six months from the date on which the receipt of the request was confirmed, the Czech Ministry of Finance should inform the requesting authority of the outcome of the investigation, which was carried out in order to obtain the requested information.
In the case of non-contact tax entities where the claim cannot be recovered, the requesting authority should also be informed of this fact.
Any amount recovered by the tax administrator shall be transferred to the requesting authority in CZK within one month of the date on which the claim was recovered.
It is not excluded that the Czech tax administrator enforcing foreign claims should allow the deduction with its payment or payment in instalments, if the consent of the State which requested enforcement agrees.
During the period of recovery, the debtor is prescribed interest or periodic penalty payments according to Act No. 337/1992 Coll., on the administration of taxes and fees.
This interest or penalty payment belongs to the State which requested recovery.
In the case of received requests for recovery, the Czech Ministry of Finance did not forward requests to locally competent tax authorities for processing on time, especially in 2006 and 2007.
A similar situation was identified in the framework of international assistance in the recovery of claims also in the case of applications received from tax authorities from the Czech Republic.
The control action revealed that the Czech Ministry of Finance did not comply with Act No. 191/2004 Coll., because it did not inform the competent authority of the Member State of the progress made in recovery within six months of the date on which the receipt of the request was confirmed.
This situation has been improving since 2008.
Statistics
The Czech Ministry of Finance, in accordance with the provisions of § 13 para. 4 of Act No. 191/2004 Coll. processes every year until 15. The commission shall, by 31 March, provide statistical data for the European Commission, indicating the number of requests for information, service or recovery, sent or received in the past year, indicating the amount of claims to which the applications relate.
The European Commission shall prepare a report on the state of recovery of claims to the Council of the EU and the European Parliament on the basis of supporting documents provided from all EU Member States.
The inspection found that the Czech Ministry of Finance underestimated the statistics due to an error in the recovery account in 2008 by 5,250,000. The amount of the taxable claim was incorrect (this was the shift of the decimal point after the receivables from Czech crowns to the value in euro).
This error was subsequently reflected in the European Commission's statistics.
Information on mutual assistance, including the amounts earned, is presented in the following table.
4.4.2 International debt recovery assistance in Germany
The legal authorisation for international administrative assistance in tax matters derives from the law of the European Communities, Council Directive 2008/55/EC of 26 June 2008 on the protection of the european communities in the approximation of the laws of the Member States relating to the application of the system of taxation and use of the Community institutions and bodies and on the free movement of such data [2] is to be incorporated into the Agreement. The commission regulation of 28 May 2008 on the recovery of claims and the Commission Regulation of 28 May 2008 on the recovery of claims and the commission regulation of 28 May 2008 on the application of Article 87(3) of the EC Treaty to state aid to 2008 (EC Implementing Directive).
In order to make the wording and clarity more accessible, the EC Directive on recovery of claims codifies Council Directive No 76/308/EEC of 15 June 1976 on the approximation of the law of the European Parliament and of the Council of 15 June 1976 on the approximation of the law, the council, the Commission, the Commission, the Council, the Council and the Commission. It is hereo that the provisions of which have already been substantially amended several times.
The provisions apply, inter alia, to the following: for the recovery of VAT, income tax and capital gains tax, including accessories.
The EC Law on recovery of claims was transposed into national German law by the Law (EC) on the collection of state taxes of 3 December 1988. They shall forthed 2003.
In Germany, the enforcement procedure is governed by the German Fiscal Code.
Article 117.2 of the Code stresses that tax authorities may provide international judicial and administrative assistance on the basis of international agreements and legal instruments of the European Communities, which are in force in national jurisdiction, and under the EC Law on Administrative Assistance.
Part Six of the German Fiscal Code (Articles 249-346) enshrines the statutory provisions governing enforcement.
The administrative tasks of the tax authorities are governed in particular by enforcement instructions and enforcement instructions.
The Federal Ministry of Finance reached an agreement with the representatives of the High Tax Offices of the Länder on the principles of administrative assistance in the assessment of taxes and transferred its own responsibility in this matter to the Federal Central Tax Office.
The general preconditions for the submission of claims for recovery are as follows:
• The legal requirements must be fulfilled (Sections 251 and 254 of the German Fiscal Code [AO]).
• All available domestic recovery resources have already been exhausted.
• Claims which are the subject of recovery requests must be final.
• No more than 5 years may have entered into until the date of the application or the date on which the claim becomes legal (i.e. it is no longer subject to appeal) until the date of submission of the applications.
• The total amount of the claim must be more than EUR 1 500.
Procedure for sending claims recovery requests to other EU Member States
German requests for recovery of outstanding tax liabilities are sent from the tax authorities' implementing services to the competent foreign office, for example, the Czech CUSTOMS, through the Intermediary Office and the Federal Central Tax Office.
The closer procedure is governed by the Methodological Guideline on International Administrative Assistance in Tax Matters (Recovery of Claims) of 19 December 2005. 1. As from 1 January 2004.25 The Working Party of the Federal Government and the Provincial Governments is currently reviewing this methodological guideline in order to adapt it to the Debt Recovery Directive.
The application, including annexes, shall be submitted electronically to the intermediary authority by the tax authority.
This authority shall check the correctness of the application in terms of content and form.
If the request is incorrect, it shall be returned to the relevant tax authority.
If it meets all the requirements, it is referred to the Federal Central Tax Office.
The Federal Central Tax Office will then provide the necessary communication with the relevant foreign office and also provide a translation of the request.
Procedure for receiving claims recovery requests from other EU Member States
Applications for recovery of claims received from other Member States shall be registered by the Federal Central Tax Office and shall send a confirmation of their receipt within 10 days.
In addition, the Federal Central Tax Office shall check whether the formal requirements have been met.
The Federal Central Tax Office shall submit these requests to the intermediary authority, which shall forward them to the competent tax authorities and monitor their processing.
The Federal Central Tax Office also sends preliminary or final reports.
Where the application is longer than 6 months, the intermediate authority shall invite the submission of a preliminary report to be submitted pursuant to Article 16 of Commission Directive No 2002/94/DG.
After carrying out an inspection of the formal and factual requirements of the application, the implementing services shall notify the recovery method.
All amounts recovered must be transferred to the bank account indicated in the application within one month of receipt.
Statistics

4.4.3 Check on debt collection, case studies
As part of international cooperation, 21 requests for international assistance in the recovery of claims between the Czech Republic and Germany were selected for inspection.
By examining the ten selected cases, among other things, the number of cases selected was Found:
1.
On 20 June 2005, the Council adopted Joint Action 10. 2006, the Czech Ministry of Finance received a request from Germany for recovery of a VAT claim for the years 2004 and 2005 totalling EUR 3 883, i.e. eur 3 883. 109 820 CZK, with the Czech tax entity.
The Czech Ministry of Finance did not send a request to the tax authorities for recovery until 26 April 2006. 2. 2008.
In order to secure the enforced claim, the Czech tax administrator established a lien on real estate owned by a Czech tax entity.
Since it was not possible to pay the entire recovery claim even by stopping the real estate, a payment schedule with instalments of at least CZK 2,000 per month was agreed with the Czech tax entity.
On 31 December 2005, the Council adopted Joint Action 8. 2009, information on the recovery status of the claim was sent to the German tax administration, on 25 April 2009. 8. 2009, this receivable was partially recovered in instalments of CZK 49,600.
This amount was sent to Germany and on 28 April 2005, the Commission sent to Germany for the purposes of the aid. On 8. 2009, another instalment of CZK 3,000 was sent to Germany.

4.4.4 Comparison and evaluation
In the field of international debt recovery assistance, all EU Member States are governed by the same European legislation.
Therefore, the method of handling applications for international assistance in the recovery of claims in the Czech Republic and Germany is the same.
The SAO and BRH compared the statistics submitted by the two Member States to the European Commission for the period 2006-2008.
The data contained in these statistics did not match.
In its 2006 report, the European Commission recommended that Member States pay close attention to keeping their statistics.
In its 2009 report, the Commission concluded that the incidence of mismatches in statistics decreased even though the number of applications had increased.
Both SAIs consider it important that statistics issues be renegotiated at EU level.
This discussion should focus on how to avoid persistent mismatches, otherwise the data reported by individual EU countries in the statistics will not be reliable and comparable.
In addition, the two SAIs agree that reliable statistics are intended to report the annual number of applications as well as the nature of the claims in question (i.e. whether the claims relate to VAT, income tax, etc.) as well as the amounts of claims recovered by each Member State.
Both SAIs consider it important for the Commission to provide more detailed analyses of the statistics submitted by The Member States, as this can help Member States assess their own effectiveness in the fight against VAT fraud.
The fact that the recovery rate can be calculated broken down into individual Member States is considered by the two SAIs to be useful in order for Member States with a lower recovery rate to intensify their efforts and to improve the recovery rate at least to the level of the EU average.
If a Member State so wishes, the Commission should actively participate in this process.
In particular, in 2006 and 2007, the Czech Ministry of Finance did not submit requests for recovery of claims in a timely manner to the local tax authorities.
A similar situation was identified for requests for international assistance received from tax authorities from the Czech Republic.
The audit action revealed that the Czech Ministry of Finance did not act in accordance with Act No. 191/2004 Coll., on international assistance in the recovery of claims, because it did not inform the local competent authority of the Member State of the progress made in recovery within six months from the date on which the receipt of the request was confirmed.
4.5 Control of large tax entities
4.5.1 Control of large tax entities in the Czech Republic
General information
The VAT audit of large tax entities is governed by the same rules as that of other tax entities.
The procedural procedure for the control of the VDS is based on Act No. 337/1992 Coll., on the administration of taxes and fees.
The Czech Ministry of Finance defined VDS as natural or legal persons who were established or established for business purposes and whose net turnover for the tax year specified in the personal income tax return amounted to EUR 2 billion. CZK or higher.
The classification of the tax entity among the VDS took place after the filing of the income tax return for the relevant tax year, for the first time in 2003.
The tax entity ceased to be referred to as VDS if, in three consecutive tax years since the end of the period in which it filed its tax return on the basis of which it was classified among the VDS, its net turnover for the tax year has fallen below that threshold.
The tax entity could not be excluded from the VDS register without carrying out a tax audit of at least one tax for one tax year.
All VDS were checked at least five years in the period by the end of 2009.
From 2010 on, a written assessment of the tax entity must be carried out at least every 2 years and tax risks must be eliminated and their negative impact on the correct determination and collection of the tax.
The control of the FE is focused on at least one type of tax; the tax administrator usually chooses several tax periods at once.
The VDS were controlled by the departments of specialised controls, which are set up for a total of 13 FA, or by the staff of the control departments of the locally competent FA.
The department of specialised controls shall carry out tax checks within the scope of the competence established by the Director of the Financial Directorate.
In addition to large tax entity audits, it also examines
• tax entities operating in unusual and specific business fields;
• entities for which tax audits are extremely difficult to carry out tax checks;
• entities with a branched territorial and organisational structure;
• entities suspected of large-scale tax evasion;
• entities linked in chains and networks suspected of widespread tax evasion and unauthorised lure of excessive deductions.
The number of tax checks carried out by the departments of specialised FA checks and the results of such checks are given in Table 3.
The Czech Ministry of Finance has proposed an amendment to Act No. 531/1990 Coll., on territorial financial authorities, which consists of the establishment of a specialised FÚ with national competence for selected tax entities (e.g. for legal entities established for business purposes, which have reached a turnover of more than EUR 2 billion. CZK).
4.5.2 Control of large tax entities in Germany
General information
VAT controls on large companies are governed by the same rules as tax controls in general, i.e. vat controls in the general market. the relevant provisions are enshrined in the following regulations: • German Fiscal Code (AO), • Fiscal Governance Act (FVG), • tax control regulations (BpO).
Other methodological documents are also in force.
German Fiscal Code
The statutory provisions on control are enshrined in Articles 193-203 of the German Fiscal Code in Section IV - Tax on-the-Spot. In particular, those articles lay down the rules on the admissibility of on-the-spot tax control (i.e. on the premises of the undertaking), their scope by subject matter, the rules on the allocation of responsibilities, the form and content of the control notice, the principles of control, the obligation of the tax body to cooperate and the preconditions for carrying out the final discussion and communication of the control report.
Tax checks on the spot are carried out by the responsible tax authorities (Article 195 of the Code).
Fiscal Administration Act Pursuant to Article 5.1(1) in relation to Article 5.1 of the 2007-2008 Fiscal Code, the Commission shall, in accordance with the procedure laid down in Article 5.1, 19 of the Act, participation in on-the-spot tax checks carried out by the tax authorities is mandatory for the Federal Central Tax Office.
The participating authorities shall agree on the spot the nature and extent of the Federal Central Tax Office's participation in tax controls.
In addition, the Federal Central Tax Office has the right to require that the specific undertakings it selects be subject to scrutiny at a time which it designates.
In this case, it may issue rules on the implementation and content of the inspection at the premises of such companies.
Rules on tax controls Under Article 108.7 of the German Constitution, the rules on tax controls (German acronym BpO 2000) have been approved by the Federal Council (Bundesrat, the upper chamber of the German Parliament, in which the governments of the Federal States are represented).
These administrative rules apply to on-the-spot checks carried out by the tax authorities of the Länder as well as by the Federal Tax Office.
Undertakings shall be classified according to size at regular intervals, in accordance with Article 3 of BpO 2000.
Large undertakings are subject to ex post control (Article 4.2 of the BpO).
According to Article 33.1 of The BpO 2000, each informed tax authority must keep a register of groups of companies as defined in BpO 2000.
Methodological guidelines
In addition to the above, the supplementary methodology for tax administration provides the following guidelines:
• Single manual for special VAT controls in Germany ;
• the USLO manual, which sets out the methodology for the use of intra-Community trade data conducted in VIES;
• zauber manual, which sets out the methodology for the use of the ZAUBER database;
• Work aids for various and special items.
The classification of tax entities is based on criteria such as turnover and net profit, with different limits depending on the type of business.
The data is published by the Federal Ministry of Finance.
They are evaluated every three years and fixed for the next three years.
The number of companies to control - not just large enterprises - must be determined at regular control intervals.
In general, checks on large enterprises are carried out on an ongoing basis.
Checks are usually announced including VAT checks.
This means that, in the course of the inspection, checks will be carried out in particular by income tax, excise duty and VAT - i.e. vat. control of all types of relevant taxes.
VAT checks can be carried out either by tax inspectors or by VAT inspectors.
Implementation varies and depends on the organizational arrangement of the Länder.
The number of tax periods covered by checks usually ranges between three and five years.
BpO 2000 foresee a control period of three years.
All taxes of the company are subject to the examination.
4.5.3 Control of large tax entities
Both SAIs decided not to examine individual cases of VDS checks carried out, but focused on management issues in order to gain an overview of how the tax administration manages the issue of VAT controls for VDS.
In the form of a questionnaire, they gathered information from tax authorities on areas they consider essential to the management of this issue.
• What statistical records and analyses relating to VAT control for VDS have at its disposal to manage tax administrations?
Especially:
• Are there any statistics or records of the extent to which a distinction is made between combating VAT fraud and, in general, VAT control?
Czech Republic: No, the ADIS system does not allow such resolution in the current data version.
Germany: The tax administration does not distinguish between the control proposed to combat VAT fraud and the general control of VAT.
• Are there any statistics or records of the timeliness of VAT controls (in relation to the time period of the transactions checked)?
Czech Republic: Records of the timeliness of enquiries with relevance for intra-community acquisition of goods for selected VAT payers are reported in the ADIS system.
In addition, the information recorded in ADIS also includes data of how long it took to query.
Germany: No, the uniform statistics at federal level for tax inspectors contain only information on the average time of the last check (information on the year).
This figure does not provide an overview of the selected control periods with respect to individual entrepreneurs.
VAT inspectors focus on the latest tax assessment period; also have the right to carry out VDS checks.
However, statistics produced at federal level for special VAT control services do not provide information on the classification of tax entities.
• Are there any statistics or records of the nature of additional tax revenues, broken down e.g. according to the following criteria:
i. a net increase in tax liability (e.g. in cases where the tax entity wrongly applied a reduced RATE of VAT instead of the standard tax rate);
ii. only a nominal increase in the tax liability (e.g. moving a fully qualified VAT case to another tax year);
iii. additional collection of tax revenue (payment of the additional tax due).
Czech Republic:
The Czech Tax Administration monitors the number of tax verifications carried out, the volumes of additional tax charged by type of tax, the number of tax entities audited and the number of tax periods audited.
Other tax practices (local investigations, proceedings) are followed in the same way.
The time data and amounts of additional taxes paid shall be recorded as a separate task.
General debt statistics broken down by type of tax are also kept, but not by the declared tax or tax determined by the tax administrator.
Germany: No, uniform statistics at federal level for tax inspectors and special VAT control services do not distinguish between those criteria.
Furthermore, these differences do not distinguish even the majority of the tax administrations visited.
• Are the areas of control recorded which generate high additional revenues?
Czech Republic: Yes, the tax administrator has the right to collect tax payers for verification on the basis of criteria that can be linked to selected indicators in special sections of the ADIS.
Germany: There are no regulations at the federal level.
It follows that uniform statistics at federal level for tax inspectors and special VAT control services do not provide such data.
However, there is one coordinated approach by the finance ministers of the Länder and the Federal Government.
In the ZAUBER database, tax inspectors or tax investigators from the Länder must write down the increased tax (VAT) liability they measure if they exceed a certain amount.
In this case, it must specify e.g. the nature of the tax increase assessed.
• What are the most common findings?
Czech Republic:
- The VDS exercise an unjustified right to deduct input tax for supplies and services:
• which have not been used to carry out any economic activity pursuant to § 72 para. 1 of the VAT Act;
• which were used for representation pursuant to § 75 para. 3 of the VAT Act;
• on the basis of tax documents which did not meet the requirements laid down in § 73 para. 1 of the VAT Act;
- VDS did not declare output VAT pursuant to § 21 para. 1 of the VAT Act.
Germany: It was noted that there were no regulations at federal level.
It follows that uniform statistics at federal level for tax inspectors and special VAT control services do not provide such data.
The findings concerning VAT are not separately registered by the Länder if they result from VDS tax controls.
However, in the ZAUBER database, where tax inspectors or tax investigators from the Länder must write down the increased tax (VAT) obligations assessed by them if they exceed a certain amount, the Federal Central Tax Office is able to analyse this information.
• Does the tax administration analyse the areas of control from which the high "yield" results and infer consequences for the management?
Czech Republic: Yes, for example, they are launching national audits on risky commodities or on the subject of economic activity.
Germany: There are no regulations at the federal level.
Uniform statistics at federal level for tax inspectors and special VAT control services do not provide data on audit areas resulting in high "revenues".
There are different views on the analysis process, as well as on case management in terms of materiality.
Some regional tax authorities provide special information, but their use is on the tax authorities' own account.
4.5.4 Comparison and evaluation
Differences in the replies of the two Member States show that the Czech Republic provides a system that collects a number of data from the tax checks carried out, as well as data from the financial statements - balance sheet and profit and loss accounts.
On the basis of a wide range of data, the Czech Republic is able to direct the selection of risk-prone cases.
The same is true of the analysis and management of VAT control in general.
In 2012, the Czech Republic plans to establish a specialised tax office for the administration of VDS.
In Germany, the tax administration does not collect this information.
It follows that it is more difficult to carry out those tasks in a similar way.
However, Germany's philosophy places greater emphasis on the selection of individual cases based on data from the tax returns submitted.
The risk management components will therefore be strengthened and improved.
On the basis of adequate reference notes, expert auditors must be able to measure the exact amount of VAT.
Both SAIs agree that Member States should be able to provide adequate financial management as well as an adequate risk management system.
This will help reduce vat gaps.
As a result, the vat collection revenue will increase and the level of risk detection among unreliable entrepreneurs will also be improved.
5. Conclusion
The cooperation of the two SAIs on parallel controls of VAT management met the objectives set by the SAO and BRH.
The two SAIs have better understood each other's systems in the following areas: • intra-community transactions, • VAT risk management, in particular as regards the selection of risk-prone transactions, • assistance in the recovery of VAT receivables and • VAT control for large tax entities.
Thanks to mutual cooperation, differences in strategies for detecting VAT fraud cases as well as differences in the above areas of VAT management in the Czech Republic and Germany have been revealed.
The control findings were compared and best practices were identified on the basis of them.
In addition, the two SAIs hope that the results achieved will provide an impetus for stakeholders to start a debate on approaches and strategies within Member States, including at European Commission level.
The extremely valuable experience and knowledge gained from the cooperation of the two SAIs can serve as an encouragement for the implementation of future control actions in the field of VAT management.
6. Communiqué
The report was prepared in Czech, English and German and signed by the President of the Supreme Audit Office of the Czech Republic and the President of the Federal Court of Auditors (Bundesrechnungshof) of the Federal Republic of Germany.
Editor's deadline: June 2010.
